\title{\textcolor{sectionblue}{\textbf{Selenium Python Developer Notes}}}
\author{}
\date{}

\maketitle

\section{Fundamentals of Automation \& Selenium}

\subsection{What is Automation Testing?}
Automation testing matlab apne software ya website ko \textbf{automatically test} karwana—matlab human ko baar baar manually check nahi karna padta. Ek script banate ho, woh khud sab test steps follow karti hai.

\subsubsection*{Why use karein?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Manual testing \mostimportant{boring ho jata hai}, time lagta hai.
  \item Repeat karne mein \crossmarkinline mistake ho sakti hai.
  \item \checkmarkinline Fast, consistent, accurate results chahiye toh \concept{automation best hai}.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Kab use karein?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab project bada ho ya bhut baar same cheez check karni ho—jaise regression, smoke test, etc.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Agar na karein toh?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Test karte karte bore ho jaoge, choti choti galtiyan ho sakti hain.
  \item Release cycle slow ho jayegi.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Manual vs Automated Testing}

\begin{description}[font=\color{sectionblue}\bfseries,leftmargin=!,labelwidth=5cm]

\item[Manual Testing:]
Insaan khud manually har ek step karta hai, report karta hai. Small projects, ya one-time testing mein useful.

\item[Automated Testing:]
Script sab kuch khud karti hai, repeat kar sakte ho jitni baar chaaho—jaise ek robot har baar same kaam automatically kare.
\end{description}

\subsection{SDLC, STLC, Automation Life Cycle}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{SDLC (Software Development Life Cycle):} Software kaise banta hai—plan, code, test, deploy, maintain.
  \item \textbf{STLC (Software Testing Life Cycle):} Sirf testing wali steps—plan, create tests, execute, bugs dhundo, fix karao.
  \item \textbf{Automation Life Cycle:} Kaunse test automate karne hain decide karo, tool select karo, script banao, test chalhao, maintain karo.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Automation Testing ka ROI (Return on Investment)}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Starting mein time lagta hai scripts banane mein, lekin baad mein \checkmarkinline \textbf{bahut time bacha sakte ho}.
  \item Jaldi release ho sakte ho.
  \item Manual galtiyan kam ho jati hain.
  \item Team ka kaam aasan ho jata hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Types of Testing: Smoke, Regression, Integration, etc.}

\begin{description}[font=\color{sectionblue}\bfseries,leftmargin=!,labelwidth=4cm]
  \item[Smoke Testing:] Aisa test jisse pata chale major feature kam se kam work kar raha hai ya nahi.
  \item[Regression Testing:] Code mein change ke baad kuch aur toota toh nahi check karna.
  \item[Integration Testing:] Alag alag modules milke kaam kar rahe hain ki nahi.
  \item[Aur bhi:] functional, load, UAT, sanity testing, etc.
\end{description}

\subsection{Selenium Overview}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Selenium Suite:} IDE, WebDriver, Grid (RC ab nahi chalta)
  \item \textbf{Selenium IDE:} Simple record \& playback tool hai, jaise macro, basic automation ke liye.
  \item \textbf{WebDriver:} Yeh main tool hai jo programming languages (Python, Java, etc.) se browser ko control karta hai.
  \item \textbf{Grid:} Multiple machines/browsers pe parallel testing ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Selenium WebDriver kaise kaam karta hai? (Architecture)}

Aapka Python script \(\to\) Selenium library \(\to\) Driver (jaise ChromeDriver) \(\to\) Browser control hota hai (jaise Chrome ya Firefox).

Har browser ka apna driver hota hai.

\subsection{Supported Browsers, Languages, Platforms}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Browsers:} Chrome, Firefox, Edge, Safari, Opera, etc.
  \item \textbf{Languages:} Python, Java, C\#, Ruby, JavaScript (Node.js)
  \item \textbf{Platforms:} Windows, Mac, Linux sab pe chalta hai.
\end{itemize}

\vspace{0.5cm}

\section{��️  Environment Setup}

\subsection{Python \& Tooling}

\paragraph{Python Install karna hai:}
Official python.org se download karo, install karo.

\paragraph{Virtual Environment (virtualenv):}
Har project alag environment mein rakho toh dependency issues nahi aate.

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Virtual Environment Creation Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
python -m venv venv
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\paragraph{Activate:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Activate Virtual Environment}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
# Windows:
.\venv\Scripts\activate

# Mac/Linux:
source venv/bin/activate
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\paragraph{IDE use karo:}
PyCharm ya VSCode (Python plugin ke saath)—isme code likhna, run karna easy ho jata hai.

\paragraph{Project structure:}
Aise files/folders banao:
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{src/} (source code)
  \item \texttt{tests/} (test scripts)
  \item \texttt{resources/} (data/files)
  \item \texttt{logs/} (output ya failures track karne ke liye)
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Selenium Install Karna}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Install Selenium}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
pip install selenium
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\paragraph{Browser driver (jaise ChromeDriver) chahiye:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Chrome: ChromeDriver
  \item Firefox: GeckoDriver
  \item Edge: EdgeDriver
\end{itemize}

Download karke PATH mein dal do, ya easy way:

\paragraph{webdriver\_manager:} Yeh Python package driver ko automatically download/use karta hai.

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={webdriver\_manager usage example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium import webdriver
from webdriver_manager.chrome import ChromeDriverManager

driver = webdriver.Chrome(ChromeDriverManager().install())
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\paragraph{Environment Variables \& PATH setup:}

Driver ka path system ke environment variable mein hona chahiye, taki Selenium use kar sake.

webdriver\_manager use karoge toh yeh step mostly skip ho jayega.

\vspace{0.5cm}

\textit{Aap mujhe next specific topic batao ya poochho, ya example code ki jarurat ho toh batao main aapke level pe explain kar dunga!}

\section{Selenium WebDriver Core (\textcolor{sectionblue}{Complete Explanation})}

\subsection{\textcolor{sectionblue}{1. Browser Control}}

\subsubsection*{1. Launching Browsers (Chrome, Firefox, Edge)}

\concept{Why Important?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Jab tak browser launch nahi hoga, tab tak koi bhi web testing impossible hai.
    \item Selenium ko browser control karna hota hai taaki woh apne scripts me jo automate karna hai woh kar sake.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When To Use?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Har baar test script run karte waqt browser ko launch karna hota hai.
    \item Different browsers pe cross-browser compatibility check karna ho.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Agar Na Use Kiya Toh?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Browser open nahi hoga, test kisi tarah se run nahi hoga.
    \item Manual testing ke bina automation impossible.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code (Chrome Example):}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Chrome Launch Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium import webdriver  # Selenium ke webdriver module ko import karte hain
from webdriver_manager.chrome import ChromeDriverManager  # Chrome driver manager import karte hain

driver = webdriver.Chrome(ChromeDriverManager().install())  # Chrome browser launch karte hain aur driver automatically set karte hain
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Line-by-line Explanation:}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{from selenium import webdriver}: \concept{Selenium ke webdriver module ko import kiya, yeh module browsers ko automate karne ke liye APIs deta hai.}
    \item \texttt{from webdriver\_manager.chrome import ChromeDriverManager}: \concept{Webdriver manager ek utility hai jo ChromeDriver ko automatically download aur update karta hai, taaki manually driver manage na karna pade.}
    \item \texttt{driver = webdriver.Chrome(ChromeDriverManager().install())}: \concept{Yeh line Chrome browser ko launch karti hai. \texttt{ChromeDriverManager().install()} se driver ka path milta hai jo browser ko control karta hai.}
\end{itemize}

\textit{Note: Firefox ya Edge ko launch karne ke liye bhi yehi concept hai, bas webdriver\_manager ke corresponding module use karoge.}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Firefox Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from webdriver_manager.firefox import GeckoDriverManager
driver = webdriver.Firefox(executable_path=GeckoDriverManager().install())
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsubsection*{2. Navigating to URLs}

\concept{Why Important?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Browser ko kisi specific website pe le jana hota hai jisko test karna hai.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When To Use?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Har test case ke starting me ya kisi bhi step me URL open karna pade to.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Agar Na Use Kiya Toh?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Test script kisi page pe nahi jayega, automation steps fail honge.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={URL Navigation}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
driver.get("https://www.google.com")  # Jo browser ab open hai usko google.com pe le jate hain
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} \concept{.get() method browser ke URL bar me link dalne ke barabar kaam karta hai. Jo URL diya hai, browser us page ko load kar leta hai.}

\subsubsection*{3. Browser Operations: Back, Forward, Refresh, Close, Quit}

\concept{Why Important?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Browser navigation control karna, test script ko automate browser ke button jaisa operate karwana.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When To Use?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Browser me peeche ya aage jana ho.
    \item Page ko refresh karna ho (reload karna ho).
    \item Test ke end me browser band karna ho, ya tab close karna ho.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Agar Na Use Kiya Toh?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Navigation nahi hoga, contaminations ho sakte hain.
    \item Browser khula rahega, resource waste hoga.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Codes with Explanations:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Browser Operations}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
driver.back()     # Browser ko ek page peeche le jana hai, jaisa back button dabate hain
driver.forward()  # Browser ko ek page aage le jana hai, jaisa forward button dabate hain
driver.refresh()  # Current page ko dubara load karna hai (reload)
driver.close()    # Jo active tab ya window hai use band karta hai
driver.quit()     # Pura browser aur jitne bhi tabs khule hain sabko band karta hai
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsubsection*{4. Incognito \& Headless Mode}

\concept{Why Important?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \textbf{Incognito Mode:} Testing cookies/cache/reset state pe impact karne ke liye blueprint hota hai.
    \item \textbf{Headless Mode:} Background me browser chalana bina GUI ke, useful for CI/CD pipeline jahan UI show karna zaruri nahi.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When To Use?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Jab clean session chahiye without cache/cookies.
    \item Jab automation servers pe run karna ho jaha GUI available nahi hota (headless).
\end{itemize}

\concept{Agar Na Use Kiya Toh?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Cookies/cached data interfere kar sakta hai tests me.
    \item Automation servers pe GUI na hone ke wajah se script fail ho sakta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Incognito Mode Example:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Incognito Mode}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver.chrome.options import Options

options = Options()                  # Browser options object create karte hain
options.add_argument("--incognito")  # Incognito mode enable karne ke liye argument dete hain

driver = webdriver.Chrome(options=options, executable_path=ChromeDriverManager().install())
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textit{Options() object banaya, usme incognito argument add kiya jo browser ko private mode me kholta hai.}

\textbf{Headless Mode Example:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Headless Mode}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
options = Options()
options.add_argument("--headless")  # Browser GUI bina khole background me run karega

driver = webdriver.Chrome(options=options, executable_path=ChromeDriverManager().install())
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textit{--headless flag se browser window visible nahi hoti, background me test run hota hai.}

\subsubsection*{5. Multiple Tabs/Windows pe Kaam Karna}

\concept{Why Important?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Kabhi browser me ek se zyada tabs ya windows open karne padte hain (social login pop-ups, ads, payment windows).
    \item Selenium ko pata hona chahiye kaunsa window/tab active karna hai taaki waha commands bheje.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When To Use?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Jab naye tabs/windows open hote hain during user flows.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Agar Na Use Kiya Toh?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Selenium commands galat window/tab pe chale jayenge, tests fail ho jayenge.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example with Explanation:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Multiple Tabs/Windows}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
driver.execute_script("window.open('https://www.youtube.com', '_blank')")  # Naya blank tab open kar ke usme YouTube URL load karo

windows = driver.window_handles      # Browser ke sab khule window/tab ke handles le aao (list me)
driver.switch_to.window(windows[1])  # Window handles list me se second tab pe switch ho jao, taki ab us tab par control mile
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textit{execute\_script se browser me JavaScript execute kar rahe hain — naya tab khola gaya. window\_handles me tabs ka list, switch\_to.window se focus change.}

\vspace{0.4cm}
\section*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{WebDriver APIs Advanced Concepts}}

\subsubsection*{1. WebDriver Object, Options, Capabilities}

\concept{Why Important?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item WebDriver object browser automation ka main interface hai.
    \item Options aur Capabilities set karne se hum browser behavior customize kar sakte hain (jaise SSL certificates accept karwana).
\end{itemize}

\concept{When To Use?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Jab browser ko specific mode me chalana ho ya kisi feature ko enable/disable karna ho.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Agar Na Use Kiya Toh?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Browser ka default behavior use hoga, kuch cases me automation fail ho sakti hai, jaise SSL errors.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Capabilities Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver.common.desired_capabilities import DesiredCapabilities
from selenium import webdriver

cap = DesiredCapabilities().CHROME.copy()  # Chrome capabilities copy karte hain
cap['acceptSslCerts'] = True               # SSL certificate errors ko accept karne ka flag set karte hain

driver = webdriver.Chrome(desired_capabilities=cap, executable_path=ChromeDriverManager().install())
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textit{DesiredCapabilities se browser ke advanced options set hote hain. acceptSslCerts se insecure SSL certificates ke warnings ko bypass kar sakte hain.}

\subsubsection*{2. JavaScript Execution with \texttt{execute\_script()}}

\concept{Why Important?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Standard WebDriver methods se kaam nahi hota, ya kisi element ko special handle karna ho (scroll, alerts, page ke variables, etc).
    \item JS execute karne ka option flexibility deta hai.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When To Use?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Scroll karna, hidden element dikhaana, alert box dikhana, JS ke variables ko access karna, custom framework ke ops.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Agar Na Use Kiya Toh?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Limited browser access hota hai, kuch advanced ops possible nahi hoti.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={JavaScript Execution}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
driver.execute_script("alert('Hello from Selenium!')")  # Browser me ek alert pop-up show karo
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textit{execute\_script() JS code ko direct browser me chalata hai. Yahan ek alert box open hota hai.}

\vspace{0.6cm}

\section*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Summary Table}}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.25}
\begin{tabular}{ |p{3.1cm}|p{3.8cm}|p{2.7cm}|p{4cm}| }
\hline
\textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Why Important} & \textbf{When To Use} & \textbf{Core Usage Example} \\
\hline
Browser Launch & Browser control ke liye & Har automation run me & \texttt{webdriver.Chrome()} \\
\hline
URL Navigation & Web page open karne ke liye & Test case start ya step me & \texttt{driver.get(url)} \\
\hline
Browser Nav Ops (Back/Forward) & User navigation replicate karne ke liye & Navigation test scenario & \texttt{driver.back()}, \texttt{driver.forward()} \\
\hline
Browser Close/Quit & Resource cleanup & Test end me & \texttt{driver.quit()} \\
\hline
\hline
Incognito Mode & Clean session for tests & Cache, cookies problems ke liye & \texttt{Options().add\_argument("\textbackslash-incognito")}
\\

\hline
Headless Mode & GUI bina test run & CI/CD pipelines, servers & \texttt{Options().add\_argument("--headless")} \\
\hline
Multiple Tabs Handling & Multi-tab automation & Naya tab/window open hone par & \texttt{driver.switch\_to.window()} \\
\hline
WebDriver Options/Capabilities & Browser behavior customize & Advanced scenarios & \texttt{DesiredCapabilities()} \\
\hline
JavaScript Execution & Advanced browser manipulation & Custom scroll, alerts, JS vars & \texttt{driver.execute\_script()} \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

% Code listings for Python
\lstdefinelanguage{CustomPython}{
  language=Python,
  basicstyle=\ttfamily\footnotesize,
  keywordstyle=\color{keywordblue}\bfseries,
  stringstyle=\color{stringred},
  commentstyle=\color{commentgreen}\itshape,
  morecomment=[l][\color{commentgreen}\itshape]{\#},
  breaklines=true,
  breakatwhitespace=true,
  backgroundcolor=\color{codebg},
  frame=single,
  framerule=0.5pt,
  rulecolor=\color{gray!30},
  numbers=left,
  numberstyle=\tiny\color{gray},
  numbersep=5pt,
  xleftmargin=10pt,
  showstringspaces=false,
  moredelim=[is][\color{funcorange}]{|f}{|},
  moredelim=[is][\color{varpurple}]{|v}{|}
}

\begin{document}

\section{Locators \& Element Identification in Selenium (Complete Guide)}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Why Locator Identification Important Hai?}}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Selenium ka main kaam hota hai browser ke elements (buttons, input boxes, links, etc.) ko find karke unpe actions karna.
  \item Agar elements ko sahi tarah locate nahi karoge, toh test fail ho jayega kyunki Selenium ko pata nahi chalega kis element pe kaam karna hai.
  \item Locator selection test ki speed, reliability aur maintainability ko directly affect karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{When Use Karein?}}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab bhi interaction karna ho page ke kisi element ke saath (click, type, read text).
  \item Har ek test step ke liye element locate karna zaroori hota hai.
  \item Dynamic web pages me locator strategy smart honi chahiye.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Agar Locator sahi na chuna ho (If Not Used Correctly)?}}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Tests break honge frequently.
  \item Element not found exceptions ayenge.
  \item Flaky tests bante hain, jisme kabhi pass kabhi fail ho.
  \item Maintenance bohut difficult ho jayega.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Basic Locators in Selenium}}

\subsubsection*{1. ID Locator}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Element ka HTML attribute \texttt{id} ka use karta hai. Har element ka id usually unique hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Fastest, sabse reliable locator.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab element ka id available aur static ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={ID Locator Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element = driver.find_element("id", "username")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Line Explanation:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{find\_element()} method use karte hain.
  \item \texttt{"id"} specify karta hai locator strategy ko.
  \item \texttt{"username"} woh unique id value hai jise match karna hai.
  \item Selenium is element ko find karke \texttt{element} variable mein store karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{2. Name Locator}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Element ka \texttt{name} attribute use karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item ID ke bad option, particularly form elements me common hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab id nahi ho aur name unique ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Name Locator Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element = driver.find_element("name", "password")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:}  
Same way jaise id ke liye, par yahan locator strategy \texttt{"name"} hai aur \texttt{"password"} attribute value.

\subsubsection*{3. Class Name Locator}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Element ka \texttt{class} attribute use karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Tab use karo jab class unique ya specific ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab id/name nahi ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Caution:}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Class name usually shared hota hai, toh first match milega.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Class Name Locator Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element = driver.find_element("class name", "btn-primary")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsubsection*{4. Tag Name Locator}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item HTML tag jaise \texttt{input}, \texttt{button}, \texttt{div} se locate karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab sirf tag basis par search karna ho, ya parent element ke andar multiple similar tags ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Complex scenarios me jab aur options nahi mil rahe.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Tag Name Locator Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element = driver.find_element("tag name", "button")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsubsection*{5. Link Text Locator}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{<a>} tags me jo visible link text hota hai, uske basis par element locate karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Simple aur readable locator links ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab link text fix ho aur woh accurately identifiable ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Link Text Locator Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element = driver.find_element("link text", "Click here")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsubsection*{6. Partial Link Text Locator}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Link text ka exact nahi, kuch part ka match karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab pura text yaad nahi ho ya change ho sakta ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Flexible partial match ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Partial Link Text Locator Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element = driver.find_element("partial link text", "Click")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsubsection*{7. CSS Selector}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item CSS selector syntax ka use karke elements locate kar sakte hain.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Powerful, flexible and fast.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab id/name/class nahi mile ya complex hierarchy chahiye.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Examples:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={CSS Selector Examples}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element1 = driver.find_element("css selector", "#email")           # id ke liye #
element2 = driver.find_element("css selector", ".input-field")      # class ke liye .
element3 = driver.find_element("css selector", "input[type='text'][name='email']")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{\#email}: id \texttt{email} wala element.
  \item \texttt{.input-field}: class \texttt{input-field} wala element.
  \item Complex selector jisme input tag ke andar \texttt{type='text'} aur \texttt{name='email'} dono condition apply hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{8. XPath}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item XML path syntax se element location karte hain.
  \item Sabse flexible locator hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Sab complex aur dynamic structure me useful.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab koi basic locator kaam na kare, ya nested element chahiye.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={XPath Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element = driver.find_element("xpath", "//button[@id='submitBtn']")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{//button}: page ke jitne bhi \texttt{button} tags hain.
  \item \texttt{[@id='submitBtn']}: jinka \texttt{id='submitBtn'} attribute hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Advanced Locators}}

\subsubsection*{1. Dynamic XPath: contains(), starts-with(), axes}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Element attribute dynamic ya change hota rahta hai, toh simple exact match fail ho jata hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab element ke id/class dynamic strings generate kar raha ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Examples:}

\textbf{contains():}  
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={contains() Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element = driver.find_element("xpath", "//*[contains(@id, 'user_')]")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textit{Iska matlab: Kisi bhi tag ka wo element jiska \texttt{id} me 'user\_' substring ho.}

\textbf{starts-with():}  
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={starts-with() Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element = driver.find_element("xpath", "//*[starts-with(@name, 'pass')]")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textit{Iska matlab: Jo elements ka \texttt{name} attribute 'pass' se start hota ho.}

\textbf{Axes (Sibling, Parent, Child):}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={XPath Axes Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element = driver.find_element("xpath", "//label[text()='Username']/following-sibling::input")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textit{Explanation: XPath me \texttt{label} jiska text 'Username' hai, uske just baad jo input sibling element ho usko select karna.}

\subsubsection*{2. Custom Attributes: data-\*, aria-\*}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Web accessibility aur testing ke liye custom attributes use karte hain jise identify karna easy hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Example:}

% Note: Original HTML section was empty (``````) so we omit it but keep everything else faithfully.

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Custom Attributes CSS Selector}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element = driver.find_element("css selector", "div[data-test='loginButton']")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsubsection*{3. SelectorHub Plugin}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Browser extension jo automatic XPath/CSS selector generate karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why Important?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Beginner-friendly tool locator banana aur test karna asaan ho jata hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When Use?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab complex locator chahiye ya time-save karna hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{4. Accessibility Locators (ARIA roles)}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{aria-*} attributes se elements ko locate kar sakte hain.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Example XPath:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={ARIA Accessibility Locator Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element = driver.find_element("xpath", "//*[@role='button' and @aria-label='Submit']")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab app me accessibility features implemented hain, inhe use karna reliable hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\vspace{0.5cm}

\section*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Summary Table}}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{|p{3.2cm}|p{4.2cm}|p{3.1cm}|p{4.5cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Locator Type} & \textbf{Use Case / When to Use} & \textbf{Why Important} & \textbf{Example} \\
\hline
ID & Unique id attribute & Sabse fast, reliable & \texttt{find\_element("id", "username")} \\
\hline
Name & Name attribute suitable mostly forms & Good fallback & \texttt{find\_element("name", "password")} \\
\hline
Class Name & Class attribute, often multiple matches & Use when unique class & \texttt{find\_element("class name", "btn-primary")} \\
\hline
Tag Name & Tag type locator & Simple element list & \texttt{find\_element("tag name", "button")} \\
\hline
Link Text & Exact link text & Link identification & \texttt{find\_element("link text", "Click here")} \\
\hline
Partial Link Text & Partial text match for link & Flexible link matching & \texttt{find\_element("partial link text", "Click")} \\
\hline
CSS Selector & CSS selectors hierarchy or attribute & Powerful \& faster & \texttt{find\_element("css selector", "\#email")} \\
\hline
XPath & Complex queries \& relationships & Most flexible locator & \texttt{find\_element("xpath", "//button[\@id='submitBtn']")} \\
\hline
Dynamic XPath & Dynamic attributes (contains, starts-with) & Handle dynamic UX & \texttt{/*[contains(@id, 'user\_')]} \\
\hline
Custom Attributes & data-, aria- attributes & Accessibility \& testing & \texttt{div[data-test='loginButton']} \\
\hline
Accessibility Locators & ARIA labels \& roles & Inclusive design, reliable & \texttt{/*[\@role='button' and \@aria-label='Submit']} \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\section{Web Element Interactions in Selenium Python — Complete Guide}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{What are Web Element Interactions?}}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab hum Selenium se browser me kisi element ko locate kar lete hain (jaise textbox, button, checkbox, dropdown etc.), tab hume un elements ke saath interact karna hota hai.
  \item Interaction matlab user ki tarah us element pe click karna, usme text type karna, kisi dropdown me option select karna, checkbox check/uncheck karna, ya us element se koi information lena.
  \item Selenium ka purpose hi hai browser elements ke saath automatic interaction karna, bina human ke manual clicks/inputs ke.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Why Use Web Element Interactions?}}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Manual testing me har ek interaction manually karna padta hai, ye bohot slow aur repetitive hota hai.
  \item Automation se ye sab interactions programmatically perform hote hain jo fast, accurate aur repeatable hote hain.
  \item Testing ke liye ye interactions required hain taaki app ka behavior verify kar sako user ke jaise.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{When Use Web Element Interactions?}}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab bhi test case ka koi step hota hai jisme input dena ho ya button dabana ho.
  \item Form filling, login, navigation, filtering, submitting, selecting, aur reading outputs sab ke liye use hota hai.
  \item Har functional flow automation me ye basic building blocks hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Agar Na Use Karein (If Not Used)?}}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Test scripts incomplete rahenge — koi input nahi hoga, buttons click nahi honge.
  \item Automation ka purpose hi khatam.
  \item Manual intervention ke bina test cases chalana mushkil ho jayega.
  \item Sabhi core UI actions automate karna possible nahi hoga.
\end{itemize}

\section{1. send\_keys(), click(), clear() Methods}

Ye teen sabse common methods hain Selenium me element ke saath interaction ke liye.

\subsubsection*{a) send\_keys()}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Input field (textbox, textarea) me text type karne ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item User input ko replicate karta hai automation ke through.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab form fill kar rahe ho, login kar rahe ho, koi search box me typing kar rahe ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Example Code + Explanation:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={send\_keys() Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium import webdriver
from selenium.webdriver.common.by import By
from webdriver_manager.chrome import ChromeDriverManager

# Browser open karna
driver = webdriver.Chrome(ChromeDriverManager().install())

# Website open karna jisme interact karenge
driver.get("https://example.com/login")

# Username input field locate karna (id='username' assume kar rahe hain)
username_input = driver.find_element(By.ID, "username")

# Us input box me "myusername" type karna
username_input.send_keys("myusername")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{driver.find\_element(By.ID, "username")}: Browser me element locate kar raha hai jiska id \texttt{username} hai.
  \item \texttt{.send\_keys("myusername")}: Us element me text “myusername” type kar diya.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{b) clear()}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Input field me already jo value/hai use clear (delete) karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Kabhi-kabhi fields pre-filled hote hain, toh purana text hata ke naya type karna hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={clear() Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
username_input.clear()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Ye line \texttt{username\_input} field se pehle wali value hata degi taaki nayi value sahi jaye.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{c) click()}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Button, checkbox, link, ya kisi bhi clickable element pe click karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item User clicks ko automate karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab form submit karna ho, button click karna ho, link open karna ho, checkbox select/unselect karna ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={click() Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
password_input = driver.find_element(By.ID, "password")
password_input.send_keys("mypassword")

login_button = driver.find_element(By.ID, "loginBtn")
login_button.click()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Pehle password field locate karke password type kiya.
  \item Phir login button locate karke uspe click kiya.
\end{itemize}

\section{2. Get Text / Get Attributes}

Kabhie element se uska visible text ya koi attribute chahiye hota hai.

\subsubsection*{a) Get Visible Text}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Element par jo dikh raha visible text hai usko lena.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Verify karne ke liye ki sahi message ya label dikh raha hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Form submission ke baad success message check karna ho.
  \item Page header, error messages, labels ko verify karna ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Get Visible Text Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
heading = driver.find_element(By.TAG_NAME, "h1")
print(heading.text)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{heading.text}: us element ke andar ka jo visible text hai, wo fetch karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{b) Get Attribute Value}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Element ke kisi attribute ki value lena, jaise href, value, title.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Link URL verify karna ho, placeholder text check karna ho, koi custom attribute validate karna ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Verification or assertion ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Get Attribute Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
link = driver.find_element(By.LINK_TEXT, "Click Here")
url = link.get_attribute("href")
print(url)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Yahaan \texttt{href} attribute ka value link ke liye liya gaya.
\end{itemize}

\section{3. Handling Checkboxes}

\subsubsection*{What?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Checkboxes select/unselect karna.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Forms me options select karna zaruri hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab forms fill kar rahe ho ya kisi filter option select karna ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code + Explanation:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Checkbox Handling Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
checkbox = driver.find_element(By.ID, "subscribe")

# Checkbox select hai ya nahi check karna
if not checkbox.is_selected():
    checkbox.click()  # Selected nahi hai toh click karke select karo

# Agar unselect karna ho
if checkbox.is_selected():
    checkbox.click()  # Selected hai toh click karke unselect karo
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{.is\_selected()} check karta hai ki checkbox selected hai ya nahi.
  \item \texttt{click()} se toggle hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\section{4. Handling Radio Buttons}

\subsubsection*{What?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Radio buttons me se ek choose karna.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item User ke choices capture karne ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab gender, payment method, ya koi exclusive option select karna ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Radio Button Handling Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
radio_male = driver.find_element(By.ID, "gender_male")

radio_male.click()               # Select karna
print(radio_male.is_selected()) # Check karna kya select hua hai
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Radio buttons me multi-select allowed nahi hota.
\end{itemize}

\section{5. Dropdowns via Select Class}

\subsubsection*{What?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item HTML dropdown element me option select karna.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item User ko list me se ek option dena hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Country select karo, product category choose karo, etc.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example + Explanation:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Dropdown Select Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver.support.ui import Select

# Dropdown element locate karo (id='country' assume kar rahe hain)
dropdown = Select(driver.find_element(By.ID, "country"))

# Option select karne ke 3 tarike
dropdown.select_by_visible_text("India")   # Jo text dikhta hai usse select karo
dropdown.select_by_value("IN")              # Value attribute ke basis par select karo
dropdown.select_by_index(5)                  # Index se (0-based) select karo
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{Select} class ko import karna hota hai.
  \item Alag-alag tarike se select kar sakte hain depending on use case.
\end{itemize}

\section{6. Working with Sliders, Date Pickers, Drag and Drop}

\subsubsection*{a) Sliders}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Slider control move karne ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Volume, brightness, price filter jaise sliders control karte hain.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Test case me slider ko adjust karna ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code + Explanation:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Slider Control Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver import ActionChains

slider = driver.find_element(By.ID, "volumeSlider")
action = ActionChains(driver)

# Slider ko 50 pixels right drag karo
action.click_and_hold(slider).move_by_offset(50, 0).release().perform()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{ActionChains} mouse/keyboard advanced actions ke liye hota hai.
  \item \texttt{.click\_and\_hold()}: mouse button down karke
  \item \texttt{.move\_by\_offset(50,0)}: 50 pixels right move karna
  \item \texttt{.release()}: button chhodna
  \item \texttt{.perform()}: action execute karwana
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{b) Date Pickers}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Date input field me date dalna.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Forms me date of birth, appointment date select karna hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab input field simple type ka ho — datepicker nahi complex pop-up.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Date Picker Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
date_field = driver.find_element(By.ID, "dob")
date_field.send_keys("2025-07-26")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Agar datepicker complex ho tab JavaScript execute karna pad sakta hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{c) Drag and Drop}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Ek element ko drag kar ke doosre element par drop karna.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item UI me reorder lists, file upload fields, ya custom drag-drop controls me.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Drag and Drop Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
source = driver.find_element(By.ID, "drag")
target = driver.find_element(By.ID, "drop")

action = ActionChains(driver)
action.drag_and_drop(source, target).perform()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{drag\_and\_drop()} ek simple method hai drag-drop ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\section{7. File Uploads \& Downloads Automation}

\subsubsection*{a) File Upload}

\textbf{What?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item File select karna (upload karna) browser me.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Form inputs me resume upload, profile photo etc.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab HTML input type=file ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={File Upload Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
upload = driver.find_element(By.ID, "file-upload")
upload.send_keys("C:\\Users\\User\\Desktop\\testfile.txt")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Yahan \texttt{.send\_keys()} ko file ka \textbf{absolute} path dena hota hai.
  \item Selenium native OS file dialogs ko handle nahi karta, isliye input element ki help se hi file upload hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{b) File Download Automation}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Selenium khud direct control nahi karta download pop-ups pe kyunki browser control bahar hota hai.
  \item Par browser preferences set karke downloads folder change kar sakte hain.
  \item Advance automation tools/plugins ke saath download automation hoti hai.
\end{itemize}

\section*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Summary Table (Quick Reference)}}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{|p{5.5cm}|p{7cm}|p{3.5cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Method/Approach} & \textbf{Use Case} \\
\hline
Text input & \texttt{send\_keys()} & Type text in input fields \\
\hline
Button/link click & \texttt{click()} & Click buttons, links \\
\hline
Clear input & \texttt{clear()} & Purana text remove karna \\
\hline
Get visible text & \texttt{.text} & Text retrieve karna \\
\hline
Get attribute & \texttt{.get\_attribute("attr")} & href, value, title, custom attrs \\
\hline
Checkbox select/unselect & \texttt{click()} + \texttt{.is\_selected()} & Checkbox control \\
\hline
Radio button select & \texttt{click()} + \texttt{.is\_selected()} & Radio buttons \\
\hline
Dropdown select & \texttt{Select} class + \texttt{select\_by\_*} methods & Select option from dropdown \\
\hline
Slider move & \texttt{ActionChains.move\_by\_offset()} & Slider drag \\
\hline
Drag \& Drop & \texttt{ActionChains.drag\_and\_drop()} & Drag element to target \\
\hline
File Upload & \texttt{.send\_keys(file\_path)} on file input & Upload file automation \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\begin{document}

\section{Handling Alerts, Frames, Windows}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Why important hai?}}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Web applications mein bahut baar JavaScript alerts, confirm boxes, ya prompt dialogs aate hain user interaction ke liye, jinke bina test automation ruk sakta hai.
  \item Websites mein frames or iframes hote hain jinke andar page ke nested content hota hai — bina unhe switch kiye, elements ko access nahi kar sakte automation se.
  \item Multiple browser tabs/windows hoti hain—automation script ko pata hona chahiye kaunsi window/tab pe kaam karna hai, warna errors aayenge.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{When to use?}}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab alert/dialog aaye usko accept ya dismiss karna ho (jaise confirm dialog).
  \item Jab iframe ke andar ke elements ko interact karna ho.
  \item Jab aapka test case multiple windows ya tabs ke beech switch karta ho (pop-ups, social login windows, payment gateways).
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Agar na karein toh?}}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Alert aane pe agar handle na karein toh script popup ke wajah se ruk jaata hai (Exception error).
  \item Frame ke andar ke elements ko bina switch kiye locate nahi kar paoge.
  \item Multiple windows ke beech switch na karoge toh galat window pe commands bhejoge, test fail ho sakta hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{JavaScript Alerts, Confirm, Prompt Popups}}

JavaScript alerts are simple popups with a message and OK button, confirm boxes have OK and Cancel, prompts ask for user input.

\textbf{Code example + explanation:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={JavaScript Alert Handling Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium import webdriver
from selenium.webdriver.common.by import By
from selenium.webdriver.support.ui import WebDriverWait
from selenium.webdriver.support import expected_conditions as EC
from webdriver_manager.chrome import ChromeDriverManager

driver = webdriver.Chrome(ChromeDriverManager().install())
driver.get("https://example.com/alert-demo")

# Assume button pe click karke alert open hota hai
alert_button = driver.find_element(By.ID, "alertButton")
alert_button.click()

# Switch to alert box:
alert = driver.switch_to.alert

# Alert ka text get karo
print(alert.text)  # Alert me kya likha hai woh dikhayega

# Alert accept karo (OK button press)
alert.accept()

# Agar confirm box ho toh reject karna ho (cancel), use karo:
# alert.dismiss()

# Agar prompt box hai jisme input dena hai:
# alert.send_keys("Hello Alert")
# alert.accept()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \verb|driver.switch_to.alert| se Selenium ko alert box ka control milta hai.
  \item \verb|alert.text| alert mein jo message hai wo fetch karta hai.
  \item \verb|alert.accept()| alert ke OK button ko press karta hai.
  \item \verb|alert.dismiss()| Cancel button click karta hai.
  \item Prompt box me input ke liye \verb|send_keys()| bhi use karte hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Handling Frames \& IFrames}}

Frames simply ek webpage ke andar embedded documents hote hain. Selenium ke liye, agar aap element frame ke andar ho, toh us frame pe switch karna zaroori hota hai.

\textbf{Why important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Agar frame me content hai aur frame switch nahi karoge, Selenium \texttt{NoSuchElementException} dega; elements nahi milenge.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When to use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab aapko frames/iframes wale webpage pe automate karna ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Basic methods to switch:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \verb|driver.switch_to.frame()| — frame me switch karna.
  \item \verb|driver.switch_to.default_content()| — parent/main page me wapas aana.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Frame Handling Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
driver.get("https://example.com/frame-demo")

# Frame ko locate karo (id/name ke through)
frame = driver.find_element(By.ID, "frame1")

# Frame switch karna
driver.switch_to.frame(frame)

# Ab frame ke andar elements access kar sakte hain
inner_element = driver.find_element(By.ID, "inside_frame")
print(inner_element.text)

# Frame se bahar (main page) switch karna
driver.switch_to.default_content()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \verb|switch_to.frame(frame)| se driver us specific frame ke andar ka context le leta hai.
  \item \verb|default_content()| se wapas main page pe aa jaate hain.
\end{itemize}

Frames ko index ya name se bhi switch kar sakte hain:

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Frame Switch by Index or Name}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
driver.switch_to.frame(0)              # pehla frame (index 0) me switch
driver.switch_to.frame("frameName")   # frame name se switch
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Switching Between Windows/Tabs}}

\textbf{Why important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab test me new tab/window open ho, toh default selenium driver usi original tab/window par rahta hai.
  \item Aapko script me explicitly nayi window/tab par switch karna hota hai.
  \item Nahi kare toh element nahi milega ya galat window pe commands dene lagenge.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When to use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Popups, social logins, payment gateways jaha window/tab switch hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Methods:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \verb|driver.window_handles| — list deta hai sab open windows/tabs ke handles.
  \item \verb|driver.current_window_handle| — current window handle.
  \item \verb|driver.switch_to.window(handle)| — switch karna specific window/tab pe.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Window/Tab Switching Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
driver.get("https://example.com")

# maan lo button click se new tab open hota hai
new_tab_button = driver.find_element(By.ID, "newTabBtn")
new_tab_button.click()

# Sab window handles le lo
windows = driver.window_handles
print(windows)  # e.g. ['CDwindow-1', 'CDwindow-2']

# Current window handle
current_window = driver.current_window_handle

# New tab/window pe switch karna (jo current se alag ho)
for window in windows:
    if window != current_window:
        driver.switch_to.window(window)
        break

# Ab new tab me jaa ke kaam karo
print(driver.title)

# Jab kaam ho jaye, wapas main tab par aana:
driver.switch_to.window(current_window)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Summary}}

\begin{tabular}{|p{5cm}|p{6cm}|p{5cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Method/Concept} & \textbf{Use Case / Why Important} \\
\hline
JavaScript alerts/confirm/prompt & \verb|driver.switch_to.alert| & Alert/dialog aane pe usko handle karna (accept/dismiss/input) \\
\hline
Frames/Iframes & \verb|driver.switch_to.frame()| & Frame ke andar element access ke liye frame switch karna \\
\hline
Frames se bahar aana & \verb|driver.switch_to.default_content()| & Frame se main page pe wapas jana \\
\hline
Multiple windows/tabs switching & \verb|driver.switch_to.window(handle)| & Nayi tab/window pe automate karne ke liye switch karna \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\begin{document}

\section{Advanced Actions \& Mouse Events}

Selenium mein basic click/send\_keys toh aa gaya, lekin real-world automation mein mouse hover, double click, right-click, keyboard shortcuts, ya page pe scroll bahut zaruri hai. In ke liye \concept{ActionChains} aur kuch built-in methods use hote hain.

\subsection*{Why Important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Mouse Hover (hover actions):} Menus, tooltips, dropdowns ya hidden items ko dikhane ke liye zaruri hai.
  \item \textbf{Double/right click:} Kuch features ya menus sirf double-click ya right-click pe open hote hain.
  \item \textbf{Keyboard actions:} Form automation, navigation, hotkey usage test karne ke liye.
  \item \textbf{Scroll:} Bahut saare web pages pe elements scroll ke baad hi visible hote hain—bina scroll kiye interact nahi kar sakte.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Agar na use karein toh:} Test wahan atak jaayega jahan page ya element visible nahi hai, ya action expected nahi ho raha.

\subsection*{ActionChains: Mouse Hover, Double Click, Right Click}

Selenium me advanced mouse actions ke liye \texttt{ActionChains} ka use hota hai, jis se aap mouse se jo bhi manually karte the, woh sab automate ho jata hai.

\textbf{Example Setup (Import):}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Imports for Advanced Actions}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium import webdriver
from selenium.webdriver.common.by import By
from selenium.webdriver.common.action_chains import ActionChains
from webdriver_manager.chrome import ChromeDriverManager
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{webdriver}: Main driver, browser control karta hai.
  \item \texttt{By}: Element ka locator strategy (id, name, etc.) ke liye.
  \item \texttt{ActionChains}: Advanced mouse/keyboard actions ke liye.
  \item \texttt{ChromeDriverManager}: Driver ka auto-setup.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{1. Mouse Hover (move\_to\_element)}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Mouse Hover Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
driver = webdriver.Chrome(ChromeDriverManager().install())
driver.get("https://example.com")

menu = driver.find_element(By.ID, "menu")           # Menu element locate kiya
actions = ActionChains(driver)                      # ActionChains ka object banaya
actions.move_to_element(menu).perform()             # Mouse pointer menu pe hover kiya
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{move\_to\_element(menu)}: Mouse ko "menu" ke upar le gaya.
  \item \texttt{perform()}: Jo bhi actions ab tak queue hue, woh run kiye.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{2. Double Click (double\_click)}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Double Click Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
el = driver.find_element(By.ID, "doubleClickBtn")   # Element locate kiya
actions.double_click(el).perform()                  # Uspe double-click kiya
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\texttt{double\_click(el)}: Us element pe tez dubble-click hua.

\subsubsection*{3. Right Click (context\_click)}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Right Click Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
el = driver.find_element(By.ID, "rightClickBtn")    # Element locate kiya
actions.context_click(el).perform()                 # Uspe right-click (context-click) kiya
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\texttt{context\_click(el)}: Us element pe right mouse button click kiya.

\subsection*{Keyboard Actions: Keys.TAB, Keys.ENTER}

Selenium me keyboard keys send karne ke liye \texttt{Keys} class hoti hai.

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Keyboard Actions Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver.common.keys import Keys

input_box = driver.find_element(By.ID, "inputBox")
input_box.send_keys("Hello Bro")
input_box.send_keys(Keys.TAB)         # Tab dabaya (next field pe jump)
input_box.send_keys(Keys.ENTER)       # Enter dabaya (jaise form submit)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{send\_keys(Keys.TAB)}: Tab key send karta hai—form navigation ke liye.
  \item \texttt{send\_keys(Keys.ENTER)}: Enter key send karta hai—button click ya form submit ke liye.
\end{itemize}

Agar aap bina element directly keyboard key bhejna chahte ho:

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Direct Keyboard Key Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
actions.send_keys(Keys.ENTER).perform()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

Direct browser ke focused element pe key send ho jaata hai.

\subsection*{Scroll to Element}

Agar element page pe niche ya upar chhupa hai, toh usko scroll karke view mein lana zaruri hai. Selenium do tareeke deta hai:

1. \textbf{ActionChains se scroll:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Scroll using ActionChains}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element = driver.find_element(By.ID, "myID")
actions.move_to_element(element).perform()   # Element ke paas scroll ho jayega
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\texttt{move\_to\_element(element)}: Mouse ko element tak le jaata hai, aur page ko us position pe scroll kar deta hai.

2. \textbf{JavaScript se scroll:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Scroll using JavaScript}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element = driver.find_element(By.ID, "myID")
driver.execute_script("arguments[0].scrollIntoView(true);", element)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\texttt{execute\_script("arguments[0].scrollIntoView(true);", element)}: Direct JavaScript chala ke element ko screen ke view mein le aata hai.

Useful jab ActionChains ka scroll work na kare, ya precise position chahiye.

\subsection*{Scrolling with JavaScript: Custom Scroll}

Agar aap page pe custom vertical/horizontal scroll karna chahte hai (e.g., end pe, top pe, pixel-wise):

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={JavaScript Custom Scroll Examples}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
# Scroll to bottom of page
driver.execute_script("window.scrollTo(0, document.body.scrollHeight);")

# Scroll to top of page
driver.execute_script("window.scrollTo(0, 0);")

# Scroll by 200 pixels vertically
driver.execute_script("window.scrollBy(0, 200);")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

JavaScript ke \texttt{window.scrollTo} aur \texttt{window.scrollBy} se aap page ko kisi bhi position pe scroll kara sakte ho.

\subsection*{Summary Table}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{|p{5cm}|p{6cm}|p{5cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Action} & \textbf{Method/Function} & \textbf{Kyun Zaruri Hai} \\
\hline
Mouse hover & \texttt{ActionChains.move\_to\_element().perform()} & Hidden menus, hover \\
\hline
Double click & \texttt{ActionChains.double\_click().perform()} & Special UI, open file \\
\hline
Right-click & \texttt{ActionChains.context\_click().perform()} & Context menu \\
\hline
Keyboard (TAB/ENTER/other keys) & \texttt{send\_keys(Keys.TAB/ENTER)} & Navigation \\
\hline
Keyboard (actions, no element focus) & \texttt{ActionChains.send\_keys(Keys.KEY).perform()} & Direct shortcut \\
\hline
Scroll to element & \texttt{move\_to\_element()} or \texttt{JS scrollIntoView()} & Element not visible \\
\hline
Custom Scrolling (JavaScript) & \texttt{driver.execute\_script("scroll...")} & Pixel-wise, full-page \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\section*{Waits \& Synchronization in Selenium}

\subsection*{Why Is Synchronization Important?}

Modern web apps slow ya dynamically load hote hai—kuch cheezein turant nahi dikhai deti, ya kuch actions background mein chal rahe hote hain.

Agar Selenium script ne element pe action kar diya aur element abhi page pe aya hi nahi, toh error aa jayegi.

Synchronization techniques ensure ki tumhaari script tab tak ruk jaye jab tak element ready na ho, taki test reliable rahe123.

\subsection*{Kab use karein?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab elements dynamically aa rahe ho.
  \item Jab web app slow hai ya network ke chaal pe depend karta hai.
  \item Jab apne test stable aur robust banane hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Agar use nahi karein toh?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Scripts unreliable, kabhi pass kabhi fail.
  \item False negatives (bugs nahi milte, ya sahi test case fail ho jata hai).
  \item CI/CD pipeline mein problems aati hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Sync Problems in Web Testing}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Page load hota hai, but element baad mein aata hai.
  \item Animations, Ajax, ya JS events ke wajah se timing mismatch ho jata hai.
  \item Selenium DOM ko real-time poll nahi karta, isliye mismatch easily ho jaate hain12.
\end{itemize}

\section*{Selenium Wait Types (with Python examples and step-by-step explanation)}

\subsection*{1. Implicit Wait}

\paragraph{Kya hai?}  
Global timeout—jitne bhi \texttt{find\_element()} ya similar locators hain, un sab pe ek wait lag jaata hai. Agar element turant mil jaata hai toh aage badh jayega, nahi toh set time tak try karega.

\paragraph{Syntax:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
driver.implicitly_wait(5)
\end{lstlisting}

Yahan driver 5 secs tak try karega element dhoondhne ka, har \texttt{find\_element()} ke liye4567.

Pura session global hai—jab set kar diya, jab tak close nahi karte, apply hota hai.

\paragraph{Pros:} Simple

\paragraph{Cons:} SLOW, har element pe lagega, kabhi-kabhi expected nahi hota.

\paragraph{Best for:} Static ya mostly predictable websites.

\subsection*{2. Explicit Waits (WebDriverWait, ExpectedConditions)}

\paragraph{Kya hai?}  
Tum khud define karo kisko (kaunsi condition) kitni der tak wait karna hai.

\paragraph{Syntax:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver.common.by import By
from selenium.webdriver.support.ui import WebDriverWait
from selenium.webdriver.support import expected_conditions as EC

driver = webdriver.Chrome()
driver.get("https://example.com")

# Wait up to 10 sec till element with ID 'myID' is present
element = WebDriverWait(driver, 10).until(
    EC.presence_of_element_located((By.ID, "myID"))
)
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{WebDriverWait}: Maximum 10 secs tak wait karega.
  \item \texttt{EC.presence\_of\_element\_located}: Jaise hi condition true ho gayi (element mil gaya), wait break ho jayega.
  \item Other conditions: visibility, clickable, text present, title, etc.489710
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Pros:} Targeted, efficient, only as long as needed

\paragraph{Cons:} Thoda code zyada lagta hai

\paragraph{Best for:} Dynamic web apps, real-world use

\subsection*{3. Fluent Waits}

\paragraph{Kya hai?}  
Explicit ka advanced version—yahan tum define kar sakte ho:
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Max time kitna,
  \item Kitni baar poll kare,
  \item Kaunse exceptions ignore karein.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Syntax:}
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver.support.ui import WebDriverWait
from selenium.common.exceptions import NoSuchElementException

wait = WebDriverWait(
    driver, 
    timeout=10, 
    poll_frequency=2,                   # Har 2 sec me check karega
    ignored_exceptions=[NoSuchElementException]
)

element = wait.until(
    lambda driver: driver.find_element(By.ID, "myID")
)
\end{lstlisting}

Maximum 10 seconds tak, har 2 seconds me retry karega.

Agar \texttt{NoSuchElementException} aayi toh ignore karega, next poll karega11712.

\paragraph{Pros:} Zyada control, perfect for flaky/dynamically loaded elements

\paragraph{Cons:} Complexity thodi badh jati hai

\subsection*{4. Custom Waits using Lambda Functions}

Agar tumhara condition predefined ExpectedConditions me nahi hai, toh tum lambda ya custom function de sakte ho:

\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
element = WebDriverWait(driver, 10).until(lambda d: d.find_element(By.CLASS_NAME, "custom-class").is_displayed())
\end{lstlisting}

Jab tak element visible nahi hota, yeh check chalta rahega.

Kisi bhi custom condition ke liye use kar sakte ho137.

\subsection*{5. Page Load Strategies}

By default Selenium poori page loading (CSS/images/js) ka wait karta hai. But kabhi-kabhi tumhe jaldi proceed karna hota hai (like only DOM loaded but images pending).

\paragraph{Strategies:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{normal} (default): Wait till everything loaded (recommended for most).
  \item \texttt{eager}: Wait only till DOMContentLoaded.
  \item \texttt{none}: Bilkul bhi wait na karo, jaise hi navigation ho jaye, code aage badh jaye.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Python Example:}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver.chrome.options import Options

options = Options()
options.page_load_strategy = 'eager'  # 'normal', 'eager', or 'none'
driver = webdriver.Chrome(options=options)
\end{lstlisting}

Aap script ki requirement ke hisaab se set kar sakte ho, lekin none risky hai1415.

\section*{Summary Table}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{|p{3.5cm}|p{2.5cm}|p{3.5cm}|p{3.5cm}|p{3.0cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Wait Type} & \textbf{Scope} & \textbf{Use-Case} & \textbf{Pros} & \textbf{Cons} \\
\hline
Implicit Wait & Global & Mostly static sites & Easy, set once & Can slow suite, not targeted \\
\hline
Explicit Wait & Per action & Dynamic elements, AJAX, etc. & Accurate, reliable & More code needed \\
\hline
Fluent Wait & Per action & Unstable/delayed elements & Max control & Little complex \\
\hline
Custom Waits & Per action & Unusual conditions & Any logic & Must handle error \\
\hline
PageLoadStrategy & Session & Fast page(s), partial loads & Speed boost & Risk of missing elements \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\vspace{5pt}
\section*{Golden Rules:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \mostimportant{Do NOT mix implicit and explicit waits.} Unpredictable results milte hain!7
  \item Be specific: Only wait as much as needed, warna scripts slow ho jayengi.
  \item Debug properly: Wrong waits == hard to fix flaky scripts.
\end{itemize}

\section{Working with Web Tables in Selenium Python}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Why Important Hai?}}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Web tables mein data organize hota hai rows aur columns mein.
  \item Testing mein zaruri hota hai tables se data nikalna, check karna, ya koi row filter karna.
  \item Agar table dynamic hai (rows change hote hain), toh handle karna thoda tricky hota hai.
  \item Agar na samjho toh data verification mushkil ho jayega, ya test fail hoga.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{1. Table Data Read Karna (Rows aur Columns)}}

\textbf{Step-by-step example}

Suppose ek simple HTML table hai jisme rows ke andar columns hain. Humko poora table data read karna hai:

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Table Data Read Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium import webdriver
from selenium.webdriver.common.by import By
from webdriver_manager.chrome import ChromeDriverManager

driver = webdriver.Chrome(ChromeDriverManager().install())
driver.get("https://example.com/webltablepage")

# Table locate karo - maan lo ID se mil raha hai
table = driver.find_element(By.ID, "exampleTable")

# Table ke sare rows lo tbody ke andar se
rows = table.find_elements(By.TAG_NAME, "tr")

# Loop se har ek row ke cells read karna
for row in rows:
    cells = row.find_elements(By.TAG_NAME, "td")  # td matlab columns
    for cell in cells:
        print(cell.text, end=" | ")  # har cell ka text print karo
    print()   # naya line next row ke liye
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{find\_element(By.ID)} table locate karta hai.
  \item \texttt{find\_elements(By.TAG\_NAME, "tr")} se table ke rows milte hain.
  \item Har row mein \texttt{find\_elements(By.TAG\_NAME, "td")} se columns milte hain.
  \item \texttt{cell.text} se us column ka text milta hai.
  \item Print karke table ka pura data console mein dekh sakte ho.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{2. Search/Filter Specific Rows}}

Agar aapko table me se kuch specific data wala row find karna ho, jaise kisi column me "India" hona chahiye, toh aise karenge:

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Search Specific Row Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
for row in rows:
    cells = row.find_elements(By.TAG_NAME, "td")
    for cell in cells:
        if "India" in cell.text:     # Agar kisi cell me 'India' hai
            print("Found Row:", [c.text for c in cells])
            break  # row mil gaya toh next row pe jao
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Advanced: XPath se directly kisi condition wale rows dhoondhna}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Search Rows with XPath}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
rows = driver.find_elements(By.XPATH, "//table[@id='exampleTable']//tr[td[contains(text(),'India')]]")
for row in rows:
    print([cell.text for cell in row.find_elements(By.TAG_NAME, "td")])
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item XPath me condition lagake woh rows dhoondh raha hai jisme kisi bhi column ka text 'India' ho.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{3. Dynamic Content Handling in Web Tables}}

Dynamic table ka matlab rows/columns page load ke baad change ho sakte hain—jaise pagination, sorting ya Ajax calls ki wajah se data update hota hai.

\textbf{Key Tips:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Explicit Wait lagao taaki table ke rows fully load ho jayein.
  \item Pagination aaye toh uske buttons ko automate karo aur data extract karo.
  \item Rows ya columns count har baar calculate karo, na ki fixed number treat karo.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Wait example for dynamic content:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Explicit Wait for Table}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver.support.ui import WebDriverWait
from selenium.webdriver.support import expected_conditions as EC

wait = WebDriverWait(driver, 10)
table = wait.until(EC.presence_of_element_located((By.ID, "exampleTable")))
rows = table.find_elements(By.TAG_NAME, "tr")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Pagination example (agar table multiple pages me data rakhta hai):}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Pagination Handling Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
while True:
    rows = driver.find_elements(By.XPATH, "//table[@id='exampleTable']/tbody/tr")
    for row in rows:
        print([cell.text for cell in row.find_elements(By.TAG_NAME, 'td')])
    next_button = driver.find_element(By.ID, "nextPageBtn")
    if "disabled" in next_button.get_attribute("class"):
        break  # end of pages
    else:
        next_button.click()
        wait.until(EC.staleness_of(rows[0]))  # Wait for table to reload new data
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Har page ke rows print kiye jaate hain.
  \item Next button disable hone par loop end ho jata hai.
\end{itemize}

\vspace{0.5cm}
\section*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{Summary Table}}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{|p{4.8cm}|p{5.5cm}|p{5.3cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Selenium Methods Used} & \textbf{Use Case / Explanation} \\
\hline
Locate Table & \texttt{find\_element(By.ID or XPATH)} & Locate the full table element \\
\hline
Get Rows & \texttt{table.find\_elements(By.TAG\_NAME, "tr")} & Get all rows in table \\
\hline
Get Columns/Cells & \texttt{row.find\_elements(By.TAG\_NAME, "td")} & Get all cells in each row \\
\hline
Read Cell Text & \texttt{cell.text} & Get visible data from each cell \\
\hline
Search Rows & Loop condition or \texttt{XPath} with \texttt{contains(text(),...)} & Filter rows containing specific text \\
\hline
Handle Dynamic Content & Use Explicit Waits, Recaculate rows each time & Handle changing table data or pagination \\
\hline
Pagination Handling & Click next buttons, wait for reload, continue & Traverse all pages of table automatically \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\vspace{0.5cm}
