\begin{document}

\section*{Data-Driven Testing (DDT) in Selenium Python — Full Detailed Explanation}

\subsection*{1. DDT Kya Hai? (What is Data-Driven Testing?)}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{DDT matlab} test automation ka ek aisa approach jisme hum apne test scripts ko alag-alag data se chala sakte hain. 
  \item Matlab ek hi test case ko multiple data sets ke saath run kar sakte hain, bina code change kiye.  
  \item Data alag source (Excel, CSV, JSON, APIs) se liya jata hai aur test input/output uske hisaab se hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Example:} Agar tumhara login page hai, toh alag-alag usernames/passwords se authentication test kar sakte ho bina baar-baar alag code likhe.

\subsection*{2. Kyun Use Karte Hain DDT? (Why Use Data Driven Testing?)}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Manual data ko baar baar change karna time-consuming hota hai aur galtiyan ho sakti hai.  
  \item Automation me data ko alag rakh kar test maintain karna easy ho jaata hai.  
  \item Same test script se multiple scenarios (valid, invalid, edge cases) ko efficiently test kar sakte hain.  
  \item Scalability badh jaati hai, aur tests zyada reliable aur repeatable ho jaate hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{3. Kab Use Karein? (When to Use Data-Driven Testing?)}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab test cases me bar-bar alag inputs se test karna ho (login, registration, search, filters).  
  \item Jab smoke/regression boundary aur negative test cases banana ho.  
  \item Jab large test data ho jo baar-baar input lena ho.  
  \item Jab test automation ko modular aur maintainable banana ho.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{4. Agar Na Karo DDT Toh Kya Problem Hai? (If Not Used, Then?)}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Bar-bar test script ka code copy-paste ya hardcoding mein extra time lagega.  
  \item Test data update karna complicated ho jayega.  
  \item Test cases jitne ho utne complex management ho jayega.  
  \item Test coverage limited ho jayega edge cases ke liye.  
  \item Automation slow aur error prone banega.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{5. Kaise Implement Karte Hain DDT? (How to Implement Data-Driven Testing?)}

Hum alag-alag data sources se data le sakte hain, phir us data ko test cases me use karte hain.

\subsubsection*{Option 1: Excel File se Data Read/Write karna (using openpyxl or pandas)}

\paragraph{Excel Data Read karna (openpyxl ke saath)}

\textbf{Setup:}  
Pehle openpyxl install karo:

\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
pip install openpyxl
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Code Example:}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import openpyxl

# Excel file load karo
wb = openpyxl.load_workbook("testdata.xlsx")

# Specific sheet select karo
sheet = wb['Sheet1']

# Row 2 se start karte hain (assuming row1 headings hain)
for i in range(2, sheet.max_row + 1):
    username = sheet.cell(row=i, column=1).value  # Column 1 ka data (username)
    password = sheet.cell(row=i, column=2).value  # Column 2 ka data (password)
    print(username, password)
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{Line-by-Line Explanation:}  
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{load\_workbook("testdata.xlsx")} : Excel file ko memory me load karta hai.  
  \item \texttt{sheet = wb['Sheet1']} : 'Sheet1' naam ke tab ka content access karta hai.  
  \item \texttt{sheet.max\_row} : Sheet me total rows ki count deta hai.  
  \item Loop me har row ka username aur password uthaya gaya.  
  \item \texttt{.cell(row=x, column=y).value} : specific cell ka value extract karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Excel Data Write karna Example}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
# Row 2 aur column 3 me "Login Pass" likh rahe hain
sheet.cell(row=2, column=3, value="Login Pass")

# Excel file ko save karna na bhoolo, tabhi changes rakhe jayenge
wb.save("testdata.xlsx")
\end{lstlisting}

\paragraph{Pandas Se Excel Data Read Karna (Simple aur Fast)}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import pandas as pd

df = pd.read_excel("testdata.xlsx")

for index, row in df.iterrows():
    print(row["username"], row["password"])
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{pd.read\_excel()} se pure Excel ko dataframe me convert karta hai.  
  \item \texttt{df.iterrows()} se row by row data read karte hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Option 2: CSV File se Data Read Karna}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import csv

with open("testdata.csv", newline='') as file:
    reader = csv.DictReader(file)  # Header ke hisaab se dictionary bana deta hai
    for row in reader:
        print(row["username"], row["password"])
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item CSV files simple text format hote hain.  
  \item \texttt{DictReader} se har row ek dict ban jata hai with keys as header names.  
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Option 3: JSON File se Data Read Karna}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import json

with open("testdata.json") as file:
    data = json.load(file)
    for entry in data:
        print(entry["username"], entry["password"])
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item JSON files structured data format hai, API responses me common use hota hai.  
  \item Python \texttt{json.load()} se us data ko dictionary/list structure me load kar lete hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{6. Pytest ke Saath Data Injection (parametrize decorator)}

\subsubsection*{Kya Hai? (What is pytest.mark.parametrize?)}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Pytest ka ek powerful decorator hai jo ek test function ko multiple data sets ke saath baar-baar run karne deta hai.  
  \item Manual loop ya multiple test likhne ki zarurat nahi.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Kab Use Karein?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab same test case ko multiple data se run karna ho (login with multiple username/password).  
  \item Test code clean aur maintainable chahiye.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Agar Na Karein?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Repetitive aur messy code  
  \item Data ko manually change karna padega  
  \item Test coverage kam ho jayega
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Parametrize Example (Simple)}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import pytest

@pytest.mark.parametrize("username,password", [
    ("user1", "pass1"),
    ("user2", "pass2"),
    ("user3", "pass3")
])
def test_login(username, password):
    print(username, password)
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Yahan test\_login function 3 baar alag-alag data ke saath chalega.  
  \item Har tuple me username aur password define kiye hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Excel/CSV Data pytest ke Saath Link Karna}

Agar tum Excel/CSV se data directly chahte ho inject karna, toh ek helper function likh kar data lo, fir parametrize me use karo:

\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import pytest
import openpyxl

def get_excel_data():
    wb = openpyxl.load_workbook("testdata.xlsx")
    sheet = wb['Sheet1']
    data = []
    for i in range(2, sheet.max_row+1):
        username = sheet.cell(row=i, column=1).value
        password = sheet.cell(row=i, column=2).value
        data.append((username, password))
    return data

@pytest.mark.parametrize("username,password", get_excel_data())
def test_login(username, password):
    print(username, password)
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{7. Automated Form Submission with DDT}

\paragraph{Example Code}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium import webdriver
from selenium.webdriver.common.by import By
import pytest

@pytest.mark.parametrize("username,password", [
    ("user1", "pass1"),
    ("user2", "pass2"),
])
def test_form_submission(username, password):
    driver = webdriver.Chrome()
    driver.get("http://example.com/login")

    driver.find_element(By.ID, "username").send_keys(username)
    driver.find_element(By.ID, "password").send_keys(password)
    driver.find_element(By.ID, "btnLogin").click()

    # yahan assertions karo login success ke liye

    driver.quit()
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Explanation}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Har test run me browser chal raha hai.  
  \item Login page open hota hai.  
  \item Username aur password input fields me data fill karte hain.  
  \item Login button click karte hain.  
  \item Multiple data sets ke saath baar-baar ye test repeat hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\section*{Final Summary Table: DDT Quick Reference}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{|p{4.5cm}|p{4.5cm}|p{5cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Task} & \textbf{Library / Tool} & \textbf{Description / Example} \\
\hline
Excel read/write & openpyxl / pandas & Excel data read karke test me use karna \\
\hline
CSV read & csv & CSV data file se data lena \\
\hline
JSON read & json & JSON se structured data lena \\
\hline
Data injection in pytest & pytest.mark.parametrize & Multiple data sets ek test function me \\
\hline
Form submission automation & Selenium webdriver & send\_keys, click ke saath data use karna \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\section*{Golden Rules for DDT:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Test data ko \textbf{code se alag rakho} (Alag files ya DB me).  
  \item Data source fix karo, format standardize karo.  
  \item Test failures ke liye data aur results ko track \& log karna zaroori hai.  
  \item Repeatable, scalable aur maintainable tests banao.
\end{itemize}

\begin{document}

\title{\textcolor{sectionblue}{\textbf{Page Object Model (POM) Framework — Complete Guide with Examples}}}
\author{}
\date{}
\maketitle

\section{What is Page Object Model (POM)?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item POM ek \concept{design pattern} hai jo \concept{test automation me use hota hai}.
    \item Iska purpose hai \mostimportant{UI elements ka access aur actions ko organize karna ek structured tarike se}.
    \item Matlab: Har webpage ya screen ka ek \textbf{Python class} banta hai jisme us page ke \textbf{sare locators} (buttons, fields, links) aur \textbf{actions} (click, type karna, read karna) likhe jaate hain.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Example:}

Login page ka ek \texttt{LoginPage} class banega jisme username/password field ke locators aur login button click karne ka method hoga.

\section{Why POM Use Karna Zaroori Hai?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \mostimportant{Code Reusability}: Same UI element locator baar-baar har test me likhne ki zarurat nahi. Ek jagah update karo, sab jagah update ho jaayega.
    \item \mostimportant{Maintainability}: Agar UI me change aaye, toh sirf us page class me locator change karna padega, test scripts ko touch karne ki zarurat nahi.
    \item \mostimportant{Readability}: Test scripts bahut clean aur readable ho jaate hain, kyunki wo business steps par focus karte hain, technical UI details par nahi.
    \item \mostimportant{Separation of Concerns}: UI representation (Page class) aur test logic (test scripts) alag-alag rehta hai, jisse code organized banta hai.
\end{itemize}

\section{When Should You Use POM?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab \mostimportant{complex ya bade projects} pe kaam kar rahe ho.
  \item Jab \mostimportant{multiple testers/developers} ek saath automation code pe kaam karte ho.
  \item Jab test cases \mostimportant{long term ke liye maintainable} hone chahiye.
  \item Jab aap chahte ho ki \mostimportant{automation framework professional aur scalable} bane.
\end{itemize}

\section{Agar POM Na Use Karo: Problem Kya Hogi?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Test code me \mostimportant{bohot sari duplicate locators/actions} honge.
  \item UI me chhote bade changes par sari test scripts toot sakti hain.
  \item Project ka maintenance \mostimportant{husarang mushkil aur costly} ho jayega.
  \item Code \mostimportant{readability aur modularity khatam} ho jaayegi — har test me UI details fir se likhne padenge.
\end{itemize}

\section{POM Structure Ke Core Concepts}

\subsection{Page Classes (Locators + Actions)}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Ek webpage ko represent karta hai.
    \item Har element ka locator define hota hai (eg: \texttt{By.ID}, \texttt{By.XPATH}, etc.).
    \item Jo actions user page pe karta hai (text type karna, buttons click karna) wo methods ke form me likhe hote hain.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Example: \texttt{LoginPage.py}}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={LoginPage.py Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver.common.by import By

class LoginPage:
    def __init__(self, driver):
        self.driver = driver
        # Locators: har element ke liye tuple (Locator type, locator value)
        self.username_input = (By.ID, "username")
        self.password_input = (By.ID, "password")
        self.login_button = (By.ID, "loginBtn")

    # Actions as methods:
    def enter_username(self, username):
        self.driver.find_element(*self.username_input).send_keys(username)

    def enter_password(self, password):
        self.driver.find_element(*self.password_input).send_keys(password)

    def click_login(self):
        self.driver.find_element(*self.login_button).click()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Line-by-line Explanation:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{\_\_init\_\_(self, driver)}: Constructor jisme browser driver pass hota hai, jiske saath ye page kaam karega.
    \item \texttt{self.username_input = (By.ID, "username")}: Ye tuple locator define karta hai, jisme pehle locator ka type hai (ID), aur dusra locator value hai ("username").
    \item \texttt{enter_username(self, username)}: Method jo username input box me diya hua text type karta hai.
    \item \texttt{self.driver.find_element(*self.username_input)}: Python ka unpacking operator \texttt{*} use hota hai, jisse ye tuple \texttt{find_element(By.ID, "username")} me expand ho jaata hai.
    \item \texttt{send_keys(username)}: Selenium ka method, text input karne ke liye.
    \item Click method bhi ise tarah button ko find karke click karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Reusability \& Maintainability}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Page class me ek baar locator aur actions define karo, fir \mostimportant{sab test scripts me reuse karo}.
    \item Agar locator change hota hai to sirf page class me change karo—baaki test scripts automatic update ho jaayenge.
    \item Test scripts zyada clean aur business logic par focused hote hain, UI complexity mein nahi uljte.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{BasePage \& TestBase Structure}

\paragraph{BasePage.py}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Common helper methods sabhi pages ke liye. Jaise explicit wait, error handling, scrolling etc.
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={BasePage.py Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver.support.ui import WebDriverWait
from selenium.webdriver.support import expected_conditions as EC

class BasePage:
    def __init__(self, driver):
        self.driver = driver

    def wait_for_element(self, locator, timeout=10):
        return WebDriverWait(self.driver, timeout).until(EC.presence_of_element_located(locator))
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Isko sab pages inherit kar sakte hain — code repeat nahi hoga.
    \item Example: LoginPage could inherit BasePage to use wait methods.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{TestBase.py}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Test suite run karne ke liye setup/teardown ka kaam karta hai:
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={TestBase.py Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import unittest
from selenium import webdriver
from webdriver_manager.chrome import ChromeDriverManager

class TestBase(unittest.TestCase):
    def setUp(self):
        self.driver = webdriver.Chrome(ChromeDriverManager().install())
        self.driver.maximize_window()

    def tearDown(self):
        self.driver.quit()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Har ek test class ko \texttt{TestBase} inherit kar lena chahiye — tool setup and cleanup handle ho jayega.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Utility Classes — Waits, Logger, Screenshots}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \textbf{WaitUtils:} Explicit, fluent wait ke methods ko yahan rakho for reuse.
    \item \textbf{Logger:} Automation run time info ko log karne ke liye logger setup.
    \item \textbf{ScreenshotUtils:} Test fail hone par screenshot capture aur save karne ke liye helper class.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Screenshot Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={ScreenshotUtils Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import time

class ScreenshotUtils:
    def __init__(self, driver):
        self.driver = driver

    def take_screenshot(self, name='screenshot'):
        timestamp = time.strftime("%Y%m%d-%H%M%S")
        filename = f"{name}_{timestamp}.png"
        self.driver.save_screenshot(filename)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Har test ke fail hone par screenshot lena easy ho jaata hai.
\end{itemize}

\section{Ek Simple End-to-End Example — Test Case Using POM and TestBase}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={test\_login.py Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
# test_login.py
from TestBase import TestBase
from LoginPage import LoginPage

class TestLogin(TestBase):
    def test_valid_login(self):
        self.driver.get("http://example.com/login")

        login_page = LoginPage(self.driver)
        login_page.enter_username("testuser")
        login_page.enter_password("testpass")
        login_page.click_login()

        # yahan assertions lagao jaise dashboard load hua ya nahi
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{TestLogin} class \texttt{TestBase} inherit karta hai jisme driver setup/teardown hai.
    \item \texttt{self.driver.get()} browser ko page open karne ke liye.
    \item \texttt{LoginPage} object create kiya, jise driver pass kiya.
    \item UI interaction methods ko call kiya, test ka main flow simple aur readable bana.
    \item Assertions add karke verify kar sakte hain ki login successful hua ya nahi.
\end{itemize}

\section{Summary Table (POM Components)}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{|p{4cm}|p{6cm}|p{6cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{POM Component} & \textbf{Kya Kaam Karta Hai / Kya Contain Karta Hai} & \textbf{Kyun Zaroori Hai / Use Kyun Karte Hain} \\
\hline
Page Class & Locators + Page specific actions/methods & Reusability, locator update easy \\
\hline
BasePage & Common utilities jaise waits, scrolling, error handling & DRY code, shared common flows \\
\hline
TestBase & Browser setup, initialization, teardown & Har test ke liye common driver/session management \\
\hline
Utility Classes & Logging, screenshots, waits etc. & Framework ki maintainability, debugging enhance karne ke liye \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\section{Golden Rule}

\begin{quote}
Agar POM use nahi karoge, toh tumhara automation code \mostimportant{duplicate}, \mostimportant{mushkil maintain karne wala}, aur \mostimportant{unstable} ho jayega. Chhoti chhoti UI changes me puri test suite fail hogi.

Isliye, \mostimportant{POM sikhna aur use karna job-ready automation ka sabse zaroori step hai}.
\end{quote}

\vspace{0.5cm}

Agar chaho main \concept{ready-to-use folder structure}, \concept{multiple page class examples}, \concept{advance features jaise inheritance use karke common utility kaise banao}, ya kisi aur specific doubt clear karu toh batao bro!  
Main tumhari madad ekdum step-by-step karne ko tayyar hoon!

===============================

  linkcolor=blue,
  urlcolor=cyan,

\begin{document}

\section{PyTest Framework (Industry-Standard) — Beginner Friendly Guide}

\subsection*{1. PyTest Installation \& Usage}

\subsubsection*{What?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item PyTest ek popular Python testing framework hai.
  \item Ye simple hai, lightweight hai aur bahut powerful features provide karta hai.
  \item Automated test likhne aur chalane ke liye use hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item PyTest me test likhna bohot simple aur expressive hota hai.
  \item \texttt{assert} ka use karke expected vs actual check kar sakte ho.
  \item Fixtures, markers, parametrization easy hain.
  \item Large projects me scalable aur modular banata hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab bhi Python me automated tests banana ho, chahe unit ho, integration ho, ya Selenium automation ho.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Instead of pytest, agar basic \texttt{unittest} use karoge toh boilerplate zyada hota.
  \item Complex fixtures aur parametrization manually implement karna mushkil.
  \item Test execution aur reporting limited hoti hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Installation Command:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={PyTest Installation}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
pip install pytest
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsubsection*{Basic Usage:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item PyTest automatically test files ko find karta hai jiska naam \texttt{test\_} se shuru ho ya \texttt{\_test} se khatam ho.
  \item Test functions ka naam \texttt{test\_} se start hona chahiye, jaise \texttt{def test\_addition():}.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Simple Test Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Simple Test Function}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
def test_addition():
    assert 2 + 3 == 5
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{def test\_addition()} : Ye ek test function hai jo PyTest ko run karna hai.
  \item \texttt{assert 2 + 3 == 5}: Assert Python ka keyword hai, check karta hai expression true hai ya nahi. True hai toh test pass hoga.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{PyTest Run Command:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Run PyTest}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
pytest
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

Ye command current folder me test files dhundh ke run karta hai.

\newpage
\subsection*{2. Writing Tests with Assert}

\subsubsection*{What?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{assert} keyword built-in Python ka hota hai.
  \item Iska use to verify actual vs expected results.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Simple assertion se pata chalta hai test pass hai ya fail.
  \item PyTest fail hone pe error message dete hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Har test me use karo to verify correctness.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Test invalid hoga, ya Google/test framework ko pata nahi chalega test success ya failure ka.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Assertion Examples:}

\textbf{Passing assertion:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Passing Assertion}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
def test_subtract():
    result = 10 - 5
    assert result == 5   # Test will pass
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Failing assertion:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Failing Assertion}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
def test_fail():
    assert 1 == 0    # Test fail hoga with AssertionError
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

Jab assertion fail hota hai, PyTest detailed traceback aur error show karta hai console me.

\subsection*{3. Organizing Tests into Modules}

\subsubsection*{What?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Tests ko logically organize karne ke liye alag-alag Python files ya folders me rakhna.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Large projects me test management asaan hota hai.
  \item Bugs trace karna, specific test group chalana easy hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab test suite bada ho.
  \item Jab multiple test categories ho.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Sab tests ek file me hone se code messy ho jayega.
  \item Run/select karna specific subset mushkil hoga.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Folder Structure Example:}

\begin{verbatim}
tests/
    test_login.py
    test_checkout.py
    test_search.py
\end{verbatim}

PyTest recursively \texttt{tests/} directory scan kar ke sari test files aur functions run karega.

\subsection*{4. Fixtures: Setup \& Teardown at Different Levels}

\subsubsection*{What?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Fixtures predefined functions hote hai jo test se pehle setup aur test ke baad teardown me chalate hain.
  \item Ye reusable components hote hain jisse test code clean aur DRY banta hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Repetitive setup/cleanup code ko ek jagah manage karna asaan hota hai.
  \item Browser launch, database connect, environment prepare karna fixtures me hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab common pre-condition aur post-condition chahiye ho tests ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Har test me setup/cleanup likhna padega — code duplicate hoga.
  \item Maintenance tough hoga.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Simple Fixture Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Fixture Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import pytest

@pytest.fixture
def setup_browser():
    print("Setup before test")
    yield
    print("Teardown after test")

def test_example(setup_browser):
    print("Test running")
    assert True
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{@pytest.fixture} decorator se function fixture ban gaya.
  \item \texttt{yield} ke pehle ki line setup ke liye, baad ki line teardown ke liye hoti hai.
  \item \texttt{test_example} function me fixture \texttt{setup\_browser} ko argument ki tarah diya gaya — PyTest usko automatically call karta hai.
  \item Test chalne se pehle "Setup before test" print hoga, test run hoga, phir "Teardown after test" print hoga.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Fixture Scopes:}

\begin{tabular}{ | l | p{7cm} | l | }
\hline
\textbf{Scope} & \textbf{Explanation} & \textbf{Example} \\
\hline
function   & Har test function ke liye alag call (default) & \texttt{scope="function"} \\
class      & Ek test class ke sab tests ke liye ek baar call & \texttt{scope="class"} \\
module     & Ek file ke sab tests ke liye ek baar call & \texttt{scope="module"} \\
session    & Pure test session ke liye ek baar chalata hai & \texttt{scope="session"} \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\subsubsection*{Example Fixture with Scope:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Scoped Fixture Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
@pytest.fixture(scope="module")
def setup_module():
    print("Setup module")
    yield
    print("Teardown module")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{5. Hooks: Custom Code During Test Lifecycle}

\subsubsection*{What?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Hooks special functions hote hain jo PyTest ke test run ke different phases me automatically call hote hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item PyTest run ko customize karne ke liye.
    \item Jaise failures pe logs capture karna, report me kuch add karna, ya custom setup karna.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Advanced test framework banate wakt.
    \item Custom logging \& reporting me.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Test execution me flexibility kam hogi.
    \item Some features ko automate nahi kar paoge.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Example Hooks in \texttt{conftest.py}:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Hook Examples}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
def pytest_runtest_setup(item):
    print(f"Setting up {item.name}")

def pytest_runtest_makereport(item, call):
    if call.when == 'call':
        if call.excinfo is not None:
            print(f"Test {item.name} failed")
        else:
            print(f"Test {item.name} passed")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \texttt{item.name}: current test ka name.
    \item \texttt{call.when}: test ke phase (setup, call, teardown).
    \item \texttt{call.excinfo}: exception info agar test fail hua to.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{6. Markers: Test Functions Ko Categorize Karna}

\subsubsection*{What?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Markers decorations hote hain jisse test ko category/class assign karte hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Different suite run karna easy hota hai.
    \item Kuch test ko skip/xfail karne me madad karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Smoke, regression, sanity tests ko alag chalana ho.
    \item Kuch tests temporarily skip karna ho.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Sab test ek saath chalayenge, time zyada lagega.
    \item Filters aur reports me confusion hoga.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Common Marker Examples:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Marker Examples}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import pytest

@pytest.mark.smoke
def test_smoke1():
    assert True

@pytest.mark.regression
def test_regression1():
    assert True

@pytest.mark.skip(reason="Skipping temporarily")
def test_skip():
    assert False

@pytest.mark.xfail(reason="Known bug")
def test_expected_fail():
    assert False
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsubsection*{Run only smoke tests:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Run Only Smoke Tests}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
pytest -m smoke
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{skip} wale test run nahi honge.
  \item \texttt{xfail} expected failed tests ko mark karta hai taaki report me pass/fail wisely dikhe.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Custom Markers Add Karna (\texttt{pytest.ini}):}

\begin{verbatim}
[pytest]
markers =
    smoke: smoke tests
    regression: regression tests
    sanity: sanity tests
\end{verbatim}

\subsection*{7. Parallel Execution With pytest-xdist}

\subsubsection*{What?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Multiple test cases ek saath (parallel) chalana.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Test execution time kam karna.
  \item Large test suites ke liye must.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab test suite bada ho.
  \item Continuous integration pipelines me fast feedback chahiye.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Sequential execution slow hoga.
  \item Productivity kam hogi.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Installation:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Parallel Execution Installation}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
pip install pytest-xdist
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsubsection*{Run Tests in Parallel:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Run Tests in Parallel}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
pytest -n 4
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item 4 CPU threads pe parallel tests chalenge.
  \item \texttt{-n auto} se CPU cores auto detect karke chalata hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Best Practices:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Tests ko isolate karo.
  \item Shared global state avoid karo.
  \item Data conflicts na ho aise likho tests.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\subsection*{Summary Table}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{|p{4cm}|p{6cm}|p{6cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Purpose / Explanation} & \textbf{Example} \\
\hline
PyTest Installation & PyTest install karna & \texttt{pip install pytest} \\
\hline
Writing Tests & Assert se test likhna & \texttt{def test\_func(): assert True} \\
\hline
Organizing Tests & Multiple files and folders me organize karna & Folder jaise \texttt{tests/test\_login.py} \\
\hline
Fixtures & Setup/teardown reusable code & \texttt{@pytest.fixture} use karo \\
\hline
Hooks & Custom actions during test lifecycle & \texttt{pytest\_runtest\_setup}, \texttt{pytest\_runtest\_makereport} \\
\hline
Markers & Test categorize karne ke liye & \texttt{@pytest.mark.smoke} \\
\hline
Parallel Execution & Tests ko ek saath chalana & \texttt{pytest -n 4} \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\subsection*{Ek Simple Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Simple PyTest Example with Fixture and Markers}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import pytest

@pytest.fixture(scope="module")
def setup_data():
    print("Setup module data")
    yield
    print("Teardown module data")

@pytest.mark.smoke
def test_addition(setup_data):
    assert 2 + 2 == 4

@pytest.mark.regression
def test_subtraction():
    assert 5 - 3 == 2

@pytest.mark.skip(reason="Not ready yet")
def test_skip_me():
    assert False
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Run command (Smoke tests verbose):}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Run Smoke Tests Verbose}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
pytest -m smoke -v
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{Agar Chahiye Toh}

Main aapko advanced PyTest frameworks, detailed examples, Selenium integration, reporting & logging, aur CI/CD pipelines ke liye PyTest ka best use bata sakta hoon. Bas batayega!

\begin{document}

\section{Logging, Reporting \& Debugging - Complete Structure se Explanation}

\subsection*{1. Logging with \texttt{logging} Module}

\concept{Why Logging?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab test chal rahe hote hain toh har action, step, warning, aur error ko record karna zaroori hota hai.
  \item Agar koi bug ya failure aaye toh logs dekh kar pata lagta hai kahan dikkat hai.
  \item Logs debugging, maintenance aur audit ke liye best practice hain.
  \item Team members ko bhi samajh aata hai ki test execution me kya hua.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When to Use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Har test automation framework me use karo.
  \item Especially bade projects me jahan multiple test cases aur users involved ho.
  \item Jab flaky tests ya complex failures diagnose karne ho.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Agar Na Use Karein Toh?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Failures ki wajah samajhna mushkil ho jayega.
  \item Test results inconsistent lagenge.
  \item Debug karne me time aur effort zyada lagega.
  \item Automation ka fayda kam ho jayega.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example + Line-by-Line Explanation:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Logging Setup Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import logging  # Python ka logging module import kar rahe hain

logging.basicConfig(
    level=logging.DEBUG,  # Sabse detailed level se logging shuru karenge (DEBUG se upar ke sab log honge)
    format='%(asctime)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s',  # Log message ka format (timestamp, level, message)
    filename='test_log.log',  # Logs ek file me save karenge jiska naam test_log.log hoga
    filemode='w'  # Har baar naye run pe file overwrite hogi, purani delete ho jayegi
)

logging.debug("Ye debug message hai")  
# DEBUG ka matlab sabse low level ka detail message — mostly development ke liye useful hai

logging.info("Test start ho gaya")
# INFO level ka message — jab test start ho jaye ya koi important milestone ho

logging.warning("Thoda dhyan se! Unexpected behavior")
# WARNING ka matlab kuch ajeeb ya unexpected hua, lekin abhi problem nahi

logging.error("Error aaya element locate karte waqt")
# ERROR ka message — jab error aaye ya koi step fail ho

logging.critical("Critical failure, pura test hang")
# CRITICAL sabse bada error, system ya test execution pura fail ho raha ho
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{0.5cm}
\subsection*{2. Screenshot Capture (Full Page / Elements)}

\concept{Why Important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab test fail ho jata hai to us waqt ka screenshot lena debugging ke liye bahut help karta hai.
  \item Visual proof milta hai ki screen pe kya dikh raha tha.
  \item Developers ya testers ko samajhne me ease hoti hai problems ko.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When to Use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab test case fail ho.
  \item Kabhi kabhi pass hone wale cases me bhi document karne ke liye.
  \item Automated screenshot generation on failure hooks me.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Agar Na Use Karein?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Failures ka reason samajhna bohot mushkil hoga.
  \item Bug reproduce karne me time waste hoga.
  \item Report me proof kam hoga.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example + Explanation:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Screenshot Capture Examples}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
driver.save_screenshot("full_page.png")
# Ye pura browser window ka screenshot "full_page.png" file me save karta hai

element = driver.find_element(By.ID, "submitBtn")
element.screenshot("element_screenshot.png")
# Sirf specific element ka hi screenshot "element_screenshot.png" file me save karega
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{0.5cm}
\subsection*{3. PyTest HTML Reports (\texttt{pytest-html})}

\concept{Why Important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Readable aur user-friendly report chahiye jisme pass/fail clearly dikhai de.
  \item Automatic screenshot attach kar sakte hain failure ke time.
  \item Team members ko results easily share karne me help karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When to Use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab detailed test reports chahiye.
  \item Integration with CI/CD pipelines me.
  \item Jab manual intervention ke bina test results samajhne hain.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Agar Na Use Karein?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Sirf console logs pe depend karna padega.
  \item Complex failures ko samajhna mushkil hoga.
  \item Dushre stakeholders ke liye sharing muskil hoti hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example \& Usage:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Install \& Run pytest-html}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
pip install pytest-html

pytest --html=report.html --self-contained-html
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\noindent Is command se \texttt{report.html} file generate hogi, jisme test results, errors, screenshots sab honge.

\vspace{0.5cm}
\subsection*{4. Allure Reports Integration}

\concept{Why Important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Allure rich, interactive dashboard deta hai with graphs, history and detailed logs.
  \item Industry standard hai professional reporting ke liye.
  \item Jenkins jaisi CI tools ke saath easily integrate hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When to Use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab detailed analytics aur visual feedback chahiye.
  \item Large scale projects mein testing metrics track karne ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Agar Na Use Karein?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Basic reporting hi milega, jo complex projects me insufficient hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example \& Usage:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Allure Installation \& Usage}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
pip install allure-pytest

pytest --alluredir=allure-results

allure serve allure-results
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{0.3cm}
\textbf{Screenshot on failure (Allure integration):}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Allure Screenshot Hook Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import allure

@pytest.hookimpl(hookwrapper=True)
def pytest_runtest_makereport(item, call):
    outcome = yield
    rep = outcome.get_result()
    if rep.when == "call" and rep.failed:
        driver = item.funcargs['driver']  # Assuming 'driver' fixture name
        screenshot = driver.get_screenshot_as_png()
        allure.attach(screenshot, name="Screenshot", attachment_type=allure.attachment_type.PNG)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{0.5cm}
\subsection*{5. Screenshot on Failure (Hook-Based)}

\concept{Why Important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Automatically screenshot lena jab bhi test fail ho jaye, taaki manual check na karna pade.
  \item Debugging easy ho jaati hai.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When to Use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab test suite me failures ho rahe hain aur fix karna ho.
  \item Continuous testing environment me.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Agar Na Use Karein?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Failures me screenshot nahi milega.
  \item Debug karna time-consuming hoga.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example with explanation:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Hook to Capture Screenshot on Failure}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import pytest

@pytest.hookimpl(hookwrapper=True)
def pytest_runtest_makereport(item, call):
    outcome = yield                         # Test execution result ka wait kar raha hoon
    rep = outcome.get_result()              # Result ko get kar liya
    if rep.when == 'call' and rep.failed:  # Agar actual test call phase me failure hai toh
        driver = item.funcargs.get('driver', None)  # Driver fixture ko access kiya
        if driver:
            screenshot_path = f"screenshots/{item.name}.png"
            driver.save_screenshot(screenshot_path) # Screenshot file me save kar diya
            print(f"Screenshot saved to {screenshot_path}")  # Console me message diya
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{0.5cm}
\subsection*{6. Debugging Flaky Tests}

\concept{Why Important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Flaky tests unpredictable hote hain — kab pass, kab fail.
  \item Production level automation ke liye flaky tests bohot problem create karte hain.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When to Use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab test results inconsistent aayein.
  \item Jab environment aur timings unstable ho.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Agar Na Use Karein?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Automation suite unreliable ho jayega.
  \item Confidence lost hoga testing results pe.
  \item Time waste hoga failures ko repeat karke check karne me.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Common Fixes \& Best Practices}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Use Explicit Waits (\texttt{WebDriverWait}) instead of \texttt{time.sleep()}.
  \item Improve locator reliability.
  \item Increase timeout and poll frequency.
  \item Isolate tests to avoid interference.
  \item Use retry plugins like \texttt{pytest-rerunfailures}.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Retry Example}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Retry Plugin Installation and Usage}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
pip install pytest-rerunfailures

pytest --reruns 2
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\noindent Agar test fail ho jaye to 2 baar automatically retry karega.

\vspace{0.5cm}
\usepackage{tabularx} % Add in preamble somewhere near other packages

% ...

\subsection*{Summary Table}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|p{3.5cm}|p{3.5cm}|X|p{3.5cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Concept} & \textbf{Why Important} & \textbf{When to Use} & \textbf{Code/Method Example} \\
\hline
Logging & Steps, errors track karne ke liye & Har automation framework me & \texttt{logging.basicConfig(), logging.info()} \\
\hline
Screenshot Capture & Visual error proof & Failure ya debugging time & \texttt{driver.save\_screenshot()} \\
\hline

\hline

\hline
Screenshot on Failure (Hook) & Auto screenshot on test fail & Robust debugging & \texttt{pytest\_runtest\_makereport hook} \\
\hline
Debugging Flaky Tests & Stability and reliability & Flaky tests track karne & \texttt{WebDriverWait, pytest-rerunfailures} \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}

\begin{document}

\section{Visual \& Accessibility Testing — Step-by-Step Guide}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{1. Full-Page Screenshots with Image Comparison (using PIL, OpenCV)}}

\textbf{What is this?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Ye technique hoti hai jisme hum poore web page ya application ka screenshot lete hain.
  \item Us screenshot ko baseline (pehle se store image) ke sath compare karte hain.
  \item Difference detect kar ke dekhte hain ki UI ya design me koi unexpected change to nahi hua.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why important hai?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Software ke UI (colors, fonts, layout, spacing) me chhote-chhote badlav ko manually pakadna mushkil hota hai.
  \item Manual inspection me visual bugs miss ho sakte hain, jo production me ja sakte hain.
  \item Automated comparison se pata lagta hai ki kya change hua, aur exact jagah color ya shape ka fark kaha hai.
  \item Isse hum production release se pehle bugs catch kar sakte hain jo visual quality ko effect karte hain.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When use karein?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Har build ya release ke baad UI regression test karte waqt.
  \item Jab website me CSS, front-end code frequent change hote hain.
  \item Responsive design testing, cross-browser compatibility check karne ke liye.
  \item Jab user experience critical ho (E-commerce, banking app, complex portals).
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Agar na karein toh?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item UI bugs unnoticed rahenge.
  \item Production me visual inconsistencies aayengi, user disappoint hoga.
  \item Brand reputation nuksaan me ja sakta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example (Screenshot + Image Comparison):}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Image Comparison Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import pyautogui              # Screen capture ke liye
from PIL import Image          # Image processing ke liye
import numpy as np            # Array operations ke liye
import cv2                    # OpenCV, image difference aur processing ke liye

# Step 1: Screenshot lena
screenshot = pyautogui.screenshot()     # Screen ka screenshot capture karte hain
screenshot.save("current.png")           # Screenshot ko file me save karte hain

# Step 2: Pehle se saved baseline image (reference image) load karo
img1 = np.array(Image.open("baseline.png"))   # Pehle se stored image ko numpy array me convert karte hain
img2 = np.array(Image.open("current.png"))    # Abhi ka screenshot bhi numpy array me convert karte hain

# Step 3: Do images ka difference nikaalo (pixel level)
diff = cv2.absdiff(img1, img2)            # Absolute pixel difference, jahan pixels same nahi hote wahan white color create hota hai

# Step 4: Differences ko grey scale me convert karo
gray = cv2.cvtColor(diff, cv2.COLOR_BGR2GRAY)   # Color difference ko grayscale me badalna

# Step 5: Threshold apply karo jisse chhote mote changes ignore ho aur badi differences highlight hon
_, thresh = cv2.threshold(gray, 30, 255, cv2.THRESH_BINARY)

# Step 6: Difference ko nayi image file me save karo
cv2.imwrite("diff.png", thresh)

# Step 7: Check karo dono images bilkul same hain ya nahi
if img1.shape == img2.shape and np.all(img1 == img2):
    print("Images are identical!")
else:
    print("Images are different.")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Line-by-line explanation:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{pyautogui.screenshot()} se current screen ka screenshot liya.
  \item \texttt{screenshot.save("current.png")} us screenshot ko disk pe "current.png" naam se save kiya.
  \item \texttt{Image.open()} se PNG image open kar ke \texttt{np.array()} se NumPy array banaya, jisse pixel wise calculations easy hote hain.
  \item \texttt{cv2.absdiff(img1, img2)} se dono images ke pixels ka absolute difference liya.
  \item \texttt{cv2.cvtColor(..., cv2.COLOR_BGR2GRAY)} difference image ko grayscale me convert kiya.
  \item \texttt{cv2.threshold()} se grayscale image me threshold apply kiya jisse sirf significant differences white show kare.
  \item \texttt{cv2.imwrite()} se difference image file me save kiya.
  \item Last me check kiya ki dono images bilkul same hain ya nahi.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{2. Visual Regression Testing (Percy, Applitools)}}

\textbf{What?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Ye tools advanced visual testing ke liye automation handle karte hain.
  \item Apne build system ya test framework me integrations provide karte hain jisse har test run pe screenshots le ke automatically compare karte hain.
  \item AI/Smart diffing karte hain taaki false positives (chhoti chhoti insignificant changes) kam report ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why important hai?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Visual bugs ko jaldi identify karne me madad karta hai.
  \item Manual mistakes ya missed regression reduce hota hai.
  \item Cross-browser ya device wise UI changes manual baar-baar check karne ki zarurat nahi.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When use karein?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab Continuous Integration/Delivery (CI/CD) pipeline me regression test hai.
  \item Feature-rich UI applications me jisme frequent UI changes hote hain.
  \item Cross platform, cross browser UI consistency ensure karna ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Agar na karo toh?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Visual bugs production me chala jayega.
  \item Manual testing zyada time lega.
  \item UI consistency issues rahenge jo brand value ko hurt karenge.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Popular Tools:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Percy (BrowserStack)}: Automated screenshot + baseline compare system with CI/CD integration.
  \item \textbf{Applitools Eyes}: AI-powered visual diffing with intelligent ignore rules and easy maintenance.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Workflow:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Test ke har UI screen ya state pe screenshot lete hain.
  \item Pehle se stored baseline images se comparison karte hain.
  \item Differences highlight karte hain ek dashboard me.
  \item Reviewers changes accept/reject karte hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{3. Detect Broken Images, Links, Missing Text}}

\textbf{What?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Web page me jo images nahi load hote (broken images) ya links invalid ho (dead links).
  \item Missing important text ya UI components nahi dikh rahe.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why important hai?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Broken images aur links user experience kharab karte hain.
  \item Functional issues lead kar sakte hain (wrong navigation, errors).
  \item Early detection bugs ko jaldi fix karna allow karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When use karein?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Har regression or smoke test me.
  \item New UI/content deployments ke baad.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Agar na use karo toh?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Users ko broken UI milega.
  \item Critical bugs late detect honge.
  \item Business lose kar sakta hai user trust.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example (Broken Images Detection with Selenium + requests):}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Broken Images Detection}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium import webdriver
from selenium.webdriver.common.by import By
import requests

driver = webdriver.Chrome()
driver.get("https://example.com")

# Step 1: Saare image elements locate karo
images = driver.find_elements(By.TAG_NAME, "img")

# Step 2: Har image ka 'src' attribute leke HTTP request bhejo
for img in images:
    src = img.get_attribute("src")
    if src:
        try:
            response = requests.get(src)
            # Step 3: Agar status code 200 nahi, toh image broken hai
            if response.status_code != 200:
                print(f"Broken image found: {src} - Status Code: {response.status_code}")
        except requests.exceptions.RequestException as e:
            print(f"Error checking image {src}: {e}")

driver.quit()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Code Explanation:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{driver.find\_elements(By.TAG\_NAME, "img")}: Page ke sare image elements find kiye.
  \item Har image ka src URL liya \texttt{get\_attribute("src")} se.
  \item \texttt{requests.get(src)} se us URL pe HTTP request bheja.
  \item Server se response code 200 hai ya nahi check kiya.
  \item Code 200 nahi hone pe broken image print kar diya.
  \item Exceptions ko catch kiya taaki script crash na ho.
\end{itemize}

\textit{Note: Isi logic se links (anchor tags <a>) ke href attribute check kar sakte hain similarly. Agar href URL 404 ya error deta hai toh broken link hai.}

\subsection*{\textcolor{sectionblue}{4. Accessibility Testing Tools: axe-core, Lighthouse CLI}}

\textbf{What?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Accessibility testing ka matlab hai website ko aise banana jo sab log use kar saken — specially visually impaired, screen-reader users, keyboard users etc.
  \item \textbf{a11y testing} legal requirement hota jaa raha hai (WCAG standards).
  \item Tools like axe-core (JavaScript library) aur Google Lighthouse CLI automatically accessibility errors detect karte hain.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Why Important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Aapka product sab users ke liye accessible ho.
  \item Legal compliance aur best practices follow karna.
  \item User base aur reputation badhane ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When Use Karein?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Har major release ke pehle.
  \item Jab bhi front-end UI me changes aaye.
  \item CI/CD pipeline me automated accessibility tests integrate karna.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Agar Na Karein Toh?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Accessibility bugs production me rahenge.
  \item Legal fine and penalty ka risk badhta hai.
  \item Users base restrict ho jayega, brand damage hoga.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Tools \& Usage:}

\subsubsection*{a) axe-core (Deque)}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Javascript based accessibility engine.
  \item Selenium testing me JS execute kar ke accessibility violations detect karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Sample Usage (Selenium Python):}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={axe-core Integration}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
# Selenium me axe-core JS inject kar ke run karna:

driver.execute_script(open("axe.min.js").read())  # axe-core library ko page me inject karo
results = driver.execute_script("return axe.run(document)")  # axe-core run karo aur results lo
print(results)  # Violations ka summary print karo
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Axe-core JS ko web page me insert karte hain.
  \item axe.run(document) call se accessibility violations list milti hai.
  \item Aap is output ko parse karke test assertions bana sakte hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{b) Lighthouse CLI (Google)}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Chrome ka ek command line tool jo in-depth accessibility, performance, SEO audit karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Run command:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Lighthouse CLI Accessibility Audit}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
lighthouse https://example.com --only-categories=accessibility
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Ye report generate karta hai with scores and actionable items.
  \item Automated or manual use dono kar sakte ho.
\end{itemize}

\vspace{0.5cm}
\section*{Summary Table: Quick Reference}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{|p{4.2cm}|p{4cm}|p{4cm}|p{4cm}|p{3.1cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Topic} & \textbf{Why Important} & \textbf{When Use} & \textbf{If Not Used} & \textbf{Example / Tool} \\
\hline
Visual Screenshot Compare & UI bugs detect kare & Build ke baad, regression & UI bugs slip production & PIL, OpenCV, Percy, Applitools \\
\hline
Visual Regression Testing & Automated UI comparison & Continuous testing, UI changes & Manual testing zyada & Percy, Applitools \\
\hline
Broken Images/Links & UX aur function failure detect kare & Regression / Smoke tests & User broken UI face kare & Selenium + requests \\
\hline
Accessibility Testing & User coverage aur legal compliance & Major releases, CI/CD & Accessibility issues miss & axe-core(JS), Lighthouse CLI \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\begin{document}

\section{Cross-Browser, Parallel, and Remote Testing}

\subsection*{1. Cross-Browser Testing (Chrome, Firefox, Edge, Safari)}

\textbf{Why important hai?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Har user har browser ya device pe tumhare app ko alag-alag dekh raha hota hai.
  \item Kuch features ya CSS/JS sabhi browsers pe same nahi dikhte — Chrome me chale, Firefox me error aa jaaye, etc.
  \item Real users ka experience ensure karne ke liye cross-browser testing critical hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When use karein?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Har major release pe, production deploy karne se pehle.
  \item Responsive, design, authentication jaise features ke liye zaroor.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Agar na karo toh?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Unknown bugs slip ho jaayenge.
  \item Real users ka trust lose — production me broken UI/bugs.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Selenium Python Example: Different Browsers pe run karna}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Cross-Browser Selenium Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium import webdriver

# Chrome
driver = webdriver.Chrome()

# Firefox
driver = webdriver.Firefox()

# Edge
driver = webdriver.Edge()

# Safari (SafariDriver pe Mac pe preinstalled, Safari mein "Allow Remote Automation" ON karo)
driver = webdriver.Safari()

driver.get("https://example.com")
driver.quit()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

Har driver se respective browser open hota hai. Tum ek hi script mein browser variable pass karke bhi cross-browser loop bana sakte ho.

\subsection*{2. Parallel Testing — pytest-xdist \& multiprocessing}

\textbf{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Test bohot ho gaye toh sequentially run karoge toh time waste.
  \item Parallel run se test execution time bohot kam ho jaata hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Large test suite — 10-1000+ cases.
  \item CI/CD integration, fast feedback.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{If not used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Test suite slow, developers ko feedback late.
  \item Deployment speed kam.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{pytest-xdist ka use (Parallel run in Selenium tests):}

\textbf{Install karo:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={pytest-xdist Installation}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
pip install pytest pytest-xdist
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Simple usage (4 CPU cores pe parallel run):}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Run PyTest Parallel}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
pytest -n 4
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

Tum \texttt{-n auto} bhi likh sakte ho — jitne cores system detect kare, utne pe parallel run karega.

Multiprocessing (Python ka inbuilt module) bhi use hota hai, lekin pytest-xdist Selenium-automation me zyada popular/flexible hai.

\subsection*{3. Selenium Grid: Remote, Parallel, and Multi-Browser infra}

\textbf{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Multiple browsers \& OS pe parallel run karna ho — local system pe impossible ho jaata hai.
  \item Distributed infra ya remote machines use karna ho.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Cross-team, enterprise scale, remote VM infra, Cloud clusters.
  \item Lagatar test runs for every commit/PR.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{If not used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Local resource pe hi stuck rahoge.
  \item Scalability, coverage less hoga.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Concept: Hub \& Node}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Hub: Control center. Test requests idhar aate hain.
  \item Node: Actual browser/OS wala machine. Jo bhi hub assign kare, woh node execute karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Basic Setup (Manual) Step-by-Step:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Selenium Grid Manual Setup}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
# Selenium Server jar download karo (selenium.dev)

# Hub start karo:
java -jar selenium-server-<version>.jar hub

# Node join karo:
java -jar selenium-server-<version>.jar node --hub http://<hub-ip>:4444
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

Apne Selenium script me remote WebDriver ka config do, browser \& desired capabilities set karo.

\textbf{Docker ke Saath Selenium Grid Setup:}

\textbf{Why Docker?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Setup ekdum easy, repeatable, scalable.
  \item 1 command me grid infra create/destroy.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{How to:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Docker Grid Setup}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
# Docker install karo.

# Grid network banao:
docker network create grid

# Hub container run karo:
docker run -d -p 4444:4444 --net grid --name selenium-hub selenium/hub

# Node (browser) containers:
docker run -d --net grid -e HUB_HOST=selenium-hub selenium/node-chrome
docker run -d --net grid -e HUB_HOST=selenium-hub selenium/node-firefox
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

Apne test me remote url: \texttt{http://localhost:4444/wd/hub} likho driver setup me.

\subsection*{4. Cloud Selenium Grid Platforms}

\textbf{Why cloud?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Har browser/OS instantly milta hai, no infra headache.
  \item Tests parallel, scalable ho jaate hain (cloud infra, local nahi).
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Popular Platforms:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{BrowserStack:}

  \begin{itemize}
    \item Real browsers/devices, instant access.
    \item Code se direct cloud drivers pe test run.
    \item Advanced debugging — video, logs, screenshots.
    \item CI/CD integration easy.
  \end{itemize}

  \item \textbf{Sauce Labs:}

  \begin{itemize}
    \item Hundreds of browser/OS combos, video recording, advanced reporting.
    \item Secure infra, great community support.
    \item Parallel, scalable runs.
  \end{itemize}

  \item \textbf{LambdaTest:}

  \begin{itemize}
    \item 3000+ environments (desktop/mobile).
    \item [Python, Java, C\#, Robot] sab support.
    \item Local testing tunnel for localhost apps, geolocation, video logs.
    \item Parallel runs, analytics, CI/CD integrations.
  \end{itemize}

\end{itemize}

\textbf{Sample Python code (BrowserStack Remote WebDriver):}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={BrowserStack Remote WebDriver Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium import webdriver

caps = {
    'browser': 'chrome',
    'browser_version': 'latest',
    'os': 'Windows',
    # Add more capabilities per need
}

driver = webdriver.Remote(
    command_executor='https://YOUR_USERNAME:YOUR_ACCESS_KEY@hub-cloud.browserstack.com/wd/hub',
    desired_capabilities=caps
)
driver.get("https://example.com")
print(driver.title)
driver.quit()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{Summary Table}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{|p{4cm}|p{4.5cm}|p{4.5cm}|p{4cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Concept} & \textbf{Why Important} & \textbf{When To Use} & \textbf{Example/Tool} \\
\hline
Cross-Browser (local) & Real user experience, bug catch & UI/feature test har build & Selenium: Chrome/Firefox \\
\hline
Parallel Execution & Time-save, scalable & Badii test suite & pytest-xdist, multiple procs \\
\hline
Selenium Grid & Multi-browser, parallel remote & Team infra, scale needed & Hub+Node infra, Docker \\
\hline
Cloud Selenium & Infra-free, scalable & Release, big team, all OS & BrowserStack, SauceLabs \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\section{Security \& Resiliency Checks — Easy Step-by-Step Guide}

\section*{1. Run UI Tests Behind Login (Authentication Testing)}

\subsubsection*{What Hai Ye?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Bahut websites aur apps me real important features (jaise My Account, Orders, Payments) login karne ke baad hi dikhte hain.
  \item “Behind Login” matlab: pehle user login karta hai, phir hi aage ke pages ya actions automate karne hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why Important Hai?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Agar tum sirf public pages test karoge toh user journey incomplete rahegi.
  \item Login ke baad aane wala content, role-based access, session expiry jaisi cheezein sirf login ke baad hi test ho sakti hain.
  \item Security bugs (jaise unauthorized access) sirf login ke baad detect hoti hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When Use Karna Hai?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Har end-to-end (E2E) test ke liye jab user authentication zaroori ho.
  \item Regression cycles me jab login-protected areas bhi cover karne ho.
  \item Jab administrator ya user-specific features test karne ho.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Agar Na Kiya Toh Kya Hoga?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Bahut bugs production me chhut jayenge.
  \item User experience partial hoga.
  \item Security vulnerabilities unnoticed rahengi.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example (Line-by-line Explanation):}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={UI Login Automation}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium import webdriver
from selenium.webdriver.common.by import By

driver = webdriver.Chrome()              # Browser launch kar rahe hain (Chrome)
driver.get("https://example.com/login") # Login page open kar rahe hain

username_box = driver.find_element(By.ID, "username")  # Username input field locate kar rahe hain (id="username")
username_box.send_keys("myuser")                       # Username input me "myuser" type kar rahe hain

password_box = driver.find_element(By.ID, "password")  # Password input field locate kar rahe hain (id="password")
password_box.send_keys("mypassword")                   # Password input me "mypassword" type kar rahe hain

login_btn = driver.find_element(By.ID, "loginBtn")     # Login button locate kar rahe hain (id="loginBtn")
login_btn.click()                                       # Login button pe click kar rahe hain (form submit hoga)

# Ab yahan se aap logged-in user actions automate kar sakte hain, jaise order place karna, profile edit karna, etc.

driver.quit()                                          # Browser band karte hain
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Step-wise logic:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Browser ko kholda hain aur login page pe jaate hain (driver.get).
  \item Username aur password ke input boxes dhundte hain aur username/password bhejte hain (send\_keys).
  \item Login button ko dhund kar uspe click karte hain (click).
  \item Login successful hone par session create ho jaata hai, tab agla test step chal sakta hai.
\end{itemize}


\section*{2. Basic Vulnerability Checks (e.g., XSS Inputs)}

\subsubsection*{What Hai?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) jaise basic vulnerabilities check karna jisme attacker malicious scripts inject karta hai input fields me.
  \item Automation me commonly use hone wale XSS payloads ko input fields me daalte hain aur check karte hain ki alert box ya script execute ho rahi hai ya nahi.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Developers aksar input sanitization nahi karte, isse security loopholes bante hain.
  \item Automation se cyclic security scans kar ke vulnerabilities jaldi pakad sakte hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When Use Karein?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab bhi release aaye, jab bhi forms ya user inputs change ho rahe ho.
  \item Periodic security audit ke liye CI/CD ke sath.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Agar Na Karein?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Hackers easily app compromise kar sake hain.
  \item Bug bounty aur reputation risk badhega.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Code Example with Explanation:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={XSS Check Automation}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium import webdriver
from selenium.webdriver.common.by import By
import time

xss_payload = "alert('XSS!')"  # Yeh malicious script hai

driver = webdriver.Chrome()
driver.get("https://example.com/contact")       # Contact page open karte hain jahan comment box hai

input_box = driver.find_element(By.NAME, "comment") # Comment input field locate kar rahe hain
input_box.send_keys(xss_payload)                      # Malicious script input me dal rahe hain

input_box.submit()                                    # Form submit kar rahe hain (could also click submit btn)

time.sleep(1)    # Thoda rukna padta hai alert box aane ke liye

try:
    alert = driver.switch_to.alert                  # Browser alert box pe switch karte hain (agar alert aaya hai)
    print("XSS Vulnerable! Alert text:", alert.text) # Alert text print karte hain — matlab vulnerability hai
    alert.accept()                                   # Alert box band kar dete hain
except:
    print("XSS Not Detected.")                       # Alert nahi aya matlab vulnerability nahi mil rahi hai

driver.quit()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Step-wise Logic:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Malicious script text ko input box me daala.
  \item Form submit kara, jisse web app ke input processing hui.
  \item Agar alert box aya, toh matlab XSS vulnerability hai (javascript injection successful).
  \item Agar alert nahi aya toh app properly sanitize kar raha hai input.
\end{itemize}

\section*{3. Integrate OWASP ZAP with Selenium}

\subsubsection*{What Hai?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item OWASP ZAP open source security scanner tool hai jo Selenium tests ke background me realtime vulnerability scan karta hai.
  \item Automated pen-testing jaisa kaam karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Manually security testing karna tedious aur inconsistent hota hai.
  \item Automation ke sath integration se continuous security ensure hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When Use Karein?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Har build ke baad security scan automatic karne ho.
  \item CI/CD pipeline me integrate karna ho.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Agar Na Karein?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Security checks inconsistent rahe.
  \item Manual pen-testing costly hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Basic Setup and Code:}
\begin{enumerate}
    \item Install and run OWASP ZAP locally (default port 8080).
    \item Configure Selenium to use ZAP as a Proxy:
\end{enumerate}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Selenium through ZAP Proxy}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium import webdriver

zap_proxy = "localhost:8080"                      # ZAP proxy URL and port

chrome_options = webdriver.ChromeOptions()        # Chrome options create kar rahe hain
chrome_options.add_argument(f'--proxy-server=http://{zap_proxy}')  # Proxy ko Chrome me set kiya

driver = webdriver.Chrome(options=chrome_options) # Driver ko options ke sath create kiya

driver.get("https://your-app-url.com")            # App URL open kara (saari traffic ZAP ke through jayegi)

# Selenium usual tests run karo...

driver.quit()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Logic:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Browser setup me ZAP ko proxy bana diya.
  \item Selenium browser se jo bhi HTTP/S request hogi, wo ZAP ke through jayegi.
  \item ZAP automatically scan karke vulnerabilities report karega.
\end{itemize}

\section*{4. Secure Credential Management (Using dotenv, Vault)}

\subsubsection*{What Hai?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Credentials (username/password/API keys) directly code me store karna insecure hota hai.
  \item Secure way me environment variables ya encrypted vaults ka use karte hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why Important Hai?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Secrets leak hone se security risk badhta hai.
  \item Best practice hai ki confidential info codebase se alag rakho.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When Use Karein?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Har project me jab credentials ya keys use karna ho, especially public repo ya remote environments me.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Agar Na Karo Toh?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Credentials accidentally expose ho sakti hain.
  \item Security breach ka high risk hai.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Credential Management with dotenv}

\begin{enumerate}
    \item Install:
\end{enumerate}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Install dotenv}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
pip install python-dotenv
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{enumerate}
    \setcounter{enumi}{1}
    \item Create \texttt{.env} file in project root:
\end{enumerate}
\begin{verbatim}
USERNAME=yourusername
PASSWORD=yourpassword
\end{verbatim}

\begin{enumerate}
    \setcounter{enumi}{2}
    \item Use in Python:
\end{enumerate}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Load Credentials in Python}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from dotenv import load_dotenv
import os

load_dotenv()                      # .env file se variables load karo

username = os.getenv("USERNAME")  # Environment se username get karo
password = os.getenv("PASSWORD")  # Password bhi lo

print(f"Username is: {username}")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{enumerate}
    \setcounter{enumi}{3}
    \item Use these variables in Selenium:
\end{enumerate}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Use Secure Vars in Selenium}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
driver.find_element(By.ID, "username").send_keys(username)
driver.find_element(By.ID, "password").send_keys(password)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Vault / Secret Manager (Advanced)}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item HashiCorp Vault jaise tools encrypted secrets store karte hain.
    \item API ya CLI ke zariye secrets ko securely fetch karte hain.
    \item CI/CD pipelines me credentials secure rakhne me help karta hai.
\end{itemize}


\vspace{0.5cm}
\section*{Summary Table}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{|p{4.7cm}|p{4.7cm}|p{3.8cm}|p{4.2cm}|p{4.2cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Why Important} & \textbf{When Use} & \textbf{If Not Used} & \textbf{Example/Tool/Code} \\
\hline
UI Tests Behind Login & Auth flow test karne ke liye zaroori & E2E, regression tests & Risk of missing real bugs & Selenium: login before actions \\
\hline
Basic Vulnerability Checks & Security flaws jaise XSS detect karne & Releases, critical inputs & App vulnerable ho sakta hai & Selenium + XSS payload testing \\
\hline
OWASP ZAP Integration & Automated real-time security testing & Build pipeline, CI/CD & Manual only, inconsistent tests & Selenium + ZAP proxy config \\
\hline
Secure Credential Management & Secrets leak protect karne ke liye & Sab projects jahan keys hain & Leaks \& security risk badhta hai & dotenv, Vault, \texttt{os.getenv} \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
