\section{Mobile Testing with Appium — Full Guide (Beginner to Industry Ready)}

\subsection*{1. Appium Architecture: Kya Hai \& Kyun Important?}

\subsubsection*{What?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Appium ek open-source \textbf{Mobile Automation Tool} hai jo \textbf{Android, iOS apps (native, hybrid, web)} ko automate karne ke liye use hota hai.
  \item Yeh \textbf{Client-Server Architecture} pe kaam karta hai:
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Aapka test script (Python, Java, JS, etc.) ek Client hota hai jo commands bhejta hai Appium Server ko (jo Node.js pe run karta hai).
      \item Server fir OS-specific drivers ko commands forward karta hai — Android ke liye \texttt{UIAutomator2}, iOS ke liye \texttt{XCUITest}.
      \item Fir ye drivers device/emulator/simulator pe user interactions perform karte hain.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Mobile apps ko manual test karna time-consuming aur error-prone hota hai, especially jab baar-baar chhote-chhote changes test karne ho.
  \item Appium se ek hi test script ko Android aur iOS dono par chala sakte hain, \textbf{cross-platform automation} setup ho jaata hai.
  \item Repetitive regression, smoke, E2E testing automate ho jaati hai jo releases fast banata hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab aapko mobile app testing \textbf{automate} karni ho.
  \item Jab regression ya smoke tests bar-bar execute karne ho.
  \item Jab multi-platform coverage (Android + iOS) chahiye.
  \item Continuous Integration (CI/CD) ke part me jab automated mobile tests chalaane ho.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Manual testing slow aur incomplete hoga.
  \item Release cycles lambey ho jayenge.
  \item Bugs easily production me slip ho sakte hain.
  \item Job market ke liye ye skill na hone se aap competition me peeche rah jaoge.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{2. Appium Server Setup — Kaise Start Karen \& Kyun?}

\subsubsection*{What?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Appium server ek bridge hai jo \textbf{client commands ko devices/emulators tak pahunchata hai}.
  \item Server bina chalaye tests device pe nahi chalenge.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Server chalu hona zaroori hai, tabhi automation scripts device ke saath communicate kar payengi.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Har baar Jab automation script chalana ho.
  \item Jab naya device ya emulator add karein.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Scripts connect nahi kar payenge device/emulator se.
  \item Automation fail ho jayegi.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Step-by-Step Setup}

\begin{enumerate}
  \item \textbf{Node.js install karo} (kyunki Appium Node.js pe run karta hai)
\end{enumerate}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Node.js Version Check}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
node -v
npm -v
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{enumerate}
  \setcounter{enumi}{1}
  \item \textbf{Appium global install karo}:
\end{enumerate}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Appium Install}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
npm install -g appium
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{enumerate}
  \setcounter{enumi}{2}
  \item \textbf{Appium server start karo}:
\end{enumerate}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Appium Server Start}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
appium
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Yeh command default port (\texttt{4723}) pe server start kar deta hai.
\end{itemize}

\begin{enumerate}
  \setcounter{enumi}{3}
  \item \textbf{Android setup}:
\end{enumerate}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Android SDK / Android Studio install karo.
  \item \texttt{adb devices} run karke connected devices/emulator ka status check karo.
  \item Env variables set karo (ANDROID\_HOME, PATH).
\end{itemize}

\begin{enumerate}
  \setcounter{enumi}{4}
  \item \textbf{iOS setup (sirf Mac pe)}:
\end{enumerate}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Xcode / Command line tools install karo.
  \item \texttt{instruments} ya XCUITest driver install karo.
  \item USB se device connect karo aur trusted karo.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{3. Writing Appium Tests in Python — Simple Code + Each Line Explained}

\subsubsection*{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Python simple aur easy to learn hai.
  \item Appium official Python client support karta hai.
  \item Ek hi code Android aur iOS pe chal sakta hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item CI/CD ke liye regression runs.
  \item Daily automation.
  \item Cross-platform apps ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Manual testing hoga.
  \item Code duplicate/fixed hoga for each platform.
  \item Error prone \& time-consuming testing.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Step-by-step Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.5pt, sharp corners, title={Appium Python Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import unittest
from appium import webdriver
from appium.webdriver.common.appiumby import AppiumBy

# Device or app capabilities define karna hota hai
capabilities = {
    "platformName": "Android",             # Android ya iOS platform specify karo
    "automationName": "uiautomator2",      # Android automation driver
    "deviceName": "Android Emulator",      # Device ya emulator ka naam
    "appPackage": "com.android.settings",  # App ka Android package name
    "appActivity": ".Settings",             # Starting activity of app
    "language": "en",
    "locale": "US"
}

appium_server_url = "http://localhost:4723"

class TestAppium(unittest.TestCase):
    def setUp(self):
        # Appium server ko connect karke session create karta hai driver object
        self.driver = webdriver.Remote(appium_server_url, capabilities)

    def tearDown(self):
        # Test end me session close kar deta hai
        if self.driver:
            self.driver.quit()

    def test_find_battery(self):
        # Battery option locate karo through XPath aur click karo
        el = self.driver.find_element(by=AppiumBy.XPATH, value='//*[@text="Battery"]')
        el.click()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    unittest.main()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsubsection*{Line-by-Line Explanation:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{capabilities}: Ye dict tell karta hai ki kaunsa platform, device, aur app test hoga.
  \item \texttt{webdriver.Remote}: Appium server se session connect karta hai.
  \item \texttt{setUp()}: Har test case se pehle browser/session init hota hai.
  \item \texttt{tearDown()}: Test ke baad session close hota hai.
  \item \texttt{find\_element(...)}: Mobile app screen ke UI element ko locate karta hai.
  \item \texttt{click()}: Element pe tap karta hai.
  \item \texttt{unittest.main()}: Python test runner hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{4. Emulator vs. Real Device — Kya Farak Hai?}

\begin{tabular}{|p{4cm}|p{5cm}|p{5cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Parameter} & \textbf{Emulator} & \textbf{Real Device} \\
\hline
Cost & Free, software based & Expensive, need to buy/manage hardware \\
\hline
Accuracy & Almost real but kuch hardware features missing & Real world hardware experience \\
\hline
Maintenance & Easy to reset and configure & Device firmware updates, battery etc. \\
\hline
Parallelism & Easy multiple emulators run kar sakte hain & Hardware ki limitation hoti hai \\
\hline
Hardware Features & Limited (sensor emulation, camera limited) & Full hardware access (GPS, camera) \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\vspace{0.3cm}

\textbf{Why do we need both?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Emulator} fast dev/testing ke liye.
  \item \textbf{Real Device} real user conditions ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{When to use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Development aur early regression me emulator.
  \item Final testing, bug reproduction, real feedback ke liye real devices.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Agar na use karein?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Sirf emulator: Real world ke bugs miss kar sakte hain.
  \item Sirf real device: Costly aur testing slow ho sakti hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{5. Cross-Platform Locators (Android / iOS)}

\subsubsection*{Why?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Android aur iOS app UI structure alag hota hai.
  \item Locator strategy bhi platform wise alag ho sakti hai isliye common approach chahiye jo dono me kaam kare.
  \item Locators reliable hone chahiye taaki test stable rahe.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{When?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jab single automation framework dono platforms pe run kar raha ho.
  \item Jab cross-platform code reuse chahiye.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Agar na use karein?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Duplicate code likhna padega har platform ke liye.
  \item Maintenance zyada hoga, cost badhegi.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Common Locator Types}

\begin{tabular}{|p{4cm}|p{6cm}|p{6cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Locator Type} & \textbf{Explanation} & \textbf{Code Example} \\
\hline
\textbf{Accessibility ID} & Cross-platform best locator, content-desc/iOS label & \verb|driver.find_element(AppiumBy.ACCESSIBILITY_ID, "LoginBtn")| \\
\hline
\textbf{ID/Resource-ID (Android)} & Android-specific unique id & \verb|driver.find_element(AppiumBy.ID, "com.app:id/username")| \\
\hline
\textbf{Name (iOS)} & iOS element name / label attribute & \verb|driver.find_element(AppiumBy.NAME, "username")| \\
\hline
\textbf{Class Name} & UI element's class type, platform agnostic & \verb|driver.find_element(AppiumBy.CLASS_NAME, "android.widget.Button")| \\
\hline
\textbf{XPath} & Flexible but slow, last option & \verb|driver.find_element(AppiumBy.XPATH, "//button[@text='Submit']")| \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\subsubsection*{Notes on Flutter / React Native / Kotlin Apps}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Flutter Apps:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Traditional locators work kum ya nahi karte.
      \item Flutter specific plugin \texttt{Flutter Driver} use hota hai, jo Flutter widgets ko identify karta hai.
      \item Appium me bhi Flutter ke custom locators available hain (\texttt{flutter finders}), but thoda complex hota hai.
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{React Native Apps:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Mostly Android/iOS jaisa hi hota hai.
      \item Developers accessibility labels pe dhyan dete hain, taaki app UI testable rahe.
      \item Accessibility IDs ya content-desc use karna best practice hote hain.
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{Kotlin/Java Android Apps:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Usually resource IDs, content-desc, XPath sab normal hi use karte hain.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Summary Table}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{|p{4cm}|p{5cm}|p{5cm}|p{4cm}|p{5cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Why Important} & \textbf{When to Use} & \textbf{If Not Used} & \textbf{Example / Notes} \\
\hline
Appium Architecture & Multi-platform support, client-server & Mobile automation run & Manual testing or partial & Client script → Appium server → device \\
\hline
Appium Server & Connect script \& devices & Every test run & Scripts fail to connect & \texttt{appium} command to start server \\
\hline
Python Appium Tests & Easy scripting and code reuse & E2E, regression, CI & Manual or fragmented code & \texttt{Appium-Python-Client} library \\
\hline
Emulator vs Real Device & Fast dev \& real UX validation & Dev vs final testing & Bugs miss or costly testing & Use both as per stage \\
\hline
Cross-Platform Locators & One code multiple platforms & Cross-platform projects & Duplicate platform code & Accessibility ID, resource-id, xpath \\
\hline
Special Framework Apps & Flutter, React Native need special locators & Mobile frameworks & Locator failures, flaky tests & \texttt{Flutter Driver}, accessibility labels \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\begin{document}

\title{\textbf{\color{sectionblue}Continuous Integration \& Delivery (CI/CD)}}
\author{}
\date{}
\maketitle

\section{Git Integration: Branching \& Version Control for Test Scripts}

\subsection*{What?}
Git ek version control system hai jisme aap apne test automation code ko manage karte ho — history maintain karte ho, different versions banao, changes track karte ho.

\subsection*{Why Important?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Team me ek saath kai log codes pe kaam kar sakte hain without conflict.
  \item Agar galti se kuch big bug aa jaye toh purani stable version pe revert kar sakte hain.
  \item Code changes traceable hote hain, bugs ya issues jaldi identify hote hain.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{When Use?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Jab multiple testers/devs ho.
  \item Jab code regularly update hota ho.
  \item Jab automation ko production ke sath sync rakhna ho.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{If Not Used?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Code duplicates increase honge.
  \item Manual merging errors honge.
  \item Collaboration mushkil hoga.
\end{itemize}

\section{Jenkins}

\subsection*{What?}
Jenkins ek popular open-source \important{Continuous Integration (CI)} tool hai jo automation run karne, code pull karne, tests chalane, reports generate karne, schedule karne ke liye use hota hai.

\subsection*{Why Important?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Tests ko automated banata hai, baar baar bina manual chalaye.
  \item Developers ko continuous feedback milta hai (pass/fail).
  \item Pipelines define karke process automatic banata hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{When Use?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Medium ya bade projects jahan automation bar bar chahiye.
  \item Jenkins server configured ho.
  \item Multiple tools integrate karne ho (SonarQube, Slack, Emails).
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{If Not Used?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Manual testing/process slow hoga.
  \item Test result feedback late milega.
  \item Human error badhega.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Jenkins Pipeline Declarative Example}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Groovy,caption={Jenkinsfile Example - Pipeline}]
pipeline {
    agent any

    stages {
        stage('Checkout') {
            steps {
                git branch: 'main', url: 'https://github.com/yourrepo.git'
            }
        }
        stage('Setup') {
            steps {
                sh 'python -m venv venv'
                sh '. venv/bin/activate && pip install -r requirements.txt'
            }
        }
        stage('Test') {
            steps {
                sh '. venv/bin/activate && pytest --html=report.html --self-contained-html'
            }
            post {
                always {
                    publishHTML([
                        allowMissing: false, 
                        alwaysLinkToLastBuild: true, 
                        keepAll: true, 
                        reportDir: '.', 
                        reportFiles: 'report.html', 
                        reportName: 'PyTest Report'
                    ])
                }
            }
        }
    }

    post {
        always {
            archiveArtifacts artifacts: 'report.html', fingerprint: true
        }
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Explanation:}
\begin{itemize}
  \item \texttt{pipeline \{ agent any \}}: Pipeline kisi bhi available node par run hoga.
  \item \texttt{Checkout}: Git se code pull ho raha hai.
  \item \texttt{Setup}: Virtual env banake dependencies install ho rahe hain.
  \item \texttt{Test}: Pytest report generate karke publish kar raha hai.
  \item \texttt{post}: Report archive ho rahi hai.
\end{itemize}

\section{Schedule Jobs}

Jenkins me “Build periodically” feature se cron syntax specify kar sakte ho, jaise \texttt{0 0 * * *} (har raat 12 baje).

\section{HTML Reports \& Screenshots}

\begin{itemize}
  \item \texttt{pytest-html} se detailed reports banti hain.
  \item Jenkins me \texttt{publishHTML} plugin se integrate hoti hain.
  \item Failures par screenshot bhi reports me attach kar sakte hain.
  \item Logs Jenkins console me realtime dikhte hain.
\end{itemize}

\section{GitHub Actions}

\subsection*{What?}  
GitHub Actions ek cloud-based CI/CD service hai, GitHub ke liye, jisme automation workflows likhe jate hain YAML me.

\subsection*{Why?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Fully cloud hosted, zero infra maintenance.
  \item GitHub repo se direct integrate hota hai.
  \item YAML workflows se flexible automation.
  \item Multiplatform runners with parallelism.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{When?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Repo GitHub pe ho.
  \item Cloud based CI chahiye.
  \item Multiplatform testing.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{If Not Used?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Infra khud maintain karna hoga.
  \item Scale aur speed limited ho sakti hai.
  \item Cloud benefits miss honge.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{GitHub Actions YAML}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=YAML,caption={GitHub Actions Workflow}]
name: Python CI

on:
  push:
    branches: [ main ]
  pull_request:
    branches: [ main ]

jobs:
  build:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
    - uses: actions/checkout@v3
    - name: Setup Python
      uses: actions/setup-python@v4
      with:
        python-version: 3.10
    - name: Install dependencies
      run: |
        python -m venv venv
        source venv/bin/activate
        pip install -r requirements.txt
    - name: Run Tests
      run: |
        source venv/bin/activate
        pytest --html=report.html --self-contained-html
    - name: Upload Report
      uses: actions/upload-artifact@v3
      with:
        name: test-report
        path: report.html
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Explanation:}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Triggers on push and PR to main branch.
  \item Runs on Ubuntu latest.
  \item Checks out code, sets python, installs deps.
  \item Runs tests and generates HTML report.
  \item Uploads report as artifact.
\end{itemize}

\section{Trigger on Push / PR / Merge}

CI runs test automatically on code push or PR events to catch errors early.

\section{Slack / Email Notifications}

\subsection*{Slack Setup in Jenkins}

\begin{itemize}
  \item Install Slack plugin.
  \item Create Slack app, get webhook URL.
  \item Configure URL in Jenkins settings.
\end{itemize}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=Groovy]
post {
    failure {
        slackSend(color: 'danger', message: "Build failed: ${env.JOB_NAME} ${env.BUILD_NUMBER}")
    }
    success {
        slackSend(color: 'good', message: "Build success: ${env.JOB_NAME} ${env.BUILD_NUMBER}")
    }
}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Slack Setup in GitHub Actions}

\begin{lstlisting}[language=YAML]
- name: Slack Notification
  uses: 8398a7/action-slack@v3
  with:
    status: ${{ job.status }}
    fields: repo, commit, author
  env:
    SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL: ${{ secrets.SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL }}
\end{lstlisting}

\subsection*{Email Notifications}

Jenkins Email-ext plugin se email configure kar sakte hain. Customize templates and notify team instantly on failures.

\section*{Summary Table}

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{ |p{3.3cm}|p{3.8cm}|p{3.8cm}|p{4cm}| }
\hline
\textbf{Feature} & \textbf{Why Important} & \textbf{When Use} & \textbf{Example / Tool} \\
\hline
Git Integration & Collaboration, version control & Team projects & Git \\
Jenkins & Automated CI, pipelines & Medium to large projects & Jenkins \\
Scheduled Jobs & Regular runs, regression & Nightly / periodic jobs & Jenkins cron \\
HTML Reports & Friendly, detailed results & Reporting & pytest-html, Jenkins plugins \\
GitHub Actions & Cloud CI/CD, easy setup & GitHub hosted repos & GitHub Actions \\
Notifications & Faster feedback & Failures and successes & Slack, Email \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\begin{document}

\section{Real-World End-to-End Projects in Selenium with Python}

\subsection*{Project 1: E-Commerce Website Testing}

\paragraph{Features covered:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item User login
  \item Product search \& filtering
  \item Add products to cart
  \item Checkout process (payment simulation)
  \item Data-driven order placements
  \item Reports generation for orders \& test results
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Why important?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item E-commerce sites real-world me bahut complex hote hain.
  \item End-to-end (E2E) tests user journey ka real scenario replicate karte hain.
  \item Bugs yahan destination tak pahuchte hain, toh testing strict honi chahiye.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{When use karo?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Release se pehle full regression karni ho.
  \item Payment, cart functionality regularly check karni ho.
  \item Multi-user, multi-data scenario validate karna ho.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Basic Approach \& Examples}

\paragraph{POM Design}

Har page ko alag class banayenge:

\begin{tabular}{|p{3.5cm}|p{8cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Page} & \textbf{Features / Actions} \\
\hline
LoginPage & \texttt{enter\_username()}, \texttt{enter\_password()}, \texttt{click\_login()} \\
HomePage & \texttt{search\_product()}, \texttt{apply\_filter()}, \texttt{open\_product()} \\
ProductPage & \texttt{add\_to\_cart()}, \texttt{select\_quantity()} \\
CartPage & \texttt{verify\_cart\_items()}, \texttt{proceed\_to\_checkout()} \\
CheckoutPage & \texttt{fill\_address\_details()}, \texttt{select\_payment()}, \texttt{place\_order()} \\
OrderConfirmationPage & \texttt{verify\_order\_success()}, \texttt{get\_order\_id()} \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\paragraph{Data-Driven Orders}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Excel/CSV me products details, user info ready rakhoge.
  \item \texttt{pytest.mark.parametrize} ya external data provider se data fetch karke test chalaoge.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Sample Code Snippet (LoginPage as Example)}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={LoginPage Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver.common.by import By

class LoginPage:
    def __init__(self, driver):
        self.driver = driver
        self.username_input = (By.ID, "username")
        self.password_input = (By.ID, "password")
        self.login_button = (By.ID, "loginBtn")

    def enter_username(self, username):
        self.driver.find_element(*self.username_input).send_keys(username)

    def enter_password(self, password):
        self.driver.find_element(*self.password_input).send_keys(password)

    def click_login(self):
        self.driver.find_element(*self.login_button).click()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsubsection*{Test Example with Data-Driven}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Data-Driven Login Test}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import pytest

@pytest.mark.parametrize("username, password", [
    ("user1", "pass1"),
    ("user2", "pass2")
])
def test_login(driver, username, password):
    login_page = LoginPage(driver)
    login_page.enter_username(username)
    login_page.enter_password(password)
    login_page.click_login()
    # Assert dashboard visible, etc
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\paragraph{CI/CD Integration}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Jenkins/GitHub Actions me run karoge.
  \item PyTest-html ya Allure se report generate.
  \item Jenkins me HTML report publish karo aur Slack notify karo.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\subsection*{Project 2: HR Portal or CMS Testing}

\paragraph{Features covered:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Form submissions (employee registration, leave requests)
  \item File uploads (CV uploads, document attachments)
  \item Approval workflows (manager approval buttons, status changes)
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Why important?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Business-critical workflows hain jo manually bohot time lete hain.
  \item Automated testing se error-free, fast workflow validation.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{When use karo?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Release ke baad ya changes ke baad validate karo.
  \item Automation regression part banana ho.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Automation Approach}

\paragraph{POM Classes}

\begin{tabular}{|p{3.5cm}|p{8cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Page} & \textbf{Actions} \\
\hline
LoginPage & Same as Project 1 \\
EmployeeFormPage & \texttt{fill\_form(data)}, \texttt{upload\_documents(path)} \\
ApprovalPage & \texttt{approve\_request()}, \texttt{reject\_request()} \\
DashboardPage & \texttt{check\_request\_status()}, \texttt{filter\_requests()} \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\paragraph{File Upload Example}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={File Upload Method}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
def upload_document(self, file_path):
    upload_element = self.driver.find_element(By.ID, "fileUpload")
    upload_element.send_keys(file_path)  # File path absolute hona chahiye
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\paragraph{Additional Notes:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Waits and synchronization important hai – workflow me buttons/dynamic elements pe action karne se pehle visible and clickable hone ka wait lagao.
  \item Report generation and logs – process ke steps ka logging karna useful hota hai workflows me.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Project 3: Regression Test Suite}

\paragraph{Features Covered:}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Comprehensive test suite for core features
  \item Built using POM + PyTest for modularity and maintainability
  \item Reports (pytest-html/allure) and CI/CD integration for continuous testing
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Why important?}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Regression testing every build me mandatory hai taaki naye changes purane features break na karein.
  \item Automated and maintainable test suite efficient delivery ke liye zaroori.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Structure \& Best Practices}

\begin{verbatim}
project_root/
├── pages/              # POM classes
│    ├── login_page.py
│    ├── home_page.py
│    └── cart_page.py
├── tests/              # PyTest test cases
│    ├── test_login.py
│    ├── test_cart.py
│    └── test_checkout.py
├── utils/              # Waits, logging, reports helpers
├── data/               # Excel/CSV/JSON test data files
├── reports/            # Generated reports folder
├── conftest.py         # PyTest fixtures (setup/teardown)
├── requirements.txt
└── pytest.ini          # PyTest configurations
\end{verbatim}

\paragraph{Running All Tests}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg,colframe=black!20,boxrule=0.5pt,sharp corners,title={Run Entire Suite}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=bash]
pytest --html=reports/report.html --self-contained-html
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\paragraph{CI/CD Pipeline}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item GitHub Actions/Jenkins to pull, setup env, install dependencies, run tests and publish reports.
  \item Slack/Email notifications configured for test status alerts.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Code Reusability}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item BasePage and Utility classes for common actions (waiting for elements, logging, screenshot on failure) use karo.
  \item Fixtures me driver setup/teardown properly handle karo.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Final Tips}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Real-world projects me modularity, reusability, maintainability sabse important hai.
  \item Test data ko alag rakho (Excel/CSV/JSON).
  \item Logs/reports pe focus karo for easy debugging.
  \item CI/CD integration nahi bhoolo — automation ka future wahi hai!
\end{itemize}

\begin{document}

\section*{Advanced \& Job-Oriented Topics in Automation Testing}

\subsection*{1. Test Tagging \& Suite Management}

\concept{Why Important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Bahut saare tests hote hain, sabko ek saath chalana efficient nahi hota.
    \item Tagging se tests categorize kar sakte hain (smoke, regression, sanity, critical etc).
    \item Easily required tests ko run karo based on tag without changing code.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When to Use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Jab test suite bada ho.
    \item CI/CD pipelines mein selective test execution ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\concept{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Testing slow ho jata hai.
    \item Troubleshooting mushkil hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[title=Pytest Tagging Example,colback=codebg,colframe=black!20]
\begin{lstlisting}[style=pythonstyle]
import pytest

@pytest.mark.smoke
def test_login():
    assert True

@pytest.mark.regression
def test_checkout():
    assert True
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Run smoke tests only:}

\begin{lstlisting}[style=bashstyle]
pytest -m smoke
\end{lstlisting}

\vspace{5pt}

\subsection*{2. Test Retry Mechanism}

\concept{Why Important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Kabhi kabhi flaky tests network/dynamic content ki wajah se fail hotey hain.
    \item Retry se flaky failures reduce hote hain aur stable results milte hain.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When to Use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Flaky tests ya unstable environments me.
\end{itemize}

\concept{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item CI/CD me false negatives aate hain.
    \item Time waste hota hai failures ko repeat karne me.
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[title=Pytest Retry Plugin,colback=codebg,colframe=black!20]
\begin{lstlisting}[style=bashstyle]
pip install pytest-rerunfailures

pytest --reruns 2
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:} Failed test ko max 2 baar automatically retry karega.

\vspace{5pt}

\subsection*{3. Flaky Test Resolution}

\concept{Why Important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Flaky tests confidence kam karte hain; automation ka fayda kam hota hai.
    \item Root cause identify karna zaroori hai.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When to Use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Jab test results unpredictable ho.
\end{itemize}

\concept{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Developers ignore karte hain flaky failures ko.
    \item Bugs slip ho sakte hain into production.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Common Strategies:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Use explicit waits (`WebDriverWait`) instead of static sleeps.
    \item Use stable locators avoid karna chahiye dynamic XPaths.
    \item Test isolation and data parameterization.
    \item Manage parallel execution carefully.
    \item Use retries cautiously.
\end{itemize}

\vspace{5pt}

\subsection*{4. Locator Auto-Healing Techniques}

\concept{Why Important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item UI changes hone pe hardcoded locators break ho jate hain.
    \item Auto-healing se test khud alternate locators try karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When to Use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Large / dynamic UI projects jahaan frequent UI changes hote hain.
\end{itemize}

\concept{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Tests frequently fail honge.
    \item Maintenance zyada ho jayega.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Common Approaches:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Store multiple locators for an element with fallback logic.
    \item Use AI-powered tools (Mabl, Testim).
    \item Wrap element finding in custom functions.
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[title=Basic Auto-Healing Function,colback=codebg,colframe=black!20]
\begin{lstlisting}[style=pythonstyle]
def find_element(driver, locators):
    for locator in locators:
        try:
            element = driver.find_element(*locator)
            return element
        except:
            continue
    raise Exception("Element not found using any locator")
    
# Usage:
locators = [
    (By.ID, "submitBtn"),
    (By.XPATH, "//button[text()='Submit']"),
    (By.CSS_SELECTOR, "button.submit")
]

element = find_element(driver, locators)
element.click()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{5pt}

\subsection*{5. Code Reviews \& Pull Requests}

\concept{Why Important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Code quality improve hoti hai.
    \item Bugs early detect hote hain.
    \item Team knowledge sharing badhata hai.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When to Use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Har commit ke liye, specially large teams / projects me.
\end{itemize}

\concept{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Bad coding practices spread ho sakti hain.
    \item Code duplication aur inconsistencies badhen.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Best Practices:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Regular peer review karo.
    \item Code styling (PEP8) maintain karo.
    \item Meaningful comments aur docs likho.
    \item Unit & integration tests include karo.
\end{itemize}

\vspace{5pt}

\subsection*{6. Creating Reusable Libraries}

\concept{Why Important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Code reuse badhata hai.
    \item DRY principle follow hota hai.
    \item Maintenance easy hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When to Use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Jab multiple tests me common functionalities ho.
\end{itemize}

\concept{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Code duplication,
    \item Changes multiple jagah karne ki need.
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[title=Utility Function Example,colback=codebg,colframe=black!20]
\begin{lstlisting}[style=pythonstyle]
def login(driver, username, password):
    driver.find_element(By.ID, "username").send_keys(username)
    driver.find_element(By.ID, "password").send_keys(password)
    driver.find_element(By.ID, "loginBtn").click()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

Use is function ko multiple scripts me import kar ke.

\vspace{5pt}

\subsection*{7. Test Strategy Document Preparation}

\concept{Why Important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Stakeholders ko roadmap deta hai.
    \item Scope, objectives, resources define karta hai.
    \item Quality metrics aur risk management specify karta hai.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When to Use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Project start me.
    \item Client approval ke liye.
\end{itemize}

\concept{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Confusion in scope and expectations.
    \item Poor resource/time management.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Typical Sections:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Scope \& Objectives
    \item Tools \& Frameworks
    \item Test Types \& Coverage
    \item Test Data \& Environments
    \item Deliverables \& Reporting
    \item Risks \& Mitigation
    \item Timeline \& Milestones
\end{itemize}

\vspace{5pt}

\subsection*{8. Writing Test Cases for Automation Coverage}

\concept{Why Important?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Without well-written test cases automation adhura hai.
    \item Coverage ensures important scenarios are tested.
\end{itemize}

\concept{When to Use?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Before and during automation implementation.
\end{itemize}

\concept{If Not Used?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Important test scenarios miss ho jayengi.
    \item Coverage poor; bugs undetected rahenge.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Tips:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Clear objectives likho.
    \item Input data specify karo.
    \item Expected outcome clearly mention karo.
    \item Preconditions \& postconditions include karo.
    \item Make test cases reusable and parameterized.
\end{itemize}

\vspace{5pt}

\begin{tabular}{|l|p{8cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Test Case ID} & TC001 \\
\hline
\textbf{Description} & Verify login with valid user \\
\hline
\textbf{Steps} & 1. Open Login Page \newline 2. Enter valid username \newline 3. Enter valid password \newline 4. Click Login \\
\hline
\textbf{Expected Result} & User should be redirected to Dashboard Page \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\vspace{10pt}

\subsection*{Summary Table: Advanced Topics}

\begin{tabular}{|p{4cm}|p{6cm}|p{5cm}|p{5cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Topic} & \textbf{Why Important} & \textbf{When To Use} & \textbf{Typical Approach or Tool} \\
\hline
Test Tagging \& Suite Management & Efficient selective execution & For large suites and CI/CD & Pytest markers \\
\hline
Test Retry Mechanism & Reduce flaky failures & For unstable tests & pytest-rerunfailures \\
\hline
Flaky Test Resolution & Stability and confidence & For flaky & Better locators, waits, isolation \\
\hline
Locator Auto-Healing & Reduce test breaks due to UI changes & Frequent UI churn & Multiple locators, AI tools \\
\hline
Code Reviews \& PRs & Code quality, bug catching & Every commit & Peer reviews, style guides \\
\hline
Reusable Libraries & Speed, maintainability & Multiple test reuse & Utility functions, helpers \\
\hline
Test Strategy Document & Roadmap clarity & Project start & Word doc, Confluence \\
\hline
Writing Test Cases & Coverage & Before/during automation & Clear steps, expectations \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\begin{document}

\title{\textbf{\color{sectionblue}Job Interview Preparation for Selenium + Python Automation Roles}}
\author{}
\date{}
\maketitle

\section{Selenium \& Python Theory Questions}

\concept{Why?} Theory se pata chalta hai tumhari basic understanding kitni strong hai. Interview me basic questions zarur poochte hain to assess foundation.

\subsection*{Common Topics and Sample Questions}

\begin{tabular}{|p{4cm}|p{7cm}|p{5cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Topic} & \textbf{Sample Questions} & \textbf{Tips \& Important Points}\\
\hline
Selenium WebDriver Basics & \textit{WebDriver kya hai? WebDriver vs Selenium RC?} & WebDriver new, RC deprecated; WebDriver browser control karta hai. \\
\hline
Locators & \textit{XPath vs CSS selectors, dynamic locators kaise handle karte?} & Always prefer stable and fast locators. Use \texttt{contains()}, \texttt{starts-with()} for dynamic elements. \\
\hline
Waits & \textit{Implicit vs Explicit waits, fluent wait kya hota hai?} & Explicit wait most reliable, avoid mixing implicit and explicit. \\
\hline
Selenium Architecture & \textit{Selenium suite ke components (IDE, WebDriver, Grid)?} & Grid for parallel \& remote; IDE mostly deprecated. \\
\hline
Python Scripting Basics & \textit{List, dict, classes, decorators basics} & Useful for writing clean automation code. \\
\hline
Exception Handling & \textit{Selenium ki common exceptions (NoSuchElement, Timeout)?} & Use try-except blocks, explicit waits preempt errors. \\
\hline
Handling Popups/Frames & \textit{Alert handling, iframe switch kaise karte?} & \texttt{switch\_to.alert}, \texttt{switch\_to.frame} usage. \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\section{Debugging \& Optimization Questions}

\concept{Why?} Debugging skill test hoti hai ki tum errors kaise trace karte ho, flaky tests ko kaise fix karte ho.

\subsection*{Common Scenarios and Approaches}

\begin{tabular}{|p{5cm}|p{8cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Problem} & \textbf{Approach to Debug \& Optimize} \\
\hline
ElementNotVisible or StaleElementRef & Use explicit waits, avoid caching elements for long time \\
\hline
Flaky Tests & Add retries, use fluent waits, stabilize locators \\
\hline
Slow Test Execution & Parallel execution (pytest-xdist), selective tests run \\
\hline
Memory leaks/Driver leaks & Proper \texttt{driver.quit()}, avoid multiple driver instances \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\section{Practical Scenarios}

\subsection*{Locators}

\textbf{Example Question:} Agar xpath dynamic hai, handle kaise karoge?\\
\textbf{Best Answer:} Use \texttt{contains()}, \texttt{starts-with()}, or better stable attributes like accessibility-id, aria-labels.

\subsection*{Waits}

\textbf{Example:} Implicit vs explicit wait kab use karoge? Agar dono mix kiye toh kya hoga?\\
\textbf{Answer:} Explicit waits targeted elements ke liye sabse best hain. Dono mix karna risk hai flaky tests ka.

\subsection*{POM Questions}

\textbf{Example:} POM kya hai? Advantages kya hain? Kaise implement karte ho?\\
\textbf{Answer:} POM ek design pattern hai jisme har page ka ek class banta hai with locators \& actions, jis se reusability \& maintainability badhta hai.

\section{Git, Jenkins, Docker, API Knowledge for Automation Roles}

\subsection*{Git}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Branching basics, merging, resolving conflicts.
  \item Using branch strategies (feature, develop, main).
  \item Setup \texttt{.gitignore} for test artifacts.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Jenkins}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Pipeline setup basics.
  \item Scheduling jobs and triggering on Git commit.
  \item Archiving reports and sending notifications.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Docker}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Containerize automation environment.
  \item Use Selenium Grid with Docker for scalable parallel test execution.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{REST API Basics}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Testing APIs using \texttt{requests} module.
  \item Validate status codes, response contents in tests.
  \item Integrate API calls into automation flows.
\end{itemize}

\section{System Design for Automation Frameworks}

\concept{Important Concepts}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Modular, scalable architecture (POM + Utilities + Data Driven + Reports).
  \item Parallelism \& grid/distributed testing.
  \item CI/CD integration pipeline.
  \item Test data source management.
  \item Error handling \& retry mechanisms.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Prepare to Explain}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Folder structure.
  \item How fixtures manage setup/teardown.
  \item How test suites are grouped and executed selectively.
  \item Reporting and logging approach.
\end{itemize}

\section{Assignment-Level Projects from Companies}

\concept{Common Requirements}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Login + CRUD operations automation.
  \item Data-driven scenarios with multiple datasets.
  \item Reporting + screenshots + CI pipeline.
  \item Clean, commented, maintainable code.
\end{itemize}

\concept{Best Practice}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Use POM + PyTest.
  \item Write meaningful asserts and error messages.
  \item Handle dynamic elements patiently.
  \item Automate environment setup using Docker if possible.
\end{itemize}

\section{Bonus Tools to Learn (Job-Ready Plus)}

\begin{tabular}{|p{4cm}|p{6cm}|p{5cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Tool} & \textbf{Purpose} & \textbf{Why Important} \\
\hline
requests & REST API testing & API validation integral part of modern automation \\
openpyxl, pandas & Excel automation & Data-driven testing, test data handling \\
faker & Test data generation & Generate realistic random test data \\
pytest-xdist & Parallel test execution & Speed up test runs \\
allure-pytest & Beautiful test reports & Interactive, shareable reports \\
dotenv & Secure credentials storage & Avoid hardcoding secrets \\
SelectorHub, ChroPath & XPath/CSS locator generation & Fast, error-free locator creation \\
Selenoid, Zalenium & Scalable Grid + video recording & Parallel \& remote cross-browser testing \\
Docker & Containerized test environments & Consistent environment setup \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\section*{You Are Job-Ready If You Can:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Selenium WebDriver APIs deeply samjho, confidently use karo.
  \item POM + PyTest framework effectively banake run kar sakte ho.
  \item Dynamic elements, waits, popups, frames handle properly karte ho.
  \item Readable, maintainable aur reusable test code likh sakte ho.
  \item Cross-browser tests automate karke CI/CD pipeline me integrate kar chuke ho.
  \item Automation reports generate kar sakte ho (pytest-html, allure).
  \item Flaky tests ko identify aur fix karte ho.
  \item Real data se test karte ho aur multiple user journeys automate karte ho.
\end{itemize}

\section*{Extra Tips for Interview Preparation}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Real-life project examples ready rakho (GitHub repo links preferred).
  \item Code ko samjho, har function ka kya kaam hai clarity rakho.
  \item Python basics (data types, functions, OOP) thoda revise karo.
  \item Practice debugging with real Selenium errors.
  \item Mock interview questions focus on scenario-based answers.
\end{itemize}

\lstdefinelanguage{CustomPython}{
  language=Python,
  basicstyle=\ttfamily\footnotesize,
  keywordstyle=\color{keywordblue}\bfseries,
  stringstyle=\color{stringred},
  commentstyle=\color{commentgreen}\itshape,
  morecomment=[l][\color{commentgreen}\itshape]{\#},
  breaklines=true,
  backgroundcolor=\color{codebg},
  frame=single,
  framerule=0.5pt,

  showstringspaces=false,
}

\begin{document}

\title{\textbf{\color{sectionblue}Most Helpful Plugins \& Tools for Selenium + Python Automation}}
\author{}
\date{}
\maketitle

\section{SelectorHub (Browser XPath/CSS Tool)}

\textbf{What?}

- SelectorHub ek Chrome/Firefox extension hai jo \textbf{XPath aur CSS selectors} automatically aur accurately generate karta hai for any web element[1].

\textbf{Why use karein?}

- XPath/CSS locator banana manual process mein galtiyan hoti hain – especially dynamic, lengthy, ya complex DOM structure me.
- SelectorHub real-time valid selectors suggest karta hai, aur verify bhi karta hai ki selector unique hai ya nahi.

\textbf{When to use karein?}
- Jab new locator banana ho, ya dynamic element ke liye alternate locator chahiye ho.
- Jab manually XPath likhna error-prone ho raha ho.

\textbf{If not used toh kya problem?}
- Locators galat ho sakte hain, automation script frequently break hogi.
- Development/debugging time badh jayega.

\textbf{How to Install/Use:}
\begin{enumerate}
    \item Chrome/Edge/Firefox browser mein jao, \textbf{SelectorHub extension} search karo.
    \item Install karlo (official store, trusted source only).
    \item Kisi bhi web page pe jao, right click $\rightarrow$ Inspect (DevTools open).
    \item SelectorHub tab dikh raha ho to use open karo. Koi web element select karo $\rightarrow$ aapko recommended XPath/CSS mil jayega.
    \item Copy-paste selector code in your Selenium scripts.
\end{enumerate}

\section{ChroPath (XPath/CSS Finder)}

\textbf{What?}
- ChroPath ek aur popular Chrome extension hai for generating and validating XPath, CSS Selector, Absolute XPath, etc.

\textbf{Why use karein?}
- Difficult-to-locate elements me instant/helpful selector bana deta hai.
- Auto-suggests selectors and allows one-click copy.

\textbf{When to use karein?}
- Jab complex forms, tables, popups, iframes handle kar rahe ho.
 
\textbf{If not used toh?}
- Galat selector se flaky/unreliable tests ban jayenge.

\textbf{How to Install/Use:}

- Similar to SelectorHub: Extension install karo, DOM pe element select karo, recommended locator copy karo.

\section{Axe DevTools (Accessibility Testing Plugin)}

\textbf{What?}
- Chrome/Firefox extension for \textbf{automated accessibility audits} using axe-core engine.

\textbf{Why use karein?}
- WCAG/ARIA/accessibility guidelines ki violations easily detect ho jaati hain—manual a11y testing tedious ho sakta hai.
  
\textbf{When to use karein?}
- Jab aapko a11y compliance (legal ya usability reason se) ensure karna ho.

\textbf{If not used toh?}
- Visually impaired users ko app accessible nahi rahega; legal/compliance risks ho sakte hain.

\textbf{How to Install/Use:}
\begin{enumerate}
    \item Install Axe DevTools extension.
    \item Target web page open karo, DevTools $\rightarrow$ Axe tab pe click karo.
    \item "Analyze" button dabao—report mil jayega.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Testim or Mabl (AI-Based Locator Auto-Healing Tools - Advanced/Optional)}

\textbf{What?}
- Cloud-based tools jo \textbf{AI se locator break hone pe auto-heal/auto-suggest} alternative selectors dete hain and reduce script maintenance.
- Selenium/Python ecosystem me optional, advanced team ke liye.

\textbf{Why use karein?}
- UI change hone pe scripts bar-bar break hoti hain; auto-healing maintainability improve karta hai.

\textbf{When to use?}
- Large scale projects, rapidly changing frontends.
  
\textbf{If not used?}
- Manual locator update/maintenance frequently required.

\textbf{How to Use:}
- Testim/Mabl ka trial setup karo, Selenium integration steps follow karo. AI-based healing tabhi useful hai jab UI fragile ho.

\section{Allure Commandline \& Pytest-HTML (Reporting Plugins)}

\textbf{What?}
- \textbf{Allure}: Rich, beautiful reporting dashboard.
- \textbf{pytest-html}: Simple HTML report plugin for pytest.

\textbf{Why use karein?}
- Pass/fail, screenshots, logs, steps—all kuch visual format me share kar sakte ho team/clients ke saath.
 
\textbf{When to use?}
- Automated reporting after every run, CI/CD integration.

\textbf{If not used toh?}
- Output sirf console me yaa low-detail HTML; traceability poor; sharing difficult.

\textbf{How to Install/Use:}
\begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{pip install allure-pytest pytest-html}
    \item Pytest run karte waqt:  
        \texttt{pytest --html=report.html --self-contained-html}  
        \texttt{pytest --alluredir=allure-results} (then Allure serve command)
    \item For Allure dashboard, Java Allure do install and use \texttt{allure serve allure-results}.
\end{itemize}

\section{Requests Interceptor (Network API Monitoring Plugin)}

\textbf{What?}
- Chrome extension jo \textbf{network requests capture, modify, analyze} karne me madad karta hai.

\textbf{Why/When to use?}
- UI + API combined automation ya API endpoint debugging ke liye helpful hai.
- Network failures, broken API ya security vulnerability quickly detect karte hain.

\textbf{How to Use:}
- Install "Request Interceptor" extension, page reload karo, all HTTP(s) requests analyze karo.

\section{Fake Data Generator Plugins (e.g., Fake Filler)}

\textbf{What?}
- \textbf{Fake Filler} Chrome extension: Instantly form fields me random but realistic data fill karta hai.

\textbf{Why?}
- Data-driven test aur regression me form input fill karne ka time bachaata hai.

\textbf{If not used?}
- Test dev slow, manual typing repetitive actions.

\section{Other Useful Tools Quick List}

\begin{tabular}{|p{3.6cm}|p{7.3cm}|p{7.4cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Tool/Plugin} & \textbf{What/Why/When} & \textbf{Install/Use Steps} \\
\hline
Postman & API endpoint rapid testing \& automation & Download app, import/export collections \\
\hline
BrowserStack Local & Cloud device/browser testing & Install CLI agent, connect with Selenium \\
\hline
Jenkins GitHub Plugins & CI/CD triggers, notifications, status checks & Jenkins manage plugins, GitHub Actions setup \\
\hline
Python dotenv & Secure credentials/env variable manage & \texttt{pip install python-dotenv}, use \texttt{.env} files \\
\hline
Visual Studio Code Plugins & Python, Selenium, Pylance, Allure Test Reporters & Install via VSCode marketplace \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\section{FAQs / Common Interview Tasks}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item \textbf{SelectorHub ya ChroPath interview me kaise explain karo?}

    Bol sakte ho — “I use SelectorHub/ChroPath for robust XPath/CSS creation and validation. It saves time and reduces flaky test script failures by generating accurate locators, especially in dynamic web apps.”

    \item \textbf{Allure/pytest-html reporting zaruri hai?} 

    Industry me test traceability, CI/CD integration and result sharing ke liye reporting plugin essential hai.

    \item \textbf{Accessibility plugin a11y compliance ke liye kaise integrate karo?} 

    Manual and automated audit dono aap Axe DevTools/axe-core JS based automation se integrate kar sakte ho.
\end{itemize}

\section{Final Golden Rules}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
    \item Har automation setup me \textbf{minimum SelectorHub/ChroPath, Allure/pytest-html, and Axe DevTools} install rakho.
    \item Plugins/Extensions properly trusted source se install karo.
    \item Plugins sirf debugging/locator/rapid form filling/reports/analysis ke liye hi use karo—core test logic hamesha apne codebase me likho.
\end{itemize}

\begin{document}

\title{\textbf{\color{sectionblue}Web \& Mobile Element Locators in Selenium \& Appium: Beginner to Job-Ready Guide}}
\author{}
\date{}
\maketitle

\section{1. Web Element Locators in Selenium (For Beginners)}

\subsection*{A. Basic Types of Locators}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{ID:} Unique page element identity.
  \item \textbf{Name:} Form fields mein jyada use hota hai.
  \item \textbf{Class Name:} CSS class values (multiple elements ho sakte hain).
  \item \textbf{Tag Name:} E.g., input, div, button.
  \item \textbf{Link Text:} Anchor (\texttt{<a>}) text.
  \item \textbf{Partial Link Text:} Anchor text ka partial match.
  \item \textbf{XPath:} Powerful, custom locator (even complex elements).
  \item \textbf{CSS Selector:} CSS-based matching, fast \& flexible.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{B. Locators Collect Karne Ka Step by Step Tarika (Chrome Example)}

\subsubsection*{1. Manual Inspection (Without Plugin)}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Website kholo} (target page).
  \item \textbf{Right click element} $\to$ ``Inspect'' (Chrome DevTools open hoga).
  \item DevTools mein highlighted line pe hover karo:
  \begin{itemize}
    \item \textbf{ID} present hai? E.g., \texttt{<button id="submit">} $\to$ Use \texttt{By.ID}
    \item \textbf{Class}? E.g., \texttt{<button class="main-btn">} $\to$ Use \texttt{By.CLASS\_NAME} (agar class unique ho)
    \item \textbf{Name}? E.g., \texttt{<input name="user">}
    \item \textbf{Tag}? E.g., use \texttt{By.TAG\_NAME('button')}
    \item \textbf{XPath/CSS}: Right click element in DevTools $\to$ ``Copy'' $\to$ Select ``Copy XPath'' or ``Copy selector''
  \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{Paste karo value apne Selenium script me}.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Python Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Basic Selenium Locators Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium import webdriver
from selenium.webdriver.common.by import By

driver = webdriver.Chrome()
driver.get("https://example.com")

element = driver.find_element(By.ID, "submit")            # For ID
element = driver.find_element(By.CLASS_NAME, "main-btn")  # For class name
element = driver.find_element(By.XPATH, "//button[@id='submit']")  # For XPath
element = driver.find_element(By.CSS_SELECTOR, ".main-btn")        # For CSS Selector
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{C. Auto-Generate Locators Using Plugins (Recommended for Beginners)}

\subsubsection*{1. SelectorHub Extension (Best Plugin)}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Chrome/Edge/Firefox webstore pe jao, search ``SelectorHub''.
  \item \textbf{Install} karo extension.
  \item Target page kholo, \textbf{right click} $\to$ ``Inspect''.
  \item \textbf{SelectorHub tab select karo}, ab koi web element pe click ya hover karo.
  \item Tumhe \textbf{auto-generated XPath, CSS Selector} aur unka validity status milega.
  \item \textbf{Copy karo} directly from SelectorHub panel and use in Selenium code.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{2. ChroPath (Alternative Plugin)}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Same process as above.
  \item ``ChroPath'' bhi install kar sakte ho from Chrome Web Store.
  \item DevTools me ChroPath tab pe element select karte hi locator mil jayega.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{3. Fake Filler (For Form Testing)}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Chrome/Firefox extension ``Fake Filler'' install karo.
  \item Login/signup form kholke, extension click karo—\textbf{form sare fields auto-fill} ho jayenge.
  \item Isse rapid test data entry possible hai, time bachaata hai.
\end{itemize}

\newpage
\section{2. Mobile Elements in Appium (App Testing with Python)}

\subsection*{A. Locators in Mobile Automation (Appium ke liye)}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{resource-id:} Similar to \texttt{id} in web.
  \item \textbf{accessibility id:} User-accessibility label.
  \item \textbf{class name:} Android/iOS UI widget ka class.
  \item \textbf{XPath:} Powerful but a bit slower on mobile, still very useful.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{B. Locators Collect Karne Ka Tarika (Android Example)}

\subsubsection*{1. UIAutomatorViewer (Android)}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{android-sdk/tools/bin/UIAutomatorViewer} tool run karo (Android SDK installed ho).
  \item Mobile device connect rakho, target app open karo.
  \item UIAutomatorViewer me screenshot lo—\textbf{click on any element, uska resource-id, class, XPath, sab dikhega}.
  \item Copy locator and use in Appium scripts.
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Appium Android Locator Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from appium import webdriver

element = driver.find_element("id", "com.app.package:id/submit")
element = driver.find_element("accessibility id", "loginButton")  # Accessibility ID
element = driver.find_element("class name", "android.widget.Button")
element = driver.find_element("xpath", "//android.widget.Button[@content-desc='login']")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsubsection*{2. Appium Inspector (Cross-platform GUI Tool)}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Download and install ``Appium Inspector''.
  \item Start Appium server.
  \item Connect device/emulator, open Inspector.
  \item App screen ka snapshot dikhega; kisi bhi element pe click karne se sab possible locator strategies dikhenge (resource-id, class, xpath, accessibility label, etc.).
  \item \textbf{Copy locator details aur apne scripts me use karo.}
\end{itemize}

\section{3. Pro Beginner Extensions/Tools List}

\begin{tabular}{|p{4cm}|p{3cm}|p{7cm}|p{5cm}|}
\hline
\textbf{Tool/Extension} & \textbf{Platform} & \textbf{What/Why} & \textbf{Install Steps} \\
\hline
SelectorHub & Web (Selenium) & Robust XPath/CSS auto-suggest \& validation & Browser extension (WebStore) \\
\hline
ChroPath & Web (Selenium) & Alternate locator auto-suggest & Browser extension (WebStore) \\
\hline
Fake Filler & Web (Testing) & Auto-fill web forms for testing & Browser extension (WebStore) \\
\hline
Axe DevTools & Web & Automated accessibility audit (a11y) & Browser extension (WebStore) \\
\hline
Appium Inspector & Mobile (Appium) & Visual locator tool for Android/iOS apps & Download app (official site) \\
\hline
UIAutomatorViewer & Mobile (Appium) & Android XML hierarchy inspector \& locator visualizer & Included with Android SDK \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\section*{Golden Beginner Tips}
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Always try \textbf{ID/resource-id} locator first (fastest \& most reliable).
  \item Tab tak plugin/extension use karo until you get confident extracting locators manually.
  \item \textbf{Plugin locator copy karne ke baad}, apne script me paste karke test karo ki sahi kaam kar raha hai ya nahi.
  \item Mobile pe accessibility labels set karwana developers se bolo—automation simple ho jayega.
\end{itemize}

\noindent Ek beginner ko \textbf{har step hand-on practice} karna zaruri hai, plugins/Inspector tools se start karna best hai. Zeher notes bana rahe ho bro, ab in extensions ke workflow add kar loge toh full paisa vasool ho jayega!

\begin{document}

\title{\textbf{\color{sectionblue}�� E-Commerce Selenium Automation Framework - Complete Beginner Guide}}
\author{}
\date{}
\maketitle

Ye ek professional automation framework hai jo Selenium aur PyTest ke saath banaya gaya hai taaki e-commerce website (jaise OpenCart) ko test kar sako. Main tumhe har ek part ko detail mein samjhaunga – kya hai, kyun hai, kaise use karoge – taaki tum confidently isko setup karo aur professional QA tester ban jao!

\section*{�� PROJECT STRUCTURE OVERVIEW for industry ready approach ...}

Sabse pehle project ka structure samajhte hain. Ye industry-standard tarike se organized hai taaki code maintain karna aur samajhna aasan ho:

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Project Structure}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=GenericText]
ecommerce_automation/          ← Main project folder
├── README.md                  ← Project ki basic info
├── requirements.txt           ← Python packages ki list
├── pytest.ini                ← Test configuration file
├── .env                      ← Secret values jaise URL/passwords
├── conftest.py               ← Browser setup aur teardown
│
├── tests/                    ← Yahan actual test cases honge
│   ├── test_login.py        ← Login testing
│   ├── test_signup.py       ← Registration testing
│   ├── test_cart.py         ← Cart functionality
│   └── test_checkout.py     ← Order placement
│
├── pages/                    ← Page Object Model files
│   ├── base_page.py         ← Common functions
│   ├── login_page.py        ← Login page actions
│   ├── home_page.py         ← Homepage actions
│   ├── cart_page.py         ← Cart page actions
│   └── checkout_page.py     ← Checkout actions
│
├── utils/                    ← Helper functions
│   ├── logger.py            ← Log messages
│   ├── screenshot.py        ← Screenshots capture
│   └── data_reader.py       ← Excel/CSV data read
│
├── data/                     ← Test data files
│   ├── users.xlsx           ← Login credentials
│   └── products.csv         ← Product info
│
├── reports/                  ← Test reports (auto-generated)
└── screenshots/              ← Failure screenshots (auto-generated)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

Ab ek-ek karke har cheez ko detail mein dekhte hain.

\section*{�� ROOT LEVEL FILES - Setup Ka Pehla Step}

Ye files project ke root mein hoti hain aur project ko setup karne ke liye zaroori hain.

\subsection*{�� requirements.txt}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Kya hai?} Ye ek list hai Python packages ki jo project chalane ke liye chahiye.
  \item \textbf{Kyun chahiye?} Taaki ek hi command se saari dependencies install ho jayein aur team ke saath share karna aasan ho.
  \item \textbf{Kya likha hoga?}
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={requirements.txt}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=GenericText]
selenium==4.15.0         # Browser automation ke liye
pytest==7.4.3            # Testing framework
pytest-html==4.1.1       # HTML reports ke liye
openpyxl==3.1.2          # Excel files padhne ke liye
webdriver-manager==4.0.1 # Browser driver auto manage karta hai
python-dotenv==1.0.0     # .env file se data padhne ke liye
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Kaise use karoge?} Terminal mein ye command run karo:
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Installation Command}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
pip install -r requirements.txt
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{�� .env}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Kya hai?} Isme sensitive info store karte hain jaise website URL, username, password.
  \item \textbf{Kyun chahiye?} Taaki ye cheezein code mein hardcode na karni padein aur secure rahein.
  \item \textbf{Kya likha hoga?}
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={.env File}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=GenericText]
BASE_URL=https://demo.opencart.com  # Website ka base URL
USERNAME=testuser@gmail.com         # Test user ka email
PASSWORD=Test@123                   # Test user ka password
HEADLESS=false                      # Browser UI ke saath chalega
TIMEOUT=10                          # Wait time in seconds
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Kaise use karoge?} Python mein \texttt{os.getenv("BASE\_URL")} likhkar access karoge.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{�� pytest.ini}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Kya hai?} PyTest ke liye configuration file hai.
  \item \textbf{Kyun chahiye?} Tests ko run karne ke default settings set karne ke liye.
  \item \textbf{Kya likha hoga?}
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={pytest.ini}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=GenericText]
[pytest]
addopts = --html=reports/report.html --self-contained-html -v
markers =
    smoke: Quick sanity tests       # Fast basic tests
    regression: Detailed test cases # Complete tests
    cart: Cart related tests        # Cart-specific tests
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Samajhna:}
  \begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{addopts} = Har test run pe HTML report banega aur verbose output milega.
    \item \texttt{markers} = Tests ko category mein divide karne ke liye.
  \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{�� README.md}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Kya hai?} Project ka introduction aur setup instructions.
  \item \textbf{Kyun chahiye?} Taaki koi bhi nayi team member easily setup kar sake.
  \item \textbf{Kya likha hoga?}
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={README.md}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=GenericText]
# E-Commerce Automation Framework

## Setup:
1. Install Python 3.8+
2. Run: `pip install -r requirements.txt`
3. Update `.env` file with your URLs

## Run Tests:
- All tests: `pytest`
- Smoke tests: `pytest -m smoke`
- With reports: `pytest --html=reports/report.html`
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\section*{⚙️ conftest.py - Browser Setup Ka Boss}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Kya hai?} Ye file PyTest ke liye browser setup aur cleanup karti hai.
  \item \textbf{Kyun chahiye?} Taaki har test se pehle browser khule aur test ke baad band ho jaye.
  \item \textbf{Complete Code:}
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={conftest.py}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import pytest                    # Testing framework
import os                       # Environment variables ke liye
from selenium import webdriver  # Browser control
from selenium.webdriver.chrome.options import Options  # Chrome settings
from webdriver_manager.chrome import ChromeDriverManager  # Driver manager
from dotenv import load_dotenv  # .env file load

load_dotenv()  # .env file se values load karo

@pytest.fixture(scope="function")  # Har test ke liye naya browser
def driver():
    """
    Browser setup aur cleanup
    """
    chrome_options = Options()  # Chrome ke options set karo
    
    # Headless mode check (bina UI ke)
    if os.getenv("HEADLESS", "false").lower() == "true":
        chrome_options.add_argument("--headless")  # Background mein chalega
    
    chrome_options.add_argument("--no-sandbox")  # Linux compatibility
    chrome_options.add_argument("--disable-dev-shm-usage")  # Memory fix
    chrome_options.add_argument("--window-size=1920,1080")  # Window size
    
    # Chrome browser start karo
    driver = webdriver.Chrome(
        ChromeDriverManager().install(),  # Driver auto download
        options=chrome_options
    )
    
    driver.maximize_window()  # Full screen
    driver.implicitly_wait(int(os.getenv("TIMEOUT", "10")))  # Default wait 10 sec
    
    yield driver  # Test ko driver do
    driver.quit()  # Test ke baad band karo

@pytest.fixture(scope="session")  # Poore session ke liye ek baar
def base_url():
    """Base URL for all tests"""
    return os.getenv("BASE_URL", "https://demo.opencart.com")  # Default URL
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Line-by-Line:}
  \begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{@pytest.fixture(scope="function")} = Har test ke liye naya browser khulega.
    \item \texttt{yield driver} = Test ko browser deta hai, baad mein \texttt{quit()} band karta hai.
    \item \texttt{implicitly\_wait(10)} = Har action ke liye 10 sec tak wait karega.
  \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\section*{�� pages/ - Page Object Model (POM) Files}

\textbf{POM Kya Hai?} Har web page ke liye ek alag class banate hain jisme us page ke elements (locators) aur actions (click, type) define hote hain.  
\textbf{Kyun Use Karte Hain?} Code organized rehta hai, agar ek element change ho to sirf us page ki class mein update karo, baaki sab apne aap theek ho jata hai.

\subsection*{�� pages/base\_page.py - Common Functions}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Kya hai?} Ye base class hai jo sab pages ke liye common functions rakhti hai.
  \item \textbf{Kyun chahiye?} Taaki har page mein same code baar-baar na likhna pade.
  \item \textbf{Complete Code:}
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={pages/base\_page.py}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver.support.ui import WebDriverWait  # Wait ke liye
from selenium.webdriver.support import expected_conditions as EC  # Conditions
from selenium.webdriver.common.by import By  # Locators ke liye
import os  # Environment variables

class BasePage:
    """
    Base class for all page objects
    """
    
    def __init__(self, driver):  # Constructor
        self.driver = driver  # Driver save karo
        self.wait = WebDriverWait(driver, int(os.getenv("TIMEOUT", "10")))  # Wait object
    
    def find_element(self, by, locator):  # Element dhoondho
        """Element dhoondho with wait"""
        return self.wait.until(EC.presence_of_element_located((by, locator)))
    
    def click_element(self, by, locator):  # Click karo
        """Element pe click karo"""
        element = self.wait.until(EC.element_to_be_clickable((by, locator)))
        element.click()
    
    def enter_text(self, by, locator, text):  # Text daalo
        """Text field mein value daalo"""
        element = self.find_element(by, locator)
        element.clear()  # Purana text hatao
        element.send_keys(text)  # Naya text daalo
    
    def get_text(self, by, locator):  # Text lo
        """Element ka text return karo"""
        return self.find_element(by, locator).text
    
    def is_element_visible(self, by, locator):  # Visibility check
        """Check karo element dikhta hai ya nahi"""
        try:
            self.wait.until(EC.visibility_of_element_located((by, locator)))
            return True
        except:
            return False
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{�� pages/login\_page.py - Login Page Actions}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Kya hai?} Login page ke elements aur actions define karta hai.
  \item \textbf{Complete Code:}
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={pages/login\_page.py}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver.common.by import By  # Locators ke liye
from pages.base_page import BasePage  # BasePage class ko inherit kiya
import os  # Env variables ke liye

class LoginPage(BasePage):
    """
    LoginPage ne BasePage ko inherit kiya hai
    Yahan login page ke saare elements aur actions define hain
    """

    # Elements ke locators - (By method, locator string)
    EMAIL_INPUT = (By.ID, "input-email")
    PASSWORD_INPUT = (By.ID, "input-password")
    LOGIN_BUTTON = (By.CSS_SELECTOR, "input[value='Login']")
    ERROR_MESSAGE = (By.CSS_SELECTOR, ".alert-danger")

    def go_to_login_page(self):
        """Login page pe jaane ke liye URL open karo"""
        base_url = os.getenv("BASE_URL")
        self.driver.get(f"{base_url}/index.php?route=account/login")

    def enter_email(self, email):
        """Email input field mein value daalo"""
        self.enter_text(*self.EMAIL_INPUT, email)  
        # �� Yahan * ka matlab: tuple ko alag-alag arguments mein todna
        # self.EMAIL_INPUT = (By.ID, "input-email")
        # *self.EMAIL_INPUT → By.ID, "input-email"
        # Final call → self.enter_text(By.ID, "input-email", email)

    def enter_password(self, password):
        """Password input field mein value daalo"""
        self.enter_text(*self.PASSWORD_INPUT, password)

    def click_login_button(self):
        """Login button pe click karo"""
        self.click_element(*self.LOGIN_BUTTON)

    def login(self, email, password):
        """Poora login process complete karo"""
        self.enter_email(email)
        self.enter_password(password)
        self.click_login_button()

    def get_error_message(self):
        """Agar login fail ho toh error message return karo"""
        if self.is_element_visible(*self.ERROR_MESSAGE):
            return self.get_text(*self.ERROR_MESSAGE)
        return ""
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{* (Star)}: Tuple jaise (By.ID, "value") ko unpack karke function mein alag arguments bana deta hai.
  \item Agar * nahi lagayenge to poora tuple ek hi argument ban jaayega, aur error milega.
  \item Yahan BasePage ke functions ko reuse kiya gaya hai jaise \texttt{enter\_text()}, \texttt{click\_element()}.
\end{itemize}


\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Samajhna:}
  \begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{*self.EMAIL\_INPUT} = Tuple (By.ID, ``input-email'') ko unpack karta hai.
    \item \texttt{BasePage} se inherit karke \texttt{enter\_text}, \texttt{click\_element} jaise functions use hote hain.
  \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\section*{�� tests/ - Actual Test Cases}

Ye folder mein real test cases hote hain jo website ki functionality check karte hain.

\subsection*{�� tests/test\_login.py - Login Test Cases}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Complete Code:}
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={tests/test\_login.py}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import pytest  # Testing framework
import os  # Env variables
from pages.login_page import LoginPage  # Login page class

class TestLogin:
    """
    Login ke test cases
    """
    
    @pytest.mark.smoke  # Smoke test category
    def test_valid_login(self, driver, base_url):  # Valid login
        """Valid credentials se login check"""
        login_page = LoginPage(driver)  # Object banao
        login_page.go_to_login_page()  # Login page pe jao
        login_page.login(os.getenv("USERNAME"), os.getenv("PASSWORD"))  # Login karo
        assert "account" in driver.current_url, "Login nahi hua!"
    
    @pytest.mark.regression  # Regression test category
    def test_invalid_login(self, driver):  # Invalid login
        """Galat credentials se login check"""
        login_page = LoginPage(driver)
        login_page.go_to_login_page()
        login_page.login("wrong@email.com", "wrongpass")  # Galat data
        error = login_page.get_error_message()
        assert "No match" in error, "Error message nahi dikha!"
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Samajhna:}
  \begin{itemize}
    \item \texttt{@pytest.mark.smoke} = Ye test fast sanity check ke liye hai.
    \item \texttt{driver} aur \texttt{base\_url} = \texttt{conftest.py} se aate hain.
    \item \texttt{assert} = Test pass ya fail decide karta hai.
  \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\section*{��️ utils/ - Helper Functions}

Ye folder mein chhoti-chhoti helper files hoti hain.

\subsection*{�� utils/logger.py}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Kya hai?} Test ke logs banata hai.
  \item \textbf{Kyun chahiye?} Taaki pata chale test mein kya hua.
  \item \textbf{Code:}
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={utils/logger.py}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import logging  # Logging module
import os  # Folder banane ke liye
from datetime import datetime  # Timestamp ke liye

def get_logger(name):
    logger = logging.getLogger(name)
    if not logger.handlers:  # Agar handler nahi hai
        os.makedirs("logs", exist_ok=True)  # Logs folder banao
        handler = logging.FileHandler(f"logs/test_{datetime.now().strftime('%Y%m%d_%H%M%S')}.log")
        handler.setFormatter(logging.Formatter('%(asctime)s | %(message)s'))  # Format
        logger.addHandler(handler)
        logger.setLevel(logging.INFO)  # Info level logs
    return logger
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

pip install -r requirements.txt

# Sab tests run karo
pytest

# Specific test file
pytest tests/test_login.py

# Smoke tests only
pytest -m smoke

# Report ke saath
pytest --html=reports/report.html

# Verbose output (details)
pytest -v

\section*{�� Framework Ke Fayde}

\begin{enumerate}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Organized:} Har cheez alag-alag rakhi hai.
  \item \textbf{Easy Maintenance:} Ek change se sab fix ho jata hai.
  \item \textbf{Professional:} Industry mein aise hi frameworks use hote hain.
\end{enumerate}

\section*{❓ Common Doubts Clear Kiye}

\subsection*{@pytest.fixture(scope="function") Kya Hai?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Ye PyTest ko batata hai ki ye function setup ke liye hai.
  \item \texttt{scope="function"} = Har test ke liye naya browser khulega.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{POM Kyun Use Karte Hain?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Page Object Model se har page ke elements aur actions alag class mein hote hain.
  \item Agar ek locator change ho, to sirf us page ko update karo, baaki tests safe!
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Inheritance Ka Role Kya Hai?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{LoginPage} class \texttt{BasePage} se inherit karti hai taaki common functions baar-baar na likhne padein.
\end{itemize}
