\begin{document}

\begin{center}
  {\Huge\bfseries \textcolor{sectionblue}{�� XPath ka \texttt{.//} Kya Matlab Hai}} \\[10pt]
  {\large \textit{Step-by-step Explanation in Simple Words}} 
\end{center}

\vspace{15pt}

\noindent
Jab hum Selenium ya XPath likhte hain, kabhi kabhi aise likha hota hai:

\begin{tcolorbox}[mycode, title=Example XPath]
.//span[text()='Sign In']
\end{tcolorbox}

Aao isko \textbf{step-by-step aur simple words} mein samjhte hain:

\vspace{15pt}

\section*{✅ 1. \texttt{.} (Dot) ka Matlab}

\begin{tcolorbox}[keypoint, title={Meaning of \texttt{.} (Dot)}]
\texttt{dot (.)} ka matlab hai: \textcolor{textgreen}{``Current element''} yaani jahan abhi tum ho.

\begin{itemize}
  \item Agar tum ek \verb|<button>| ke andar ho, to \texttt{.} ka matlab hota hai: \textbf{wohi button} khud.
  \item Iska use tab hota hai jab tum kisi specific element ke \textbf{andar} hi search karna chahte ho.
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{5pt}

\noindent \textbf{Example:}

\begin{quote}
“Main abhi \texttt{button} ke andar hoon.” Toh XPath expression \verb|.//span| ka matlab hai, iss button ke andar kahin bhi \verb|<span>| search karo.
\end{quote}

\vspace{20pt}

\section*{✅ 2. \texttt{//} ka Matlab}

\begin{tcolorbox}[keypoint, title={Meaning of \texttt{//} (Double Slash)}]
\texttt{//} ka matlab hai: \textcolor{textgreen}{``Is jagah ke andar jitne bhi children, grandchildren hain — sabko check karo''}.

\begin{itemize}
  \item \texttt{//} recursive search karta hai.
  \item Matlab kisi bhi level pe jo match mile, \textbf{use le lega}.
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{5pt}

\noindent \textbf{Example:}

\begin{quote}
\verb|//div| matlab, document ke har jagah se \verb|<div>| elements dhundho — chahe wo kisi bhi level pe ho.
\end{quote}

\vspace{20pt}

\section*{✅ 3. \texttt{.//} ka Matlab}

\begin{tcolorbox}[keypoint, title={Combined Meaning: \texttt{.//}}]
\texttt{.//} ka matlab hai: \textcolor{textgreen}{``Current element ke andar kahi bhi (chahe nested kitna bhi deep ho) jo bhi matching element ho, use khojho.''}

\begin{itemize}
  \item Yeh \verb|.| se shuru hota hai toh search starting point \textbf{current node} hai, na ki pura document.
  \item \verb|//| matlab anywhere inside, recursive search.
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{5pt}

\noindent \textbf{Example XPath:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[mycode, title=Usage Example]
\texttt{//button[.//span[text()='Sign In']]}
\end{tcolorbox}

Iska matlab:

\begin{quote}
Select karo \verb|<button>| jiske andar kahin bhi ek \verb|<span>| ho jiska text ho \texttt{"Sign In"}.
\end{quote}

\vspace{20pt}

\section*{�� XPath \texttt{//} vs \texttt{.//} Ka Farak Aur Galatiyan}

\begin{tcolorbox}[warning, title={Avoid This Common Mistake}]
\textbf{Galti:} \verb|//button[//span[text()='Sign In']]| 

Yeh XPath sahi nahi hai kyunki:

\begin{itemize}
  \item \verb|//span[...]| pure document mein \textbf{sab jagah} \verb|<span>| dhundhta hai.
  \item Iska matlab hai ki \textbf{button ke andar hona} ka koi matlab nahi.
  \item Yeh condition XPath me \textbf{sahi tarah se limit nahi karta} ki span button ke andar hona chahiye.
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{5pt}

\noindent \textbf{Correct:} \verb|//button[.//span[text()='Sign In']]| 

Ismein \verb|.//span| button ke andar hi restrict karta hai search ko, jisse expected result milega.

\vspace{20pt}

\section*{�� Summary Table}

\begin{center}
\rowcolors{2}{tablealt}{white}
\begin{tabular}{>{\bfseries}p{5cm} p{8cm}}
\toprule
\rowcolor{tablehead}
\textcolor{white}{\textbf{XPath Syntax}} & \textcolor{white}{\textbf{Simple Meaning In Hinglish}} \\
\midrule
\verb|.| & Current element, jahan abhi tum ho \\
\verb|//| & Anywhere inside (children, grandchildren, etc.) \\
\verb|.//| & Current element ke andar kahin bhi (nested) \\
\verb|//button[.//span]| & Button jisme span nested ho \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\vspace{20pt}

\section*{�� Final Tip}

\noindent
\textbf{XPath likhte waqt:}

\begin{itemize}
  \item Agar tum kisi element ke andar \textbf{nested} elements dhundhna chahte ho, toh \texttt{.//} ka use karo.
  \item Agar tum document ka pura scope \textbf{global} check karna chahte ho, toh sirf \texttt{//} ka use karo.
\end{itemize}

\vspace{15pt}

\noindent
\textcolor{sectionblue}{\rule{\linewidth}{1.2pt}}

\vspace{10pt}

\noindent \textit{Ye guide beginner friendly hai, aur XPath ke inner working ko Hindi-English mix me simple tarike se samjhane ki koshish karta hai.}

===============================

  showstringspaces=false,
}

\begin{document}

\title{\textbf{\color{sectionblue}\texttt{pytest-watch} – Nodemon jaisa tool for Python Tests}}
\author{}
\date{}
\maketitle

\section*{Objective:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=objectivebg, colframe=sectionblue, boxrule=1pt, sharp corners, left=8pt, right=8pt, top=8pt, bottom=8pt]
Jaise Node.js projects mein \texttt{nodemon} use karte hain taaki har file change pe server auto-restart ho jaaye — waise hi \textbf{Python tests} ko auto-run karwane ke liye hum use karte hain \texttt{pytest-watch}.
\end{tcolorbox}

\section*{1. Tool Install Karna}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Installation Command}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
pip install pytest-watch
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Ye tool install karte hi tumhare system mein \texttt{ptw} command available ho jaata hai.
  \item \texttt{ptw} = \textbf{pytest watch}
\end{itemize}

\section*{2. Basic Command: Auto Run Tests}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Basic Auto-Run Command}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
ptw
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Isse \texttt{watch mode} activate ho jaata hai.
  \item Ab jaise hi tum test file ya source code file change karoge — tests \textbf{automatically run} ho jaayenge.
\end{itemize}

\section*{3. Realistic Test Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={test\_calculator.py}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
# test_calculator.py

def test_addition():
    assert 2 + 3 == 5

def test_subtraction():
    assert 5 - 2 == 3
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

Agar tum \texttt{ptw} chala doge, to har baar file save karne par dono tests dobara run honge.

\section*{4. Run Only Specific Tests (\texttt{-k} flag)}

Agar tum sirf ek specific test run karwana chahte ho (jaise sirf \texttt{test\_addition}) tab:

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Specific Test Filter}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
ptw -- -k "addition"
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Explanation:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{-k} is a filter.
  \item \texttt{"addition"} ka matlab: sirf wo test jinke naam mein "addition" word ho — wo hi run honge.
  \item Ye \textbf{partial match} hota hai.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{More Examples with \texttt{-k}:}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|X|X|}
\hline
\textbf{Command} & \textbf{What it does} \\
\hline
\texttt{ptw -- -k "login"} & Sirf tests run honge jinke naam mein \texttt{login} aata hai \\
\hline
\texttt{ptw -- -k "invalid"} & Sirf invalid waale test run honge (jaise \texttt{test\_invalid\_input}) \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}

\section*{5. Ignore Folder from Watch}

Agar tum chahte ho ki koi folder ke changes ignore ho jaayein (e.g., migrations, venv, etc.):

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Ignore Folders}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
ptw --ignore "venv/"
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\section*{6. Use Custom Runner (e.g., for verbose output)}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Custom Runner with Verbose Output}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
ptw --runner "pytest -v"
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{-v} (verbose) flag deta hai zyada detailed output har test ka.
\end{itemize}

\section*{7. Alternative for Linux/macOS:}

Agar \texttt{ptw} nahi chalta (ya Windows mein issue ho) to:

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Linux/macOS Alternative}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
watch -n 2 pytest
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Ye har \textbf{2 second} mein \texttt{pytest} run karega, chahe file badli ho ya nahi.
  \item Downside: Ye smart nahi hai — har 2 second mein run karta rahega unnecessarily.
\end{itemize}

\section*{8. Advanced Tip – Multiple Options Combine Karke}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Combined Options}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
ptw -- -v -k "auth"
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

Matlab:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Verbose output ke saath,
  \item Sirf \texttt{auth} related test hi run karne hain
\end{itemize}

\section*{Summary Table:}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|X|X|}
\hline
\textbf{Use Case} & \textbf{Command} \\
\hline
Auto-run all tests & \texttt{ptw} \\
\hline
Run only specific tests & \texttt{ptw -- -k "keyword"} \\
\hline
Verbose test output & \texttt{ptw -- -v} \\
\hline
Ignore folder changes & \texttt{ptw --ignore "foldername/"} \\
\hline
Custom runner with flags & \texttt{ptw --runner "pytest -v -k 'login'"} \\
\hline
Linux fallback & \texttt{watch -n 2 pytest} \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}

\section*{Suitable for:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \checkmarkinline Developers doing TDD (Test Driven Development)
  \item \checkmarkinline QA Engineers automating regression tests
  \item \checkmarkinline Python devs migrating from Node.js and missing \texttt{nodemon}
  \item \checkmarkinline Security testers validating test cases frequently
\end{itemize}

\section*{\texttt{ptw} (pytest-watch) \textbf{sirf ek file} run karta hai ya \textbf{saare test files}?}

\subsection*{Answer:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=warningbg, colframe=importantred, boxrule=1pt, sharp corners, left=8pt, right=8pt, top=8pt, bottom=8pt]
\texttt{ptw} \textbf{saare test files run karta hai} (jinmein test cases hain) — \textbf{jaise hi koi bhi relevant file change hoti hai}.
\end{tcolorbox}

\section*{Thoda Detail mein:}

Jab tum command chalaate ho:

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Basic Command}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
ptw
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

To:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Yeh tumhare \textbf{poore project directory ko watch} karta hai.
  \item Jaise hi \textbf{kisi bhi Python file} mein change hota hai (especially test files ya unse linked source files), \texttt{pytest} dobara \textbf{saare test cases} ko run karta hai — \textbf{sirf wo test nahi jisme change hua ho}.
\end{itemize}

\subsection*{Example:}

Agar tumhare paas yeh test files hain:

\begin{verbatim}
tests/
├── test_auth.py
├── test_cart.py
├── test_checkout.py
\end{verbatim}

Agar tum \texttt{test\_cart.py} file mein kuch change karte ho (aur save karte ho), to:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{ptw} puri directory ke test cases dobara run karega:
  \begin{itemize}
    \item test\_auth
    \item test\_cart
    \item test\_checkout
  \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

Yeh ek tarah se \textbf{full test run} hota hai \textbf{on every save}.

\section*{Want to Limit? Use Filter:}

Agar tum sirf ek particular test file ko run karna chahte ho — chahe koi file change ho ya nahi — to use karo:

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Specific File Run}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
ptw tests/test_cart.py
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

Ya phir test name filter:

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Test Name Filter}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
ptw -- -k "cart"
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\section*{Summary:}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|X|X|}
\hline
\textbf{Situation} & \textbf{Behavior} \\
\hline
Normal \texttt{ptw} & \checkmarkinline All tests run jab bhi koi change hota hai \\
\hline
Change sirf ek file mein & \checkmarkinline Tab bhi all tests run honge \\
\hline
Specific file chahiye run karna & Use \texttt{ptw test\_filename.py} \\
\hline
Specific test run karna & Use \texttt{ptw -- -k "testname"} \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}

\begin{document}

\title{\textbf{\color{sectionblue} pytest -s Command — Most important command...}}
\author{}
\date{}
\maketitle

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=objectivebg, colframe=sectionblue, boxrule=1pt, sharp corners, left=8pt, right=8pt, top=8pt, bottom=8pt]
Bahut badhiya question bhai! \texttt{pytest -s} command testing karte waqt input/output ya print statements ko samajhne ke liye kaafi kaam aata hai. Chalo simple hinglish mein full explain karta hoon:
\end{tcolorbox}

\section*{ Syntax:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Basic Syntax}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
pytest -s
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\section*{ Kya karta hai -s?}

\subsection*{ \texttt{-s} ka matlab hota hai:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=conceptgreen!10, colframe=conceptgreen!80, boxrule=1pt, sharp corners, left=8pt, right=8pt, top=8pt, bottom=8pt]
\textbf{``Don't capture output.''}
\end{tcolorbox}

Jab tum normally pytest chalaate ho, to:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{print()} ke output ya \texttt{input()} calls screen par nahi dikhte.
  \item Kyunki pytest by default stdout/stderr capture karta hai.
\end{itemize}

Lekin agar tum:

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={With -s Flag}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
pytest -s
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

chalaate ho, to:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item  \texttt{print()} ka output terminal mein dikhne lagega.
  \item  \texttt{input()} se tum input le sakte ho during test.
\end{itemize}

\section*{ Kab use karein -s?}

\subsection*{ Useful when:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Debug karna ho test code (print statements se)
  \item \texttt{input()} lena ho user se during test
  \item pdb (Python debugger) ya interactive code chalana ho
\end{itemize}

\section*{ Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={test\_example.py}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
# test_example.py

def test_addition():
    name = input("Enter your name: ")  # Without -s, ye chalega hi nahi
    print("Hello", name)
    assert 2 + 2 == 4
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\textbf{Run:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Run Command}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
pytest -s test_example.py
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{ Output:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=successbg, colframe=conceptgreen!80, boxrule=1pt, sharp corners, left=8pt, right=8pt, top=8pt, bottom=8pt]
\begin{verbatim}
Enter your name: Satyam
Hello Satyam
.
1 passed
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}

\section*{ Without -s kya hota?}

Agar tum just \texttt{pytest test\_example.py} chalaoge, to:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{input()} par test hang ya crash ho jaayega.
  \item \texttt{print()} ka output nahi dikhega.
\end{itemize}

\section*{ Summary Table:}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|X|X|}
\hline
\textbf{Command} & \textbf{Kya karta hai} \\
\hline
\texttt{pytest} & Normal test run, print/input hidden \\
\hline
\texttt{pytest -s} & Print visible, input allow karta hai \\
\hline
\texttt{pytest -s -v} & Print visible + detailed test output \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}

\vspace{10pt}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=warningbg, colframe=importantred, boxrule=1pt, sharp corners, left=8pt, right=8pt, top=8pt, bottom=8pt]
Agar tum debug kar rahe ho ya koi interactive behavior test kar rahe ho, to \texttt{-s} zaroor lagao ✅

Aur batana agar tumko pdb debugger bhi chahiye samajhna, vo bhi professional testing mein kaam aata hai.
\end{tcolorbox}

===============================

  urlcolor=cyan,

% Code listings for Python
\lstdefinelanguage{CustomPython}{
  language=Python,
  basicstyle=\ttfamily\footnotesize,
  keywordstyle=\color{keywordblue}\bfseries,
  stringstyle=\color{stringred},
  commentstyle=\color{commentgreen}\itshape,
  morecomment=[l][\color{commentgreen}\itshape]{\#},
  breaklines=true,
  breakatwhitespace=true,

  numbersep=5pt,

  language=bash,
  basicstyle=\ttfamily\footnotesize,
  keywordstyle=\color{keywordblue}\bfseries,

  frame=single,
  framerule=0.5pt,

  numbers=left,
  numberstyle=\tiny\color{gray},
  numbersep=5pt,
  xleftmargin=10pt,
  showstringspaces=false,

\begin{document}

\title{\textbf{\color{sectionblue}How \texttt{pytest} Automatically Runs Your \texttt{test\_} Functions (Without Manual Call)}}
\author{}
\date{}
\maketitle

\section*{�� 1. Tumne Ek Function Banaya:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Function Definition}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
def test_dashboard_navigation(driver):
    ...
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

Tumne is function ko \textbf{kahin pe bhi manually call nahi kiya}:

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=warningbg, colframe=importantred, boxrule=1pt, sharp corners, left=8pt, right=8pt, top=8pt, bottom=8pt]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
test_dashboard_navigation(driver)  # ❌ Aisa kuch nahi likha
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

Phir bhi jab \texttt{pytest} command chalate ho — ye function \textbf{run ho jaata hai}!

\section*{�� 2. Pytest Ka Internal Kaam: \textbf{Test Discovery System}}

\subsection*{Jab Tum Command Chalate Ho:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Pytest Command}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
pytest
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

Tab \texttt{pytest} kuch kaafi important steps karta hai:

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|c|X|}
\hline
\textbf{Step} & \textbf{Kaam} \\
\hline
1️⃣ & Current directory aur subfolders scan karta hai \\
\hline
2️⃣ & Sirf wo files select karta hai jinka naam \texttt{test\_*.py} hota hai \\
\hline
3️⃣ & Fir un files ke andar functions dhundta hai jo \texttt{test\_} se start hote hain \\
\hline
4️⃣ & Un functions ko automatically \textbf{run/call} karta hai \\
\hline
5️⃣ & Har test ka pass/fail result CLI pe show karta hai \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}

\section*{✅ Example}

\subsection*{\texttt{test\_login.py}}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={test\_login.py}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
def test_dashboard_navigation(driver):
    print("Testing dashboard navigation")
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{Run Command:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Run Command}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=BashShell]
pytest -s
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{Output:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=successbg, colframe=conceptgreen!80, boxrule=1pt, sharp corners, left=8pt, right=8pt, top=8pt, bottom=8pt]
\begin{verbatim}
Testing dashboard navigation
1 passed in 1.02s
\end{verbatim}
\end{tcolorbox}

☑️ \textbf{Tumne function manually call nahi kiya, phir bhi run hua!}

\section*{�� Kyu Run Hua Without Manual Call?}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=infobg, colframe=sectionblue, boxrule=1pt, sharp corners, left=8pt, right=8pt, top=8pt, bottom=8pt]
\textbf{Answer:}
\texttt{pytest} automatically samajh jaata hai ki:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item File ka naam \texttt{test\_*.py} → ye test file hai
  \item Function ka naam \texttt{test\_} se start ho raha hai → ye test function hai
\end{itemize}

Isliye usko \textbf{automatically run} karta hai — bina kisi manual function call ke.
\end{tcolorbox}

\section*{⚙️ Internally Pytest Ye Kaam Kar Raha Hota Hai:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Internal Working}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
import test_login                     # tumhari test file import karta hai
test_login.test_dashboard_navigation(driver=fixture_object)  
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

➡️ Tumhe kuch manually likhne ki zarurat nahi hoti — \texttt{pytest} ye sab \textbf{automatically} handle karta hai.

\section*{�� Important Rule:}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|X|X|}
\hline
\textbf{Function Naming} & \textbf{Pytest Behavior} \\
\hline
✅ \texttt{test\_abc()} & Run hoga automatically \\
\hline
❌ \texttt{abc\_test()} & Run nahi hoga pytest ke through \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}

\section*{�� Bonus: \texttt{driver} Ka Value Kahan Se Aata Hai?}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Agar function ke andar \texttt{driver} diya hai, to uska data \textbf{pytest fixture} se aata hai.
  \item Ye fixtures tum \texttt{conftest.py} file me define karte ho.
  \item Example:
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Fixture Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
@pytest.fixture
def driver():
    # setup browser driver
    yield driver_instance
    # teardown code
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\section*{�� Summary Table:}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|X|X|}
\hline
\textbf{Question} & \textbf{Answer} \\
\hline
Function manually call nahi kiya, fir bhi run kaise? & Pytest automatically discover karke run karta hai \texttt{test\_} se start hone wale functions \\
\hline
Kaunsi files pytest uthata hai? & Sirf those files jinka naam \texttt{test\_*.py} hota hai \\
\hline
Kaunsa function pytest run karta hai? & Wo functions jo \texttt{test\_} se start ho rahe hain \\
\hline
\texttt{driver} ya arguments ka value kaun deta hai? & Pytest fixtures system through setup hota hai \\
\hline
Agar naam \texttt{dashboard\_test()} ho toh? & Wo function pytest se run nahi hoga \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}

===============================
===============================
\hrule


\hypersetup{
  colorlinks=true,
  linkcolor=blue,
  urlcolor=cyan,
}

% Define colors
\definecolor{sectionblue}{RGB}{0,0,180}

  language=Python,

\title{\textbf{\color{sectionblue}Lambda Functions \& Expected Conditions in Selenium - Complete Guide}}
\author{}
\date{}
\maketitle

\section*{�� PART 1: \texttt{lambda} Function in Python (Especially for Selenium)}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=partbg, colframe=sectionblue, boxrule=1pt, sharp corners, left=8pt, right=8pt, top=8pt, bottom=8pt]
\subsection*{✅ What is lambda?}

Lambda ek \textbf{anonymous (nameless)} function hota hai jo \textbf{one-line expression} ke liye use hota hai.
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{�� Syntax:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Lambda Syntax}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
lambda arguments: expression
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{�� Example (Normal vs Lambda):}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Normal vs Lambda Function}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
# Normal function
def add(x, y):
    return x + y

# Lambda version
add = lambda x, y: x + y
print(add(2, 3))  # Output: 5
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{✅ Why we use \texttt{lambda} in Selenium?}

Selenium mein humein kai baar aise \textbf{functions pass karne hote hain as arguments} — jaise \texttt{WebDriverWait} ke andar.

\subsubsection*{�� Example:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Lambda in Selenium WebDriverWait}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver.support.ui import WebDriverWait
wait = WebDriverWait(driver, 10)

wait.until(lambda driver: driver.find_element(By.ID, "submit"))
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=infobg, colframe=sectionblue, boxrule=1pt, sharp corners, left=8pt, right=8pt, top=8pt, bottom=8pt]
�� \textbf{Explanation:}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{lambda driver:} matlab hum driver object input le rahe hain
  \item \texttt{driver.find\_element(...)} — agar element mil gaya toh wait success
  \item Jab tak element nahi milta, Selenium wait karta rahega
\end{itemize}

✅ Iska fayda: Lambda se hum \textbf{short inline logic likh sakte hain} bina alag function define kiye.
\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection*{✅ When NOT to use \texttt{lambda}?}

Agar tumhara logic 1 line se zyada ka hai, toh \textbf{normal function} hi use karo:

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Normal Function Alternative}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
def wait_for_submit(driver):
    return driver.find_element(By.ID, "submit")

wait.until(wait_for_submit)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\section*{�� PART 2: \texttt{EC} (Expected Conditions) in Selenium}

\subsection*{�� Import:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={EC Import Statement}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
from selenium.webdriver.support import expected_conditions as EC
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\section*{�� 1. \texttt{EC.presence\_of\_element\_located(locator)}}

\subsection*{✅ Meaning:}

DOM mein element \textbf{exist karta hai} ya nahi — visible ho ya na ho.

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Presence of Element Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
WebDriverWait(driver, 10).until(
    EC.presence_of_element_located((By.ID, "email"))
)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

�� Use when:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Tumhara element page mein aa gaya ho but abhi visible na ho.
\end{itemize}

\section*{�� 2. \texttt{EC.visibility\_of\_element\_located(locator)}}

\subsection*{✅ Meaning:}

Element \textbf{present bhi ho AND user ko visible bhi ho.}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Visibility of Element Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
WebDriverWait(driver, 10).until(
    EC.visibility_of_element_located((By.XPATH, "//input[@type='text']"))
)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

�� Use when:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Tum \textbf{user interaction} chahte ho — jaise typing ya clicking.
\end{itemize}

\section*{�� 3. \texttt{EC.element\_to\_be\_clickable(locator)}}

\subsection*{✅ Meaning:}

Element:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item DOM mein ho
  \item Visible ho
  \item Enabled ho
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Element to be Clickable Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
WebDriverWait(driver, 15).until(
    EC.element_to_be_clickable((By.ID, "loginBtn"))
).click()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

�� Use when:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Button ya link click karwana hai after full page load
\end{itemize}

\section*{�� 4. \texttt{EC.invisibility\_of\_element(locator)}}

\subsection*{✅ Meaning:}

Check karta hai ki element \textbf{hidden ho gaya ya remove ho gaya} DOM se.

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Invisibility of Element Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
WebDriverWait(driver, 10).until(
    EC.invisibility_of_element((By.CLASS_NAME, "loading-spinner"))
)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

�� Use when:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Wait kar rahe ho kisi loader ya overlay ke hide hone ka
\end{itemize}

\section*{�� 5. \texttt{EC.text\_to\_be\_present\_in\_element(locator, text)}}

\subsection*{✅ Meaning:}

Yeh tab tak wait karega jab tak kisi specific element mein koi \textbf{text aa jaaye.}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Text to be Present Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
WebDriverWait(driver, 10).until(
    EC.text_to_be_present_in_element((By.ID, "status"), "Order Complete")
)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

�� Use when:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Tum kisi text ke update hone ka wait kar rahe ho
\end{itemize}

\section*{�� 6. \texttt{EC.alert\_is\_present()}}

\subsection*{✅ Meaning:}

JavaScript alert pop-up present hai ya nahi.

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title={Alert is Present Example}]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
WebDriverWait(driver, 5).until(EC.alert_is_present()).accept()
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

�� Use when:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Alert ya confirmation popup aane ka wait karna hai.
\end{itemize}

\section*{�� Bonus: Full EC Conditions Cheat Sheet ��}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|X|X|X|}
\hline
\textbf{EC Condition} & \textbf{Explanation} & \textbf{Use-case Example} \\
\hline
\texttt{presence\_of\_element\_located} & DOM mein ho & Page load ke baad element aya ya nahi \\
\hline
\texttt{visibility\_of\_element\_located} & User ke liye visible ho & Typing ya UI interaction se pehle \\
\hline
\texttt{element\_to\_be\_clickable} & Clickable (visible + enabled) & Buttons, tabs, menu \\
\hline
\texttt{invisibility\_of\_element} & Element chhup gaya ya gaya & Loader, spinners \\
\hline
\texttt{text\_to\_be\_present\_in\_element} & Specific text appear ho gaya & Status messages \\
\hline
\texttt{alert\_is\_present} & JavaScript alert show ho gaya & Accept, dismiss alerts \\
\hline
\texttt{frame\_to\_be\_available\_and\_switch\_to\_it} & Frame ready hai aur switch kar sakte ho & iFrames ke saath automation \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}

\section*{�� Final Words:}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=successbg, colframe=conceptgreen!80, boxrule=1pt, sharp corners, left=8pt, right=8pt, top=8pt, bottom=8pt]
✅ Yeh cheezein \textbf{automation ko reliable banati hain} — bina random sleep ke.

✅ Agar tum \texttt{lambda} aur \texttt{EC} samajh jaate ho, toh Selenium ke saare \texttt{wait} logic powerful ho jaate hain.

✅ Shortcuts jaise \texttt{ptw}, \texttt{pytest.mark}, fixtures — yeh sab combine karke tum ek \textbf{robust test framework} build kar sakte ho.
\end{tcolorbox}

\vspace{10pt}

Agar chaho toh:

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \texttt{conftest.py} fixtures
  \item \texttt{pytest.ini} setup
  \item Page Object Model
  \item CI/CD integration with Selenium
\end{itemize}

bhi Hinglish + real-world project ke examples ke saath bana ke de sakta hoon.

\section*{�� \texttt{.click()} Behavior in Selenium}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=objectivebg, colframe=sectionblue, boxrule=1pt, sharp corners, left=8pt, right=8pt, top=8pt, bottom=8pt]
\texttt{.click()} tabhi kaam karta hai jab:
\begin{enumerate}
    \item \textbf{Element DOM mein ho} \checkmarkinline
    \item \textbf{Element screen pe visible ho agar nahi hai then scroll karke visible karo uusko..} \checkmarkinline
    \item \textbf{Element kisi aur cheez se blocked na ho} \checkmarkinline (jaise popup, modal, loader, etc.)
    \item \textbf{Element pe koi animation ya transition na chal rahi ho} \checkmarkinline
\end{enumerate}
\end{tcolorbox}

\section*{❌ Agar ye conditions fail hoti hain, toh ye errors milte hain:}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|X|X|X|}
\hline
\textbf{Situation} & \textbf{Error Type} & \textbf{Example Message} \\
\hline
Element screen ke bahar hai & \texttt{ElementClickInterceptedException} & "Element is not clickable at point..." \\
\hline
Element kisi overlay ke niche hai & \texttt{ElementClickInterceptedException} & "Click intercepted by modal/overlay..." \\
\hline
Element visible nahi hai & \texttt{ElementNotInteractableException} & "Element not interactable..." \\
\hline
Element DOM mein hi nahi hai & \texttt{NoSuchElementException} & "Unable to locate element..." \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}

\section*{✅ \textbf{Best Practices to Avoid These Errors}}

\begin{enumerate}[leftmargin=*]
\item \textbf{Scroll into view:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title=Scroll to Element]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
driver.execute_script("arguments[0].scrollIntoView({block: 'center'});", element)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\item \textbf{Wait for visibility:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title=Wait for Visibility]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
WebDriverWait(driver, 10).until(EC.visibility_of(element))
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\item \textbf{Wait for clickability:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title=Wait for Clickable]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
WebDriverWait(driver, 10).until(EC.element_to_be_clickable((By.XPATH, xpath)))
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\item \textbf{Wait for overlays to disappear:}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title=Wait for Overlay to Disappear]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
WebDriverWait(driver, 10).until(EC.invisibility_of_element_located((By.CLASS_NAME, "modal-class")))
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}

\item \textbf{Fallback to JS click (if needed):}
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, title=JavaScript Click]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
driver.execute_script("arguments[0].click();", element)
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}
\end{enumerate}

\section*{�� \textbf{Key Selenium WebElement Methods \& Their Behaviors}}

\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{|l|X|X|}
\hline
\textbf{Method} & \textbf{Behavior Summary} & \textbf{Common Pitfalls / Errors} \\
\hline
\texttt{.send\_keys()} & Text input karta hai element mein & ❌ \texttt{ElementNotInteractableException} agar element disabled ya hidden ho \\
\hline
\texttt{.clear()} & Input field ko empty karta hai & ❌ Same as above — agar element interactable nahi hai \\
\hline
\texttt{.submit()} & Form ko submit karta hai (only if element is inside \texttt{<form>}) & ❌ \texttt{JavascriptException} agar form structure galat ho \\
\hline
\texttt{.get\_attribute()} & Element ka attribute value deta hai & ✅ Safe — even if element hidden ho \\
\hline
\texttt{.text} & Element ke andar ka visible text deta hai & ❌ Hidden text return nahi hota \\
\hline
\texttt{.is\_displayed()} & Check karta hai ki element screen pe visible hai ya nahi & ❌ May return false even if element is in DOM \\
\hline
\texttt{.is\_enabled()} & Check karta hai ki element interactable hai ya nahi & ✅ Useful before \texttt{.click()} or \texttt{.send\_keys()} \\
\hline
\texttt{.is\_selected()} & Checkbox ya radio button selected hai ya nahi & ❌ Only works for selectables \\
\hline
\texttt{.get\_property()} & JS property value deta hai (e.g. \texttt{value}, \texttt{checked}) & ✅ More reliable than \texttt{get\_attribute()} in some cases \\
\hline
\texttt{.location} / \texttt{.size} & Element ka position aur dimensions deta hai & ✅ Useful for visual debugging \\
\hline
\texttt{.screenshot()} & Element ka screenshot le sakta hai & ✅ Great for visual test logs \\
\hline
\end{tabularx}

\section*{⚠️ \textbf{Common Gotchas to Watch Out For}}

\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item \textbf{Hidden Elements:} Agar element DOM mein hai but \texttt{display: none} ya \texttt{visibility: hidden} hai, toh \texttt{.click()}, \texttt{.send\_keys()} fail karenge.
  \item \textbf{Disabled Inputs:} Agar input \texttt{disabled} hai, toh \texttt{.send\_keys()} and \texttt{.clear()} fail karenge.
  \item \textbf{Dynamic DOM Updates:} Agar element reload ho raha ho (SPA apps), toh stale reference error aa sakta hai:
\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=codebg, colframe=black!20, boxrule=0.6pt, sharp corners, left=8pt, right=8pt, top=8pt, bottom=8pt]
\begin{lstlisting}[language=CustomPython]
selenium.common.exceptions.StaleElementReferenceException
\end{lstlisting}
\end{tcolorbox}
\end{itemize}

\section*{��️ \textbf{Pro Tips for Robust Testing}}

\begin{tcolorbox}[colback=protipbg, colframe=conceptgreen!80, boxrule=1pt, sharp corners, left=8pt, right=8pt, top=8pt, bottom=8pt]
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=*]
  \item Use \texttt{WebDriverWait} with \texttt{expected\_conditions} for \textbf{every interaction}.
  \item Always check \texttt{is\_displayed()} and \texttt{is\_enabled()} before clicking or typing.
  \item Prefer \texttt{get\_property("value")} over \texttt{get\_attribute("value")} for input fields.
  \item Use \texttt{try-except} blocks to handle flaky UI behavior gracefully.
\end{itemize}
\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{document}

\section*{��️‍♂️ \textbf{Hidden Element ka Matlab Selenium ke Context Mein}}

\subsection*{�� Hidden ka matlab:}
Element \textbf{DOM mein present hai}, lekin \textbf{screen pe visible nahi hai} --- ya toh CSS ke through hide kiya gaya hai, ya wo kisi scroll ke neeche chhupa hua hai.

\subsection*{�� Hidden ke 2 Types:}

\textbf{1️⃣ CSS Hidden (True Hidden)}
\begin{lstlisting}
display: none;
visibility: hidden;
opacity: 0;
\end{lstlisting}
Is case mein Selenium ke liye wo element \textbf{interactable nahi hota}. Agar tum \texttt{.send\_keys()} ya \texttt{.click()} karoge, toh error milega:
\begin{lstlisting}
ElementNotInteractableException
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{2️⃣ Scroll ke neeche (Visible but out of view)}
\begin{itemize}
    \item Element screen pe nahi dikh raha, lekin \textbf{visible hai} aur \textbf{interactable hai}.
    \item Is case mein:
    \begin{itemize}
        \item XPath usse locate kar lega \ding{51}
        \item But \texttt{.click()} ya \texttt{.send\_keys()} tabhi kaam karega jab tum usse \textbf{scrollIntoView} kara lo.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\section*{�� Example:}

\textbf{❌ Hidden Element (CSS se hide):}
\begin{lstlisting}
<input type="text" style="display: none;" id="email">
\end{lstlisting}
\begin{lstlisting}
driver.find_element(By.ID, "email").send_keys("test@example.com")
# ❌ ElementNotInteractableException
\end{lstlisting}

\textbf{✅ Scroll ke neeche element:}
\begin{lstlisting}
<input type="text" id="email">  <!-- visible but off-screen -->
\end{lstlisting}
\begin{lstlisting}
email_input = driver.find_element(By.ID, "email")
driver.execute_script("arguments[0].scrollIntoView(true);", email_input)
email_input.send_keys("test@example.com")  # ✅ Works now
\end{lstlisting}

\section*{�� How to Check if Element is Hidden}
\begin{lstlisting}
element.is_displayed()  # Returns False if hidden
\end{lstlisting}

\begin{document}

% Title
\title{\textbf{\color{headingblue}Professional Explanation: Automation Testing Mindset + E-commerce Testing Flow + Reporting}}
\author{\color{gray}Anonymous}
\date{\color{gray}August 07, 2025}
\maketitle

% Introduction
\section{Introduction}
\color{black}Bilkul! Yahaan maine aapka pura explanation \textbf{\color{emphasisred}professionally}, \textbf{\color{emphasisred}simple language}, aur \textbf{\color{emphasisred}clear structure} me rewrite kiya hai, taaki kisi QA team, manager, ya documentation me easily use ho sake:

% Section: Automation Testing Overview
\section{Automation Testing Overview}
Automation Testing me sabse zaroori cheez hoti hai:

\begin{quote}
\textbf{\color{quotepurple}``Logic and Flow pe focus, phir proper Reporting.''}
\end{quote}

Is concept ko \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}2 main parts} me samajhte hain:

% Section: Part 1 - E-commerce Website Test Flow
\section{PART 1: E-commerce Website Test Flow (Step-by-Step)}
Niche diya gaya flow ek \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}practical example} hai: login se lekar checkout tak ka automation sequence.

\subsection{Test Steps:}
\begin{enumerate}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Launch Website}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Browser open karo aur website URL enter karo.
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Login}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Username \& password fill karo, login button click karo.
      \item \textbf{\color{emphasisred}Check:} Login successful? (e.g., dashboard ya welcome message dikh raha hai?)
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Product Search}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Search bar me product name daalo aur search button press karo.
      \item \textbf{\color{emphasisred}Check:} Relevant products dikh rahe hain?
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Select Product}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Search results me se ek product select karo.
      \item \textbf{\color{emphasisred}Check:} Product details page open hua?
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Add to Cart}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item `\color{codepurple}Add to Cart' button click karo.
      \item \textbf{\color{emphasisred}Check:} Product cart me successfully add hua?
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Open Cart}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Cart page open karo.
      \item \textbf{\color{emphasisred}Check:} Selected product cart me visible hai?
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Checkout Process}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Checkout button click karo.
      \item Fill address, phone, etc.
      \item Proceed to payment page.
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Payment}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Dummy payment details enter karo (test credentials).
      \item Submit payment.
      \item \textbf{\color{emphasisred}Check:} Order placed confirmation aaya?
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Logout}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Logout button click karo.
      \item \textbf{\color{emphasisred}Check:} Logout successful?
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Step Logging}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Har step ka result log karo: \textbf{\color{emphasisred}PASS} / \textbf{\color{emphasisred}FAIL} / \textbf{\color{emphasisred}ERROR}.
    \end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

% Section: Part 2 - Reporting Test Results
\section{PART 2: Reporting Test Results to a File}
\subsection{Objective:}
Test run hone ke baad ek file generate ho jisme \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}har step ka result} clearly likha ho (\textbf{\color{emphasisred}PASS/FAIL} + message).

\subsection{How to Do It:}
\begin{enumerate}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Print message after every step:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item e.g., \lstinline[language=JavaScript,basicstyle=\ttfamily\footnotesize\color{codepurple}]|console.log("[STEP] Login - PASS")|
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Write all messages to a file:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Save all logs to a text file (e.g., \texttt{\color{codepurple}test_report.txt}).
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Include details:}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Add result status: \texttt{\color{emphasisred}PASS}, \texttt{\color{emphasisred}FAIL}, or \texttt{\color{emphasisred}ERROR}, with short message if needed.
    \end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Example Report (test\_report.txt)}
\begin{verbatim}
[STEP] Open Website - PASS
[STEP] Login as testuser - PASS
[STEP] Search for product 'Shoes' - PASS
[STEP] Select first product - PASS
[STEP] Add product to cart - PASS
[STEP] Open cart and verify item - FAIL: Cart is empty.
[STEP] Checkout - SKIPPED (Previous step failed)
[STEP] Logout - SKIPPED
\end{verbatim}

% Section: Summary for Professional Use
\section{Summary for Professional Use:}
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Before test run:} Define each step and expected outcome.
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}During test:} Log step result with clear status.
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}After test:} Open the log file to review step-by-step results.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Industry Term:}
\begin{quote}
This approach is called \textbf{\color{quotepurple}``Stepwise Logging with Reporting''} — standard practice in QA automation.
\end{quote}

% Section: Need Help With?
\section{Need Help With?}
Let me know if you want:
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}A manual-style test case/report template}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Automation code logic or pseudocode for the above steps}
  \item \textbf{\color{keytermgreen}Tools/libraries suggestion for logging \& reporting in automation frameworks (like Selenium, Playwright, etc.)}
\end{itemize}

% Conclusion
\section{Conclusion}
This version is polished, clear, and suitable for professional documentation or knowledge-sharing. Let me know if you'd like it in PDF or formatted as a report.

% Document start
\begin{document}

% Title
\title{\textbf{{\color{headingblue}\_\_init\_\_.py, Package, Module – Sab Doubts Clear (Hinglish Notes)}}}
\author{{\color{gray}Anonymous}}
\date{{\color{gray}August 12, 2025}}
\maketitle

% Introduction
\section{Introduction}
\color{black}Yeh document Python ke \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}\_\_init\_\_.py}}, \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Package}}, aur \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Module}} ke concepts ko Hinglish mein explain karta hai, har detail ke saath, bina kuch remove kiye. Selenium automation ke liye practical layout aur best practices bhi included hain.

% Section 1: Module vs Package
\section{Module vs Package – Seedhi si baat}
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Module:}} ek single {\color{codepurple}\texttt{.py}} file jisme code hota hai.
    \begin{itemize}
      \item \textbf{{\color{emphasisred}Example:}} {\color{codepurple}\texttt{cart\_page.py}} ek module hai.
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Package:}} ek folder jise Python import kar sakta hai (dotted path ke saath), jisme multiple modules ho sakte hain.
    \begin{itemize}
      \item \textbf{{\color{emphasisred}Example:}} {\color{codepurple}\texttt{pages/}} ek package, uske andar {\color{codepurple}\texttt{user\_panel\_pages/}} ek sub-package.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}
\textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Think:}} Module = room, Package = ghar jisme multiple rooms.

% Section 2: __init__.py khali hoke bhi “special” kyun hai?
\section{\_\_init\_\_.py khali hoke bhi “special” kyun hai?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Python interpreter file ka “\textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}naam}}” dekhta hai. Agar folder ke andar exact naam wali file {\color{codepurple}\texttt{\_\_init\_\_.py}} milti hai, to Python turant samajh jaata hai ki “yeh folder ek \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}package}} hai.”
  \item Yeh \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}naming convention}} aur language rule hai — content chahe empty ho, bas file ka naam magic hai.
  \item Jaise OS me {\color{codepurple}\texttt{autorun.inf}} ya Git me {\color{codepurple}\texttt{.git}} folder se special behavior trigger hota hai, waise hi Python me {\color{codepurple}\texttt{\_\_init\_\_.py}} se package behavior trigger hota hai.
\end{itemize}
\textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Memory trick:}} “Nameplate” analogy.
\begin{itemize}
  \item Ghar par nameplate lagate hi postman ko pata chal jaata hai yeh registered address hai.
  \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{\_\_init\_\_.py}} = package ki nameplate. Khali ho sakti hai, par identity de deti hai.
\end{itemize}

% Section 3: __init__.py ka kaam exactly kya?
\section{\_\_init\_\_.py ka kaam exactly kya?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Package declare karta hai:}} dotted imports enable.
    \begin{itemize}
      \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{from pages.user\_panel\_pages.cart\_page import CartPage}}
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Relative imports}} allow karta hai package ke andar:
    \begin{itemize}
      \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{from .login\_page import LoginPage}}
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Public API}} expose karne ka point:
    \begin{itemize}
      \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{\_\_init\_\_.py}} me {\color{codepurple}\texttt{from .cart\_page import CartPage}} likh do, phir bahar se short import:
        \begin{itemize}
          \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{from pages.user\_panel\_pages import CartPage}}
        \end{itemize}
    \end{itemize}
  \item Tools/IDEs/linters ko structure clearly samajh aata hai.
\end{itemize}

% Section 4: Namespace packages
\section{“Namespace packages” kya hote hain? (Why sometimes it works without \_\_init\_\_.py)}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Python 3 ne ek feature diya: bina {\color{codepurple}\texttt{\_\_init\_\_.py}} ke bhi kuch folders “\textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}namespace package}}” jaisa behave kar sakte hain.
  \item Par yeh \textbf{{\color{emphasisred}unreliable}} ho sakta hai:
    \begin{itemize}
      \item Different machines/IDEs/CI me kabhi import ho, kabhi na ho.
      \item Same-name folders merge ho sakte hain (confusing behavior).
      \item Relative imports toot sakte hain.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}
\textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Conclusion:}} Production/automation me predictable behavior chahiye. Isliye har importable folder me {\color{codepurple}\texttt{\_\_init\_\_.py}} lagana best practice.

% Section 5: Agar __init__.py NA ho to kya problems?
\section{Agar \_\_init\_\_.py NA ho to kya problems?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item {\color{emphasisred}\texttt{ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'pages'}}
  \item {\color{emphasisred}\texttt{Relative import error: Attempted relative import beyond top-level package}}
  \item Local run ok, par CI/virtualenv/VS Code debug se run karoge to fail.
  \item “\textbf{{\color{emphasisred}Works on my machine}}” type flaky issues.
\end{itemize}

% Section 6: Kab lagana chahiye?
\section{Kab lagana chahiye?}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Jis folder ko import path ka hissa banana hai (jahan se aap dotted import karoge), wahan {\color{codepurple}\texttt{\_\_init\_\_.py}} rakho.
  \item \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Typical automation project:}}
    \begin{itemize}
      \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{pages/}}, {\color{codepurple}\texttt{pages/user\_panel\_pages/}}, {\color{codepurple}\texttt{pages/admin\_panel\_pages/}}
      \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{utilities/}}, {\color{codepurple}\texttt{helpers/}}, {\color{codepurple}\texttt{config/}}, {\color{codepurple}\texttt{data/}} (agar inhen import karte ho)
      \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{tests/}} me zaroori nahi, par subfolders me rakh doge to bhi theek; imports stable rehte hain.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

% Section 7: Selenium POM layout
\section{Tumhare Selenium POM ke liye ready-to-use layout}
\begin{verbatim}
pages/
  __init__.py
  user_panel_pages/
    __init__.py
    login_page.py
    cart_page.py
    main_dashboard_page.py
    main_zone_page.py
    buy_now_page.py
    my_order_page.py
  admin_panel_pages/
    __init__.py
    admin_login_page.py
    admin_dashboard_page.py
    orders_mgmt_page.py
tests/
  user_panel_tests/
    test_login.py
    test_cart_page.py
  admin_panel_tests/
    test_admin_login.py
conftest.py (common fixtures)
Optional: pytest.ini
\end{verbatim}
\textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Imports after split:}}
\begin{itemize}
  \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{from pages.user\_panel\_pages.cart\_page import CartPage}}
  \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{from pages.user\_panel\_pages.login\_page import LoginPage}}
  \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{from pages.admin\_panel\_pages.admin\_login\_page import AdminLoginPage}}
\end{itemize}
\textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Shortcut via \_\_init\_\_.py export:}}
\begin{itemize}
  \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{pages/user\_panel\_pages/\_\_init\_\_.py}}:
    \begin{itemize}
      \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{from .cart\_page import CartPage}}
      \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{from .login\_page import LoginPage}}
    \end{itemize}
  \item Ab tests me:
    \begin{itemize}
      \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{from pages.user\_panel\_pages import CartPage, LoginPage}}
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

% Section 8: Pytest discovery rules
\section{Pytest discovery quick rules}
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Test files:}} {\color{codepurple}\texttt{test\_*.py}} ya {\color{codepurple}\texttt{*\_test.py}}.
  \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{\_\_init\_\_.py}} not required for discovery, par allowed hai.
  \item Hamesha project root se run karo:
    \begin{itemize}
      \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{python -m pytest -q}}
    \end{itemize}
  \item {\color{codepurple}\texttt{sys.path.append}} hacks avoid karo; packages sahi banane se zarurat nahi padti.
\end{itemize}

% Section 9: Mini FAQ
\section{Mini FAQ (rapid fire)}
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Q:}} {\color{codepurple}\texttt{\_\_init\_\_.py}} ka size? Content?
    \begin{itemize}
      \item \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}A:}} Empty chalega. Chahe to public API expose karne wali imports likh do.
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Q:}} Kya har folder me chahiye?
    \begin{itemize}
      \item \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}A:}} Sirf un folders me jisse import karna hai.
    \end{itemize}
  \item \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}Q:}} Django me kyon notice nahi hota?
    \begin{itemize}
      \item \textbf{{\color{keytermgreen}A:}} {\color{codepurple}\texttt{startproject/startapp}} automatically {\color{codepurple}\texttt{\_\_init\_\_.py}} bana deta hai.
    \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

% Section 10: Checklist
\section{60-second checklist (note me chipka lo)}
\begin{itemize}
  \item Importable folder? Put {\color{codepurple}\texttt{\_\_init\_\_.py}}.
  \item Use dotted imports from project root package.
  \item Relative imports sirf package ke andar ({\color{codepurple}\texttt{.something}}).
  \item Run tests from root ({\color{codepurple}\texttt{python -m pytest}}).
  \item Avoid {\color{codepurple}\texttt{sys.path.append}}.
  \item Split user/admin pages into sub-packages with their own {\color{codepurple}\texttt{\_\_init\_\_.py}}.
\end{itemize}
